1002 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


NO. 09-KA-100


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-100 (La.App. 5 Cir. 08/25/09); 20 So. 3d 501; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1546



August 25, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 13, 2009.
Writ denied by State v. Smith, 31 So. 3d 357, 2010 La. LEXIS 768 (La., 2010)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Motion granted by, Remanded by State v. Smith, 71 So. 3d 357, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 762 (La.App. 5 Cir., 2011)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Smith v. State, 2015 La. LEXIS 2083 (La., Sept. 25, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 07-6660, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE DONALD A. ROWAN, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; HABITUAL OFFENDER SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, of possession with intent to distribute a controlled dangerous substance--MDMA, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A). The trial judge found defendant to be a second felony offender and imposed a 30-year sentence without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was attempting to enter a nightclub with 50 or 60 people waiting in line outside to get in and police officers present. Posted signs stated that patrons were subject to search. Defendant triggered a beep as he walked through the metal detector. Defendant created a disturbance as security attempted to frisk him, he was arrested for disturbing the peace, and a search produced a bag of multi-colored pills, a random sample of which tested positive for MDMA. After the jury rendered its verdict, a poll revealed the vote was 11-1 in favor of conviction. Defendant argued that the non-unanimous verdict violated his right to a trial by jury, and that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 782(A) and La. Const., art. 1, § 17(A) were unconstitutional. The court held that under the exception to the general rule pretermitting review, it could consider whether Apprendi v. New Jersey had overruled Louisiana authority validating a non-unanimous jury verdict. The court held that neither Apprendi nor the other cases cited by defendant required a unanimous jury verdict. Rather, they spoke to the issues that must be decided by a jury.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. His sentence was vacated and the matter remanded for resentencing.

 

1003 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Transcon. Gas Pipe Line Corp. v. La. Tax Comm'n


NO. 2009 CA 0628 CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2009 CA 0629


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2009 0628 (La.App. 1 Cir. 08/10/09); 23 So. 3d 329; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1470; 172 Oil & Gas Rep. 307



August 10, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by, As moot Transcon. Gas Pipe Line Corp. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 15 So. 3d 385, 2009 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 525 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2009)
Reversed by, Remanded by Transcon. Gas Pipeline Corp. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 32 So. 3d 199, 2010 La. LEXIS 592 (La., Mar. 16, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. District Court Nos. 491,453 c/w 551,435. The Honorable Kay Bates, Judge Presiding.
Fla. Gas Transmission Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 10 So. 3d 1219, 2009 La. LEXIS 634 (La., 2009)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND RENDERED. ANSWER TO APPEAL DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an interstate natural gas pipeline company, appealed a partial summary judgment from the 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which, in consolidated property tax refund proceedings, determined that defendant assessors were required to reassess pipeline property and declined to rule on the company's Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, challenge to pipeline valuation rates.


OVERVIEW: Because the company met the definition of a pipeline company in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1851(K), its property was classified as public service property under § 47:1851(M) and was assessed at 25 percent of fair market value pursuant to La. Const. art. VII, § 18(B). Some of its competitors operating in intrastate commerce did not meet the definition of pipeline companies and therefore paid ad valorem taxes at the 15 percent rate applicable to properties that were not public service properties. The district court ruled that the pipeline company was entitled to reassessment at the 15 percent rate but did not address the constitutional issue. The court, after conducting a dormant Commerce Clause analysis, held that the definition of "pipeline company" found in § 47:1851(K) resulted in disparate treatment between interstate and some intrastate pipeline companies and therefore was unconstitutional and in violation of the Commerce Clause. The remaining portions of § 47:1851 were severable and valid, with the exception of the phrase "pipeline company" in § 47:1851(M), which had to be removed. The district court correctly ordered a remand for reassessment of the properties.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's determination that ad valorem taxes on all pipeline property had to be calculated at 15 percent of fair market value as determined by the assessors of the parishes within which the properties were located, reversed as to the consideration of the constitutional issue, and rendered judgment declaring § 47:1851(K) unconstitutional and ordering that the phrase "pipeline company" be stricken from § 47:1851(M).

 

1004 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moss


NO. 2008-KA-1079


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-1079 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/22/09); 17 So. 3d 441; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1447



July 22, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Moss, 31 So. 3d 382, 2010 La. LEXIS 912 (La., 2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Moss v. Louisiana, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 182742 (E.D. La., Dec. 12, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 466-307, SECTION "G". Honorable Julian A. Parker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of aggravated battery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34 and sentenced him to a period of incarceration at hard labor for eight years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for aggravated battery but the appellate court affirmed. The record contained no motion to quash challenging the assistant district attorney's signature pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 534(1), and defendant's objection at trial to the timing of the arraignment raised a different issue. Accordingly, the issue that the indictment was flawed was not properly preserved for review by the appellate court. Additionally, his argument that the State failed to prove that the offense occurred in Orleans Parish was without merit because he failed to challenge venue in a pretrial motion to quash. His eight-year sentence was not excessive because he faced a sentence of up to 10 years at hard labor and a fine of up to $5,000. The jury did not find defendant credible and the district court also considered the victim's wish that defendant be punished to the full extent of the law. First offenders had received maximum and near maximum sentences and defendant had perjured himself. A lesser sentence would have depreciated the serious nature of the offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1005 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Parish of Iberville Sales Tax Dep't v. City of St. Gabriel


2008 CA 1780


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2008 1780 (La.App. 1 Cir. 07/22/09); 21 So. 3d 955; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1442



July 22, 2009, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 18th Judicial District Court, In and For the Parish of Iberville. Trial Court No. 65,969. Honorable William C. Dupont, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REVERSED; PERMANENT INJUNCTION DISSOLVED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 18th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Iberville, Louisiana, granted judgment in favor of appellee, Parish of Iberville Sales Tax Department, by issuing a permanent injunction against appellant city, enjoining the collection of the tax. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the 2 1/2% maximum tax limit contained in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2711 was available entirely to a municipality without reference to sales and use taxes imposed by other local governmental entities. The 1998 legislative resolutions were not persuasive in the case. The city's 2007 ordinance, St. Gabriel, La., Ordinance 2007-0001-1155 contained no new tax, but merely stated the city's change in policy from abstaining from collecting all of the tax authorized by the 1996 ordinance to a new course of action, i.e., to begin collecting all of the tax authorized by the voters as stated in St. Gabriel, La., Ordinance 1996-10. The city had imposed no new tax, rather, it had begun to collect the whole of the 1996 tax. Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2711, incorporated municipalities were authorized to levy and collect sales and use taxes not in excess of 21/2% upon satisfying the procedural requirements of that statute, without reference to the limitations imposed on parishes and school boards by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2721.6(A)(2).


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the permanent injunction was dissolved.

 

1006 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Coleman


No. 44,543-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,543 (La.App. 2 Cir. 07/15/09); 18 So. 3d 153; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1419



July 15, 2009, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 469,045. Honorable Robert P. Waddell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the decision of the decision of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which found in favor of appellees, maternal grandparents (grandparents), and allowed the child's custody to remain with the grandparents.


OVERVIEW: The parents had both relinquished custody of their child to grandparents shortly after the child's birth. The grandparents' action to establish custody under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 133 immediately followed resulting in a consent judgment for their sole custody of the child. Four years later, the father commenced the current action to modify the grandparents' custody and establish his primary custody of the child. The trial court allowed the child's custody to remain in the "excellent" environment of care which the grandparents had continuously provided and the appellate court affirmed. Based upon the provisions for the award of custody to a nonparent under art. 133, the trial court correctly rejected modification of the grandparents' custody. The father produced no evidence demonstrating that the family environment that the grandparents had provided the child immediately after his birth had changed and had become unstable and inadequate to continue to serve the best interests of the child. The strength of the father's rehabilitation, which afforded him liberal visitation, did not establish by itself the requisite proof under art. 133 to modify the prior adjudication of custody.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1007 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Triplett v. Bd. of Elem. & Secondary Educ.


NO. 2009 CA 0691


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2009 0691 (La.App. 1 Cir. 07/13/09); 21 So. 3d 401; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1411



July 13, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by Triplett v. Bd. of Elem., 2010 La. App. LEXIS 668 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Case No. 575,277. The Honorable Todd W. Hernandez, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, granted judgment in favor of appellees, the Louisiana State Board of Elementary and Secondary Education (BESE), the Louisiana Department of Education (DOE), and the State of Louisiana, by sustaining a declinatory exception raising the objection of lack of jurisdiction, and dismissing appellant parents' suit with prejudice. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents argued that the trial court erred in sustaining BESE's exceptions of lack of jurisdiction and no cause of action without allowing them an opportunity to amend. The appellate court found that the parents could not have amended their petition in such a way as to provide the trial court with jurisdiction over the parents' request for mandatory injunctive relief. There was no way the parents could state a cause of action against BESE for the injunctive relief they sought. The statute the parents challenged, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:1990, specifically provided a mechanism to address the situation that the parents complained occurred when students left the Recovery School District (RSD) and returned to the East Baton Rouge Parish (EBRP) school system. The responsibility for making such adjustments was on the DOE. The RSD's use of the school buildings was authorized by La. Const. art. VIII, § 3(A) and provided an exception to the general prohibition against the loan of public property. Since La. Const. art. VIII, § 9(A) did not prohibit the creation of the RSD, it was within the plenary power of the legislature.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1008 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


New Orleans Redevelopment Auth. v. Johnson


NO. 2008-CA-1020


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-1020 (La.App. 4 Cir. 7/8/09); 16 So. 3d 569; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1404



July 8, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2007-3102, DIVISION "E-7". HONORABLE MADELEINE LANDRIEU, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the New Orleans Redevelopment Authority (NORA), brought expropriation proceedings against defendant property owners in the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana). The trial court appointed an attorney to represent a deceased property owner; the other owner did not appear. The trial court authorized the expropriation of the property, and the attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: The property owners, once husband and wife, had divorced in 1990 and neglected and ultimately abandoned their house on property in New Orleans' Ninth Ward. Complaints against the property regarding grass, rats, drug use, vagrancy, and vandalism had come in over the years. The house was demolished in 1997. No one appealed the adjudication of blight as provided by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 13:2575 and 2576 by filing a petition pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:964. The attorney argued that the intent of NORA to transfer the property to a private party, Habitat for Humanity, made the acquisition violative of La. Const. art. I, §4(B), and that La. Const. art. I, § 4(H) required that the property be offered first to the owners from whom it was taken. The court rejected these arguments, finding that La. Const. art. I, § 4(B)(2)(c) unambiguously provided that this type of expropriation was a public purpose, so that the taking was authorized. This property was not taken for the predominant use of a private party nor for the purpose of transferring the property to a private person. It was taken for the public purpose of removing a threat to the public health or safety.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both the judgment overruling the exception of unconstitutionality and the judgment granting expropriation of the property.

 

1009 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mead


No. 44,447-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,447 (La.App. 2 Cir. 07/01/09); 16 So. 3d 470; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1381



July 1, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Mead v. State, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 125079 (W.D. La., Dec. 10, 2009)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Mead v. State, 2010 La. LEXIS 908 (La., Apr. 9, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 211460. Honorable Leon L. Emanuel, III, Judge.
State v. Mead, 988 So. 2d 740, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1043 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's public intimidation conviction was reinstated on appeal, he was adjudicated a third felony habitual offender and sentenced to a mandatory sentence of life imprisonment without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. The First Judicial District Court of Caddo Parish, Louisiana, determined that a downward departure was not warranted, and defendant's term of life imprisonment was upheld. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court imposed an unconstitutionally excessive sentence. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the trial court went into great detail to explain why it believed the mandatory sentence was, in fact, not constitutionally excessive. The record indicated that, after expressing some sympathy for defendant and his situation, the trial court ultimately decided that from a legal perspective the mandatory sentence was appropriate. The trial court's decision was not unreasonable and was supported by the record. For instance, defendant's two prior felony convictions were crimes of violence, and the trial court stated that defendant showed his propensity for violence when he sent harassing letters to his wife while he was in prison. Defendant did not qualify as an exceptional case where a downward departure would have been warranted. And contrary to defendant's assertion, the trial court's compliance with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 was not required as the mandatory life sentence imposed for a third-felony habitual offender was prescribed by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(ii).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1010 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hotard


No. 44,431-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,431 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/24/09); 17 So. 3d 64; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1335



June 24, 2009, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 05-F1115. Honorable Scott Leehy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED, REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana, convicted defendant of driving while intoxicated, fourth offense. He was sentenced to 20 years at hard labor, the first 60 days without the benefit of parole, to be served consecutively to any other sentence and a $5,000 fine, in default of which he was to serve an additional year in jail consecutive to his hard labor sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the 20-year sentence at hard labor was constitutionally excessive for a 64-year-old man entering a guilty plea to fourth offense DWI. The appellate court found that the sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive. The trial court provided a considered discussion of the reasons for the sentence it was imposing, including the potential danger to society posed by a lesser sentence for a defendant with a proven record of recidivism. The trial court carefully analyzed the circumstances, defendant's repeated criminal behavior, and the fact that the instant DWI violation occurred while defendant was on supervised probation for his three prior convictions. The sentence imposed did not shock the sense of justice, was not grossly out of proportion to the seriousness of the offense, and did not needlessly inflict pain and suffering. Defendant was ordered to participate in a substance abuse treatment program. The appellate court vacated the illegally lenient sentence and remanded for resentencing. The trial court also had to make a new determination of defendant's financial condition, and if appropriate, should dismiss the default time as mandated by law.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed; the sentence imposed by the court was vacated and remanded for resentencing.

 

1011 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. D. S. J.


08-1555


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-1555 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/24/09); 15 So. 3d 1188; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1344



June 24, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-EIGHTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LASALLE, NO. 84,432. HONORABLE J.P. MAUFFRAY, JR., PRESIDING.
State v. D. S. J., 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1368 (La.App. 3 Cir., June 24, 2009)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Twenty-Eight Judicial District Court, Parish of LaSalle, Louisiana, convicting him of sexual battery, and sentencing him to serve twenty-five years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: During the period between March 1 and March 31, 2007, it was alleged that defendant touched the vagina of his eleven-year-old daughter on two separate occasions. Defendant also rubbed her breasts. Defendant subsequently entered a plea of guilty to sexual battery. The appellate court ruled that defendant's sentence was not excessive. The mandatory minimum sentence for sexual battery was not excessive on its face, as a mandatory minimum sentence was presumed to be constitutional. Based on the fact defendant committed a sexual act against his own daughter and violated a position of trust, the appellate court could not say the imposition of the mandatory minimum sentence was excessive in the instant case. Also, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.1(C) did not allow for the consideration of defendant's actual conduct, the injury inflicted upon the victim, or the sentencing guidelines. The Louisiana Legislature sought to protect innocent children by enacting the penalty provision at issue, and defendant failed to present facts particular to his case that would support a departure from the mandatory minimum sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1012 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. LeBlanc


08-1533


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-1533 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/10/09); 12 So. 3d 1125; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1136



June 10, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by State v. LeBlanc, 27 So. 3d 840, 2010 La. LEXIS 474 (La., 2010)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Leblanc, 2010 La. LEXIS 1655 (La., July 6, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. CR 116138, DIV. G. HONORABLE DURWOOD CONQUE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which sentenced her, after a guilty plea, to the maximum sentence of 30 years for vehicular homicide under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1, and the maximum of six months on each of three counts of vehicular negligent injuring under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:39.1, to be served concurrently.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the maximum sentence of 30 years was constitutionally excessive under the circumstances of her case. On appeal, the court found that defendant was not the worst type of offender for whom maximum sentences were reserved. Testimony established that defendant did not have a problem with drugs until five to eight years prior to the accident which killed a victim. Prior to her own injury in a car accident, defendant had no problems with the law and was not involved in illegal activity. Defendant became addicted to pain killers and suffered depression due to her bad second marriage and her inability to overcome her addiction. Defendant was also raising two sons, virtually on her own, during this time. The court concluded that the trial court abused its discretion when it sentenced defendant to the maximum without adequate consideration of the circumstances in the case. Imposition of the maximum sentence of 30 years was grossly disproportionate to the severity of the crime in violation of La. Const. art. I, § 20 and was nothing more than a needless imposition of pain and suffering.


OUTCOME: The court severed defendant's misdemeanor sentences, vacated the 30 year sentence imposed on the conviction for vehicular homicide and remanded the matter to the trial court for resentencing.

State v. Carter


KA 08-1469


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-1469 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/03/09); 12 So. 3d 1091; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1064



June 3, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 6, 2009.
Writ denied by State v. Carter, 28 So. 3d 1004, 2010 La. LEXIS 500 (La., 2010)
Related proceeding at State ex rel. Carter v. State, 100 So. 3d 833, 2012 La. LEXIS 3105 (La., 2012)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Carter v. Warden, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 29416 (W.D. La., Jan. 29, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 283,812. HONORABLE THOMAS MARTIN YEAGER, DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. Carter, 981 So. 2d 734, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 525 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of drug-related offenses. The State filed a multiple offender bill. The Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, No. 283, 812, Louisiana, adjudicated him a second offender. He was resentenced to twenty years at hard labor for possession with intent to distribute CDS III; ten years at hard labor for obstruction of justice; and twenty-five years at hard labor for conspiracy to distribute CDS I. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Eleven months elapsed between defendant's sentencing for several drug-related offenses, and the State's filing of a multiple offender bill of information. Defendant did not file a motion to quash or make the argument of untimeliness in the trial court; therefore, the argument could not be raised for the first time on appeal. The State had no obligation to provide defendant with its proof of the multiple offender bill prior to the hearing. The record of the pleas and the court minutes indicated that defendant was apprised of his right to a jury trial when he entered his guilty pleas. The Court of Appeal of Louisiana held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant to twenty years for distribution of hydrocodone, ten years for obstruction of justice, and twenty-five years for conspiracy to distribute marijuana. Defendant was a career criminal involved in the trafficking of dangerous drugs, and the sentences were within the statutory ranges. The sentences were not excessive under La. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1014 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wood


08-1511


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-1511 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/03/09); 11 So. 3d 701; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1058



June 3, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 6, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF CONCORDIA, NO. 07-0594/0594A/0594B. HONORABLE LEO BOOTHE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Concordia, which convicted him of three counts of second-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1 and imposed sentences of three consecutive life sentences at hard labor without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was 15 years old at the time of the murders, was convicted of three counts of second-degree murder in the murder of his parents and his alleged coconspirator. The appellate court affirmed, stating that the evidence was sufficient to prove that defendant possessed the requisite intent to kill or inflict great bodily harm on his parents. In defendant's second recorded statement to an investigator, defendant admitted to shooting his parents and the jury apparently chose to believe that statement over the previous statement in which defendant labeled the alleged coconspirator as the gunman. The victims were also shot numerous times, with multiple gunshot wounds to the upper portions of their bodies. Some of the gunshot wounds inflicted on defendant's mother were at very close range. The mandatory life sentences were appropriate given the senselessness of the three murders. The sentences were not grossly disproportionate to the offenses committed by defendant under La. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1015 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morain


08-1546


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-1546 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/03/09); 11 So. 3d 733; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1066



June 3, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 6, 2009.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Morain v. State, 2010 La. LEXIS 1186 (La., Apr. 30, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 274,397. HONORABLE JOHN C. DAVIDSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. Morain, 981 So. 2d 66, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 478 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which sentenced him to serve 15 years at hard labor after he had entered a plea of guilty to the offenses of vehicular homicide, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1(A)(1) and (2), and first-degree vehicular negligent injuring, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:39.2(A)(1) and (2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant had pled guilty to vehicular homicide and first-degree vehicular negligent injuring. He was sentenced again after a remand to serve 15 years at hard labor, 8 years to be served without benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence, and to pay a fine of $2,000. Defendant argued that his sentence was excessive because he was not the worst type of offender, and that his sentence was cruel, unusual, and excessive under La. Const. art. I, § 20. The appellate court disagreed and affirmed. Jurisprudence setting sentences in similar cases offered widely disparate sentences being assessed for the same crime. In the instant case, the question of whether the instant sentence was deemed to have shocked the sense of justice or made no measurable contribution to acceptable penal goals, was answered in the negative. The sentence was structured by the trial judge to fit the facts as determined by the court. The sentence was not so grossly disproportionate to the severity of the crime as to have been considered shocking. The relevant question was whether the trial court abused its broad sentencing discretion, not whether another sentence might have been more appropriate.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.

 

1016 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Garner v. Thomas


NO. 2008-CA-1448


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-1448 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/28/09); 13 So. 3d 784; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 996



May 28, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2008-6916, DIVISION "C-DRS 1". Honorable Sidney H. Cates, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father appealed a judgment from the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which granted plaintiff grandmother rights of monthly visitation with her grandsons.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed that the maternal grandparents enjoyed a close and loving relationship with the children prior to their mother's death. The grandfather had served a prison sentence 40 years earlier. After the grandmother obtained court-ordered visitation, the father did not communicate with her to arrange for further visits. Conflicting testimony was presented regarding disputes between the parties. The trial court found the grandmother more credible and determined that the father's failure to contact her required a judgment providing for specific hours of visitation. The court found no violation of the father's due process rights under U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV because the trial court, in determining the best interests of the children under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344, reasonably considered the facts of the case and made a specific credibility finding that was adverse to the father. Although the trial court did not specifically refer to La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 136(B) in its reasons for judgment, its findings adequately addressed the relevant factors. The trial court reasonably gave little weight to the grandfather's felony conviction because it had occurred so long ago.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Pugh


No. 44,251-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,251 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/27/09); 12 So. 3d 1085; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1009



May 27, 2009, Judgment Rendered

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 257,550. Honorable Jeanette Giddens Garrett, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, convicting him of molestation of a juvenile, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2.


OVERVIEW: In the early part of 2002, defendant, then age 32, had lewd contact and nonconsensual sex in western Caddo Parish with a 14-year-old female. The age difference between the two was almost exactly 18 years. The required unanimous six-person jury found defendant guilty of molestation of a juvenile, and defendant was sentenced to life at hard labor, without benefits. Defendant argued that the State should have proven venue at trial by a preponderance of the evidence. Venue was never placed at issue in the trial court, not before the trial, not during the trial, not in argument, not in any requested jury charge, and not in the motion for postverdict judgment of acquittal. The appellate court ruled that under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 615, defendant's failure to file a motion to quash waived any issue of venue. Also, the record did not support a finding that trial counsel's failure to file a motion to quash fell below the objective standard of reasonableness under prevailing professional norms and resulted in actual prejudice to defendant. Furthermore, the jury heard the victim testify as to the force used by defendant and felt it sufficient to render a guilty verdict.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Farquhar v. New Orleans Saints


NO. 08-CA-800


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


08-800 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/26/09); 16 So. 3d 404; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 973



May 26, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 17, 2009.
Writ denied by Farquhar v. New Orleans Saints, 2009 La. LEXIS 2818 (La., Oct. 2, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION, DISTRICT 7. STATE OF LOUISIANA. DOCKET NO. 00-833. HONORABLE JOHN C. GROUT, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After appellant professional football player (employee) suffered a career ending injury during training camp, his contract was cancelled, and he filed a disputed claim for compensation against appellee football team (employer). Ultimately, the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 7 (Louisiana), applied the league's collective bargaining agreement and awarded the employee back compensation benefits, plus costs. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the employee contended the workers' compensation court incorrectly calculated his average weekly wage and thus incorrectly determined his supplemental earnings benefits. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the workers' compensation court correctly calculated the employee's average weekly wage based on the amount he actually earned prior to his injury, and not on his contract amount. The fact that the employer ultimately paid the employee his entire contract amount plus severance was immaterial. The appellate court also found that the employee was entitled to two years supplemental earnings benefits under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1221(3)(a) if he could prove he was unable to earn wages equal to 90 percent or more of his wages at the time of injury. The workers' compensation court correctly applied the collective bargaining agreement, which stated that the team was entitled to 25 weeks credit against any compensation liability assessed since the employee was paid his entire contract amount. The employee was not entitled to attorney's fees and penalties as the team had a valid defense to the employee's claims and were ultimately successful.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Schaller


NO. 08-KA-522


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


08-522 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/26/09); 15 So. 3d 1046; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 993



May 26, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 17, 2009.
Writ denied by State v. Schaller, 2010 La. LEXIS 457 (La., Feb. 26, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 04-6311, DIVISION "J". HONORABLE STEPHEN J. WINDHORST, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; MATTER REMANDED WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, that convicted him of video voyeurism involving a juvenile under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:283B(4) and distribution of marijuana to a person under the age of 18 under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981C, arguing that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that, where defendant allowed a teenaged girl and her boyfriend to use a bedroom in his home and secretly videotaped them, the evidence supported the video voyeurism conviction. Although defendant argued that the evidence failed to prove a lewd and lascivious intent, other videotapes taken by defendant were admitted showing teenaged girls nude or scantily clan dancing suggestively or masturbating. The evidence enabled the jury to infer that defendant's sexual proclivities leaned toward teenaged girls and that he secretly taped the girl and her boyfriend intending to watch the video for his sexual gratification. Further, although there was no expert testimony regarding testing and identification of the substance seized from defendant's home, the evidence supported defendant's drug conviction because the 14-year-old girl testified about how she felt after smoking the substance defendant gave to her and a police officer assigned to the narcotics division testified that he smelled marijuana when he entered defendant's home, that he found marijuana in defendant's home, and that defendant admitted that some of his videotapes showed juveniles smoking marijuana.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed, but the case was remanded to the trial court with instructions to inform defendant in writing of his sex offender registration and notification requirements under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:542 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:542.1.

State v. Lewis


NO. 08-KA-1317


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


08-1317 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/26/09); 16 So. 3d 385; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 992



May 26, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 17, 2009.
Writ granted by State v. Lewis, 34 So. 3d 282, 2010 La. LEXIS 1194 (La., 2010)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Lewis, 2010 La. LEXIS 2265 (La., Oct. 22, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 05-2904, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE PATRICK J. MCCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of manslaughter in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31. He received a 30-year sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his manslaughter conviction and 30-year sentence and the appellate court affirmed the conviction but vacated the sentence. Defendant did not object below to the responsive verdict of manslaughter. Accordingly, he was entitled to a reversal only if the evidence was insufficient to support a conviction of the charged offense, second-degree murder, as set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1. The trial judge made a credibility call to accept testimony refuting defendant's version that the gun accidentally discharged. The appellate court was unable to say that the trial court was clearly wrong in its evaluation of the witnesses' testimony. Because the evidence was sufficient to prove second-degree murder, it was sufficient to support the responsive verdict of manslaughter. Defendant's sentence was improper because there was no evidence that defendant formed the specific intent to kill the victim at some time prior to the fight that broke out between the parties. Further, defendant had no history of violence and the record indicated that a 20-year sentence would fulfill all the requisites of the constitutional requirement of proportionate punishment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the conviction but vacated the sentence and remanded to the district court for resentencing in accord with the appellate court's opinion.

Tietjen v. City of Shreveport


NO. 44,190-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,190 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/13/09); 17 So. 3d 17; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 825



May 13, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Tietjen v. City of Shreveport, 17 So. 3d 17, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1549 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2009)
Writ of certiorari granted Tietjen v. City of Shreveport, 24 So. 3d 872, 2010 La. LEXIS 93 (La., 2010)
Reversed by Tietjen v. City of Shreveport, 2010 La. LEXIS 1215 (La., May 11, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 506522. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and a purchaser of property, sought review of an order from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which awarded judgment to plaintiffs, taxpayers and a mortgagee, in an action to declare a tax sale null and void.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers failed to pay the ad valorem taxes on their property for the 2001 tax year. The city notified them of a pending tax sale. The notice was sent via certified mail. A return receipt was signed by an employee of a physical therapy company that was housed on the subject property. The property was sold to the purchaser, subject to the right of redemption. Plaintiffs filed a petition for declaratory judgment, seeking to have the tax sale annulled. The trial court declared the sale null and void. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred in declaring the tax sale null and void. The taxpayers did not dispute the fact that, prior to the tax sale, they received notice that the taxes were delinquent and that the sale was pending. The mortgagee of the property did not request notice as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2180.1(A). The court found no merit to the taxpayers' claim that the tax sale should be declared a nullity based on the city's failure to provide post-tax sale notice. The mortgagee and the taxpayers failed to meet their burden of proving the invalidity of the tax sale for lack of statutory notice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Hanson


No. 44,223-KA, No. 44,224-KA (Consolidated cases)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,223 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/13/09); 12 So. 3d 1007; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 814



May 13, 2009, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 158,162 & 158,163. Honorable John M. Robinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, convicted defendant of two separate charges of obscenity as a first offender pursuant to a plea bargain agreement. Defendant was sentenced to serve three years' imprisonment at hard labor for each conviction, with the sentences to be served concurrently. Defendant was also ordered to register as a sex offender and to pay a fine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the sentence was excessive and the imposition of a maximum sentence was unconstitutionally excessive. The appellate court found that the record, including the confidential information contained in the presentence investigation (PSI) report regarding defendant's criminal history and the fact and circumstances surrounding the crimes, clearly supported the trial court's imposition of the maximum sentences. The trial court properly acted within its discretion in assessing defendant as a "worst offender" and his crimes of obscenity as the "worst offenses." La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:106G(1) clearly provided for a fine of not less than $1,000, nor more than $2,500, or in default, imprisonment. Defendant's sentence could not be imposed without the stipulation that it be without benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence. The information contained in the PSI confirmed that no victims were juveniles. The portion of defendant's sentence requiring him to register as a sex offender was vacated. The portion of the sentence assigning all future cases involving defendant to his own docket violated La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 253.1 and public policy.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed. The portions of defendant's sentence denying him benefits, requiring registration as a sex offender, ordering jail time in lieu of payment of fines and specifying that any further charges against defendant be assigned to the trial judge's own docket were vacated; in all other respects, the sentences of defendant were affirmed.

 

1023 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


La. Workers' Comp. Corp. v. La. Ins. Guar. Ass'n


NO. 2008 CA 0885


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2008 0885 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/13/09); 20 So. 3d 1047; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 859



May 13, 2009, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Case No. 527,676. The Honorable R. Michael Caldwell, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, granted summary judgment in favor of appellee member insurer, and denied appellant Louisiana Insurance Guaranty Association's (LIGA) cross-motion for summary judgment on the same legal issue. LIGA appealed.


OVERVIEW: The member contended that the word "contribution" used in La. Const. art. XII, § 8.1(F) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1395(D)(2) was unambiguous and referred to assessments made by LIGA to its member insurers. The appellate court disagreed. Using the member's historic premiums for the year prior to assessment as the basis for calculation of the assessment, and using that assessment to offset covered claims arising prior to the member's admission to LIGA did not amount to an unconstitutional retroactive "contribution" coerced from the member. Its contribution was still prospective in nature, that was, assessed and paid after the date of the member's admission as a member insurer. LIGA was only responsible for "covered claims," a statutorily-defined term having a precise, technical meaning. The legislature was more concerned with protection of LIGA's solvency from a potential insolvency of the member rather than protection of the member from assessment by LIGA. If the member sought and was granted the benefit of protection by LIGA on the same terms as other members, then it was only fair that it should participate in and contribute to LIGA on the same terms as other members.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and summary judgment was rendered in LIGA's favor, dismissing the petition and cause of action of the member insurer with prejudice.

St. Pierre v. La. S.W. Transp., Inc.


NO. 08-CA-532


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


08-532 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/12/09); 14 So. 3d 593; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 791



May 12, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 17, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE FORTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. JOHN THE BAPTIST, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 51617, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE MADELINE JASMINE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF JULY 27, 2007 AFFIRMED; JUDGMENTS OF SEPTEMBER 26, 2007, OCTOBER 3, 2007, AND NOVEMBER 15, 2007 VACATED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff survivor brought a wrongful death action against defendants, a truck driver, an employer, a parish, a vacuum services company, and insurers. The 40th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. John the Baptist, Louisiana, entered several summary judgments that dismissed the survivor's tort claims. The survivor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was driving on a highway in the parish when he crashed into the truck driver's rig. The survivor asserted that the parish and the vacuum services company were negligent in entering into a contract, allowing sanitary wastewater to be trucked into a treatment facility. The survivor alleged that the truck driver failed to maintain a proper lookout, and the employer negligently hired and trained the truck driver. On appeal, the survivor asserted, inter alia, that the trial court erred in granting summary judgment in favor of the vacuum services company, the employer, and the parish on the basis of statutory immunity under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800.17. The appellate court found that the motions for summary judgment were improper because the movers failed to establish that vacuum services company and the employer were state agents, contractors, or representatives. Further, for § 9:2800.17 to apply, the parish had to show that the wastewater was from Hurricane Katrina. Finally, the trial court did not err in dismissing a duty to warn claim against the vacuum services company because the duties of the Department of Transportation and Development included a duty to warn.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment granting partial summary judgment in favor of the vacuum services company on the duty to warn claim. The appellate court vacated judgments granting summary judgment on the issue of statutory immunity in favor of the vacuum service company and the insurance company; the judgment in favor of the parish; the judgment in favor of the insurer, the employer, and the truck driver. The matter was remanded.

State v. Lee


NO. 09-KA-37


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


09-37 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/12/09); 15 So. 3d 229; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 842



May 12, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 17, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 07-648, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE PATRICK J. MCCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED; MATTER REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) of two counts of armed robbery. Defendant was sentenced to two consecutive fifteen year sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his two consecutive fifteen year sentences were constitutionally excessive. The court of appeal disagreed. At sentencing, the trial judge in the case specifically noted both defendant's youth and his extensive juvenile record, as well as his arrest record. The judge noted the seriousness of the armed robberies and the fact that one of the victims thought he was going to die. The judge stated that he had considered the sentencing guidelines and found that any other sentence would deprecate from the seriousness of the crime. Defendant chose not to accept a plea bargain. Furthermore, as the State noted in brief, during the trial the trial court heard the testimony of both victims in great detail, thus making the judge aware of the severity of the armed robberies. The State also noted that the trial court took into account the extensive arrests and juvenile record of defendant. For those reasons, the sentences imposed were not vindictive.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded for correction of the commitment minute entry to have it conform with the transcript. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Council of New Orleans v. Wash.


NO. 2009-C-0389


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2009-0389 (La. 05/12/09); 13 So. 3d 662; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 784



May 12, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, Remanded by, Set aside by Council of New Orleans v. Washington, 9 So. 3d 854, 2009 La. LEXIS 1004 (La., May 29, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON SUPERVISORY WRIT FROM THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2009-2279, DIVISION "D-16". Honorable Lloyd J. Medley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; JUDGMENT VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator, a requester of public records, sought a supervisory writ from an order of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, granting respondent city's motion for a preliminary injunction against the requester's publication of the records she received.


OVERVIEW: The requester's written public records request sought email records from a number of city council members. These emails were stored in the city's server, an electronic filing cabinet. Fearing the imminent disposal of the emails, the requester enlisted the assistance of a sanitation department employee, who facilitated pick-up and production of the emails. The documents were therefore produced without the city's attorneys reviewing them for privileged material. Approximately 3 months after the release of the documents, the city sought and received a preliminary injunction allowing it to review the documents for privileged material prior to the requester's publication of them. The court held that such a prior restraint violated the requester's rights under the First Amendment, although the requester did not raise any First Amendment arguments below. While the requester might be subject to discovery rules and ethical rules preventing disclosure, such as La. St. Bar art. XVI, R. 4.4(b), and La. Code Civ. Proc. art. 1424(D), and privileged materials were not public records under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:4.1(C), the requester's First Amendment rights were paramount.


OUTCOME: The court granted the requester's supervisory writ and vacated the trial court's judgment and dissolved the injunction.

Reed v. St. Charles Gen. Hosp.


NO. 2008-CA-0430 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2008-CA-0431 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2008-C-0570 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2008-C-0571 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2008-C-0572 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2008-C-0573


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-0430 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/06/09); 11 So. 3d 1138; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 783



May 6, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Reed v. St. Charles Gen. Hosp., 2009 La. LEXIS 2619 (La., Sept. 18, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NOS. 88-18141, C/W 90-7487, DIVISION "G-11". HONORABLE ROBIN M. GIARRUSSO, JUDGE.
Reed v. St. Charles Gen. Hosp., 815 So. 2d 319, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1386 (La.App. 4 Cir., Mar. 27, 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, brought a medical malpractice action against defendant hospital in the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana). After their deaths, their children proceeded. The children asked the district court to approve their petitions to settle their claims against the hospital so that they could obtain payments from the Patient's Compensation Fund (PCF). The district judge approved the petitions. The PCF appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband received a blood transfusion in the hospital in 1985 and contracted AIDS, which he unknowingly communicated to his wife. The husband died in 1988; the wife in 1995. The PCF filed peremptory exceptions of no cause of action and no right of action to the petition to settle the wife's claim pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 927(A)(5) and (6). The court held that the exception of no cause of action was appropriate based on the law of the case: the court had previously held that the Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.41 et seq., did not apply to the wife's claim because she was not a "patient" as defined under the Act. The court held that the PCF had standing to object in order to protect the integrity of its fund. As to the husband's claim, the PCF could not urge the exception of prescription because the hospital had settled the claim. Because the patient had settled, no constitutional challenge to the Act survived, and therefore the PCF did not have the right to intervene under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.44(D)(2)(b)(xii).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's denial of the exception of prescription as to the husband's claim, its approval of the settlement on behalf of the husband, and its denial of the PCF's motion to intervene. The court reversed the district court's approval of the settlement with the wife. The court remanded the husband's claim for trial of damages in excess of the $ 100,000 settlement, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.44(C)(5)(a).

 

1028 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Hernandez v. Barataria Park, L.L.C.


NO. 08-CA-791


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


08-791 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/28/09); 13 So. 3d 200; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 604



April 28, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 17, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 654-608, DIVISION "O". HONORABLE ROSS P. LADART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners challenged a decision from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, a landowner and a parish, in a case alleging the taking of property without just compensation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' property was subjected to several servitudes, including one in favor of a lot located behind plaintiffs' land. After construction began of a paved road on the servitude, plaintiffs alleged that their land was converted into a public street for public use. Summary judgment was granted for defendants, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court noted that a resubdivision plan and its accompanying documents were executed prior to the plaintiffs' purchase of the property. They were sufficient to constitute a dedication of the servitude to public use, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:5051. Also, the evidence offered in support of the motion for summary judgment was sufficient to establish an implied dedication prior to plaintiffs' purchase of the land. The evidence established the combination of an unequivocally manifested intent to dedicate on the part of the owner and an equally clear intent to accept on the part of the public. The appellate court declined to hear an issue relating to an extinguishment of the servitude because trial court made no ruling on it, and the affirmance of the summary judgment on dedication of the servitude concluded the case.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

State v. Raymond


NO. 08-KA-1204


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


08-1204 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/28/09); 13 So. 3d 577; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 607



April 28, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 17, 2009.
Writ denied by State v. Raymond, 27 So. 3d 296, 2010 La. LEXIS 298 (La., 2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Raymond v. Cain, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 82691 (E.D. La., May 3, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE FORTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. JOHN THE BAPTIST, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 04-196, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE MARY H. BECNEL, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Fortieth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. John the Baptist, Louisiana, that convicted him of second-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1, arguing that the trial court erred in denying his challenge for cause to a prospective juror and erred in granting the State's challenge to a juror outside of defendant's presence.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's juror challenge under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 797 because, although the juror said that his relationships with defense counsel, the assistant district attorney, and one of the investigators would influence him, he did not say whether he would be influenced in favor of the State or the defense. The juror also indicated that he could follow the law, would hold the State to its burden of proof, would give defendant the presumption of innocence, would find him not guilty if the case was not proven beyond a reasonable doubt, and would not hold it against defendant if he chose not to testify. Further, the trial court did not err under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 831A and 841 in granting the State's challenge for cause to a prospective juror outside of defendant's presence because defense counsel was present to protect defendant's interests at the conference during which the juror expressed concern for her safety due to the fact that she lived near the crime scene and defendant's residence and because defendant's presence would likely have inhibited inquiry into the juror's safety concerns.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

1030 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Breaux


08-1061


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-1061 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/01/09); 6 So. 3d 982; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 508



April 1, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. L. B., 2010 La. App. LEXIS 494 (La.App. 3 Cir., Apr. 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 8751-07. HONORABLE ROBERT WYATT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AMENDED IN PART; AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty of attempted aggravated rape and three counts of aggravated rape. The Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, Louisiana, denied defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal. He was sentenced to fifty years at hard labor for attempted aggravated rape and to life imprisonment on each count of aggravated rape. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with several sexual offenses against children. He was charged with having committed the offensive acts against one of his victims between May 1, 1977 and December 31, 1980; at that time the penalty for aggravated rape was death. Therefore, the trial court was required to comply with the procedural rules for capital cases, such as a unanimous jury and sequestration of the jury. The Court of Appeal of Louisiana held that the trial court committed reversible error by convicting defendant of one count of aggravated rape based on a verdict in which only 10 out of 12 jurors found him guilty. The trial court's failure to sequester the jury was harmless, as defendant did not object and a death sentence was not imposed. The testimony of the child victims was sufficient to support his conviction for the sex offenses. Under the statutory scheme that applied at the time defendant committed his crimes, the trial court erred by imposing his sentences without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for one count of aggravated rape was reversed, and the sentence was reversed; defendant's remaining convictions were affirmed. Defendant's sentences for the remaining two counts of aggravated rape were amended to delete the portion of the sentences to be served without benefits. Defendant's sentence for the attempted aggravated rape conviction was vacated and remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

 

1031 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Morrell v. Fisher


08-1260


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-1260 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/01/09); 7 So. 3d 1264; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 506



April 1, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 2006-3441. HONORABLE DAVID A. RITCHIE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a livestock owner and his insurer, appealed a judgment from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which, in a jury trial, ruled in favor of plaintiff driver in a negligence action. The trial court found that the insurer acted in bad faith in its handling of the driver's property damage claim and awarded a penalty to the driver.


OVERVIEW: While driving on a rural roadway on a foggy night, the driver collided with a bull that had broken through the owner's fence. She sustained personal injuries, and her vehicle was totaled. The owner presented evidence that he and his son had searched for the bull; however, the owner had not alerted the authorities to the bull's escape. Prior to trial, the parties stipulated that the location of the accident was a closed range area on the date of the accident. The jury instruction was based upon La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:2803. The driver's uncontroverted testimony established that the insurer never contacted her to investigate her claim. The court held that because the accident occurred in a closed range area, the owner was presumed negligent under § 3:2803 and was required to prove that he had taken reasonable precautions to keep the bull in an enclosed area and to prove how the bull escaped. The trial court did not err by not instructing under an ordinance instead. The burden of proof rested upon the owner to exculpate himself from even the slightest degree of negligence. The facts supported a bad faith finding and penalty under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 22:1892(A)(3), 22:1973.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1032 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


City of Denham Springs v. Perkins


NUMBER 2008 CA 1937


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2008 1937 (La.App. 1 Cir 03/27/09); 10 So. 3d 311; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 451



March 27, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied City of Denham Springs v. Perkins, 8 So. 3d 568, 2009 La. LEXIS 1492 (La., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Twenty-First Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of Livingston State of Louisiana. Docket Number 118228. The Honorable Ernest G. Drake, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee City filed a petition for injunctive relief and order of abatement against appellees, a company and its owner (owner), for supporting the maintenance of a nuisance by knowingly permitting prohibited activity to exist on the owner's bar or bar/restaurant. The Twenty-First Judicial District Court of Livingston Parish, Louisiana, rendered a judgment and order of abatement. The owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the owner contended, inter alia, that the City had no legal right to close the bar or bar/restaurant located on his property through an abatement action, and the district court erred in finding that the owner knowingly permitted maintenance of a nuisance. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the relief the City was seeking was specifically provided for under the abatement statutes, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4711 et seq., and that the enjoining and abating of a nuisance was a civil remedy over which the district court had subject matter jurisdiction. Contrary to the owner's assertions, the City was not required in its petition, in addition to its well-pled allegations, to describe the specific incidents where the owner knowingly permitted prohibited activity; the City's notices of violation to the owner were sufficient and stated a cause of action. The testimony and evidence of overwhelming criminal activity on the premises and the testimony that the owner and proprietors were aware of this activity, yet did not take sufficient precautions or measures to curtail or eliminate this activity, showed that they knowingly permitted these prohibited activities to exist.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1033 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Kozlowicz v. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr.


2008 CA 1806


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2008 1806 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/27/09); 9 So. 3d 1000; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 461



March 27, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Kozlowicz v. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr., 2009 La. App. LEXIS 644 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 4, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, IN AND FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, DOCKET NUMBER 553,402, DIVISION J(25), THE HONORABLE CURTIS A. CALLOWAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. MOTION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant petitioner sought habeas relief, contending he was entitled to early release based on good time credit. The petition was dismissed. On rehearing, the petitioner amended his petition challenging the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4(A). The Nineteenth Judicial District Court of East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, granted appellee Attorney General's exception of no cause of action. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the petitioner raised several issues contending the trial court erred in interpreting La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4(S) and that he had a constitutionally protected interest in the good time that he earned. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the intention of the legislature in enacting the statute was to impose the additional requirement of an approved residency plan prior to the release of prisoners incarcerated for sex crimes, whether they were released by parole or by order of the office of adult services. The reason the petitioner was not released on his good time discharge date was because he did not have an approved residence plan. The fact that he had a constitutionally protected interest in good time did not deprive the legislature of the right to enact legislation that possibly had the effect of impacting that statutorily created interest. And the fact that the Department could not deprive the petitioner of good time without a hearing did not have any legal relevance to the situation here because the Department did nothing to deprive petitioner of his good time; rather, the Department was prohibited by statute from releasing the petitioner.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1034 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


McMillin v. McMillin


08-502


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-502 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/25/09); 6 So. 3d 414; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 437



March 25, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CONCORDIA, NO. 39500 "B". HONORABLE LEO BOOTHE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, AS AMENDED; REVERSED IN PART; AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grandparents filed a motion and rule for contempt against defendant mother in the Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Concordia (Louisiana). The trial court denied the mother's exception of no cause of action, ordered visitation for the grandparents, ordered the mother to inform the child of the existence of her biological father, and found the mother in contempt. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The mother and father had one baby and were divorced a year later. The father died not long after the divorce, and the grandparents (his parents) and the mother agreed to a visitation schedule. Meanwhile, the mother remarried and had another child, her third. The grandparents claimed that the mother had twice denied them visitation. The court held that the trial court erred in not granting the mother's exception of no right of action as to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344. The father was divorced at the time of his death and neither interdicted nor incarcerated; § 9:344 was inapplicable. The court found that the consent judgment affording grandparent visitation created an extraordinary circumstance, allowing visitation under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 136(B); however, the extensive grandparent visitation granted, two weekends per month, was unreasonable. They lived three hours apart; the mother was caring for three children who had other visitation obligations. The court reduced the amount of visitation to one weekend a month, with the grandparents doing the driving. The mother, not the court, could decide when her daughter should be told about her biological father.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court as to its denial of the exception of no cause of action only as it pertained to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment awarding grandparent visitation but reduced the amount of time to one weekend per month, with the grandparents in charge of transportation.

 

1035 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Pate v. Reg'l Transit Auth.


NO. 2008-CA-1147


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-1147 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/11/09); 8 So. 3d 744; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 390



March 11, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 14, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2005-9901, DIVISION "D-16". HONORABLE LLOYD J. MEDLEY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT AMENDED AND, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After her first suit was dismissed, appellant passenger brought a second suit against appellee transit authority for injuries sustained by inhaling dangerous chemical fumes while riding on a bus. The transit authority filed an exception of prescription, which the Civil District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, granted. The passenger appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the passenger contended the trial court erred in granting the transit authority's exception of prescription. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that the time that the passenger's first lawsuit was pending from its filing to its dismissal did not interrupt or suspend the running of prescription. The passenger was required to file her second suit and to request service on the transit authority within 90 days of filing of the lawsuit, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5107(D). Since she failed to file this second lawsuit by that date, the trial court's granting of the exception of prescription was correct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was amended to set forth that the passenger's lawsuit was prescribed and, accordingly, it was dismissed with prejudice.

 

1036 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Derouen's Heavy Equip., Inc. v. Lafayette City-Parish Consol. Gov't


08-1077


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-1077 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/04/09); 7 So. 3d 48; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 339



March 4, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. C 20082189. HONORABLE GLENNON P. EVERETT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sought review of an order from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which denied its petition for a preliminary injunction against defendant city government in an action challenging the constitutionality of a zoning ordinance.


OVERVIEW: In 2003, the property owner secured a permit from the Louisiana Department of Environmental Quality (DEQ) to operate a construction and debris landfill. In 2008, the city-parish determined that the landfill had to comply with the greenbelt and buffer requirements provided in an ordinance. The owner ceased landfill operations and filed a petition for a preliminary injunction. The owner claimed that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague. The trial court denied the preliminary injunction. On appeal, the court found that the owner failed to prove that the city-parish threatened any irreparable injury. Because a showing of irreparable harm was necessary to prove entitlement to a preliminary injunction, and the owner failed to meet that burden, the court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's denial of the preliminary injunction. Further, the owner failed to exhaust its administrative remedies. While completing the process to get a permit from DEQ, the owner never took any steps to ensure compliance with the ordinance, or sought a waiver from those parts of the ordinance it found burdensome by petitioning the city-parish for a waiver or variance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.
