State v. Jacobs


08-1068


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-1068 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/04/09); 6 So. 3d 315; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 401



March 4, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Jacobs, 23 So. 3d 931, 2009 La. LEXIS 3693 (La., 2009)
Writ denied by, Post-conviction proceeding at State ex rel. Jacobs v. State, 2014 La. LEXIS 2158 (La., Oct. 3, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 288,098. HONORABLE THOMAS M. YEAGER, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana) of possession of cocaine, greater than 28 grams and less than 200 grams in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(F)(1)(a). Defendant appealed, raising many issues including ineffective assistance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised many issues on appeal, but the court affirmed. The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because he had constructive possession of the cocaine seized. The trial court concluded that defendant's explanation for excluding a juror was a pretext of discrimination. The court did not disturb this on appeal. The juror declared that she could be fair and impartial and there was no indication that her part-time employment in a church nursery would affect her ability to be fair. Thus, defendant's seemingly race-neutral explanation was not plausible or supported by the record. Because, contrary to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 841(A), defendant failed to object to the trial court's ruling regarding another juror, defendant did not preserve the right to appeal this ruling. Given that a letter not part of the record could not be considered regarding defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel, plus the record lacked information needed to substantiate defendant's claim, the claim could not be resolved on appeal and had to be relegated to post-conviction relief under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The ineffective assistance matter was relegated to post-conviction relief.

 

1038 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


France v. Eastern Cent. Bossier Fire Prot. Dist. No. 1


No. 44,058-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


44,058 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/25/09); 4 So. 3d 959; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 267



February 25, 2009, Judgment rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by France v. E. Cent. Bossier Fire Prot. Dist. No. 1, 8 So. 3d 589, 2009 La. LEXIS 1510 (La., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 124,006. Honorable Jeffrey S. Cox, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED. PARTIAL SUMMARY JUDGMENT GRANTED. REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fireman brought a civil service claim against his employer, appellee fire district, for denial of procedural due process when he was terminated. The Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, granted summary judgment in favor of the district and dismissed it from the suit on the grounds that the fireman was not entitled to the protections of the Louisiana civil service law. The fireman appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the fireman contended the district court erred by dismissing the district from the suit and granting it summary judgment. The appellate court agreed, finding that even if La. Const. art. X, § 16 extended constitutional protection to a small subset of fire protection districts, the Article made no express prohibition barring the general plenary power of the legislature to enact civil service laws for all other fire protection districts. Likewise, if the purpose of La. Const. art. X, § 16 was to provide constitutional protection to only a subset of all fire protection districts, such purpose was not inconsistent or irreconcilable with the legislative purpose of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2531 et seq., which had previously established civil service for all fire protection districts. As such, the appellate court concluded that the civil service system of § 33:2531 et seq. applied to the district, the fireman's employer, and summary judgment in its favor was improper.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment was reversed; the fireman's motion for partial summary judgment was granted; and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

State ex rel. J.S.


NO. 2008-CA-1401


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-1401 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/18/09); 6 So. 3d 904; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 381



February 18, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 24, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JUVENILE COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2008-053-01-DQ-E, SECTION "E". Honorable Louis F. Douglas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged a judgment of the Juvenile Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), adjudicating him delinquent for possession marijuana.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the juvenile court erred by admitting into evidence the criminalist certificate as prima facie proof of its contents and proper custody, and therefore the juvenile's adjudication as delinquent was reversed, because the juvenile had subpoenaed the criminalist who made the certificate five days in advance of trial under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:501(B)(1) and the juvenile court was without authority to shorten defense counsel's time frame for filing in order to be timely. The court also held that the juvenile court did not err by denying the juvenile's motion to suppress marijuana because the officer's actions did not constitute either an actual stop or an imminent actual stop, and therefore, the juvenile abandoned the bag containing marijuana prior to any unlawful intrusion into his right to be left alone from governmental interference.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded to the juvenile court for a new trial.

Needom v. Robein


NO. 2008-CA-0318 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2008-CA-0319


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-0318 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/18/09); 7 So. 3d 30; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 358



February 18, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 24, 2009.
Writ denied by Needom v. Robein, 6 So. 3d 814, 2009 La. LEXIS 363 (La., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NOS. 2005-7076, 2005-12408, DIVISION "B-15". HONORABLE ROSEMARY LEDET, JUDGE.
New Orleans Firefighters Local 632 v. City of New Orleans, 887 So. 2d 475, 2004 La. LEXIS 3542 (La., Nov. 15, 2004)
New Orleans Firefighters Local 632 v. City of New Orleans, 887 So. 2d 475, 2004 La. LEXIS 3543 (La., Nov. 15, 2004)
New Orleans Firefighters Local 632 v. City of New Orleans, 980 So. 2d 760, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 332 (La.App. 4 Cir., 2008)
New Orleans Firefighters Local 632 v. City of New Orleans, 876 So. 2d 211, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1520 (La.App. 4 Cir., May 26, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff firefighters appealed a judgment of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), dismissing their legal malpractice action against defendant attorney with prejudice on the ground that the action was not timely filed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605.


OVERVIEW: The attorney filed suit against the city on behalf of the firefighters in 1981. In 2004, the firefighters learned that the suit against the city did not include a claim for longevity pay under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:1992(B) and in 2005 they sued the attorney for legal malpractice for failing to including the claim. On appeal, the court held that § 9:5605 was constitutional and therefore the firefighter's action was properly dismissed. The court held that § 9:5605 did not violate La. Const. art. I, § 22 because the firefighters' erroneous argument that the access to courts clause ensured everyone a right to have his claims heard ignored the exclusions from that universal access concept by means of the legislatively created statutes of limitations. The court further held that it could not consider § 9:5605's legislative history it making its determination because the statute was clear and unambiguous.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Rochon v. Young


NO. 2008 CA 1349


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2008 1349 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/13/09); 6 So. 3d 890; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 208



February 13, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Rochon v. La. State Dep't of Corr., 25 So. 3d 824, 2010 La. LEXIS 222 (La., 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari dismissed by, Motion denied by Rochon v. Cain, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 4313 (U.S., May 24, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Case No. 536,041. The Honorable Timothy E. Kelley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; MOTION FOR TRANSFER OF DOCUMENTATION GRANTED; MOTION FOR PRELIMINARY DEFAULT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner filed a petition for writ of mandamus, asking the court to compel appellee prison employees to first obtain his written consent before authorizing anyone to photograph him for anything other than a prison identification card. The 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, dismissed the petition without prejudice for failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: A Commissioner recommended that the prisoner's suit be dismissed without prejudice because the court lacks subject matter jurisdiction due to the prisoner's failure to exhaust his administrative remedies. The Commissioner also recommended that the prisoner be assessed a strike for filing suit prior to exhausting his administrative remedies. The trial court followed the recommendations. The prisoner alleged that the trial court erred in dismissing his petition because the trial court had original jurisdiction to hear his petition for mandamus, alleging La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171 was unconstitutional, and challenging the trial court's assessment of a strike against him under the Prison Litigation Reform Act (PLRA). The prisoner's challenge to the constitutionality of the statute was required to be questioned first in the trial court, and it was required to be specifically pled. The issue was not properly before the appellate court. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171, the prisoner was required to first submit his complaint to the administrative remedy process prior to filing suit, and his failure to do so deprived the court of jurisdiction over the matter.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the petition without prejudice, granted his motion to transfer documentation, and denied his motion for preliminary default.

 

1042 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. D.J.


NO. 2008-CA-0786 C/W NO. 2008-CA-0981


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-0786 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/11/09); 5 So. 3d 923; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 244



February 11, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 16, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM JUVENILE COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NOS. 2008-105-02-DQ-F C/W 2008-179-03-DQ-F, SECTION "F". HONORABLE MARK DOHERTY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a judgment from the Juvenile Court Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which granted defendant juvniles' motions to quash.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a delinquency petition against both juveniles charging them with illegal possession of a handgun by a juvenile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.8. The juveniles both filed a motion to quash claiming that the offenses could not be the basis of a delinquency petition and that § 14:95.8 was not a charge that met the definition of a delinquent act under La. Child. Code Ann. art. 804.3. The court found that there was a major distinction between the adult offense condemned by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95(A)(1), carrying a concealed weapon, and the underlying offense in § 14:95.8, which condemned merely the knowing possession of a handgun by a person under seventeen. None of the operative provisions of § 14:95(A) condemned what was prohibited by § 14:95.8(A). Because an adult could not be charged with a violation of § 14:95.8 and La. Child. Code Ann. art. 804.3 defined a delinquent act as an act committed by a child of 10 years of age or older which if committed by an adult was designated an offense under the statutes or ordinances of the State of Louisiana, the delinquency proceedings in the juvenile court could not be based on a violation of § 14:95.8.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the juvenile court's judgment.

 

1043 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sede


NO. 08-KA-547


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


08-547 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/10/09); 8 So. 3d 702; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 200



February 10, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Sede v. State, 2010 La. LEXIS 507 (La., Mar. 5, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 01-5336, DIVISION "C". HONORABLE JUNE B. DARENSBURG, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, convicting him of two counts of first degree murder, and sentencing him to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: In 2001, a grand jury indicted defendant on two counts of first degree murder. Defendant pled not guilty and was later found incompetent to stand trial. Almost two years later, the trial court held another sanity hearing and determined defendant was competent to stand trial. In June 2005, defendant changed his former pleas to not guilty by reason of insanity. In March 2007, defendant withdrew those pleas and entered guilty pleas on both counts of first degree murder. The trial court accepted defendant's pleas and sentenced defendant to life imprisonment. Defendant was granted an out-of-time appeal. Defendant argued that the trial judge should have recused herself under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 671 and refused to accept his guilty pleas because she represented defendant at his arraignment. The appellate court ruled that defendant was barred on appeal from raising the issue of the trial judge's failure to recuse because he entered an unconditional guilty plea and the failure to recuse was a non-jurisdictional defect that was waived by an unconditional guilty plea. Also, the appellate court declined to consider the trial judge's failure to recuse sua sponte as an error patent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

1045 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


City of Jeanerette v. Hamilton


08-1248


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-1248 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/04/09); 3 So. 3d 674; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 147



February 4, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 08-04199, DIST. 04. SAM L. LOWERY, ADMINISTRATIVE LAW JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city filed a Disputed Claim for Compensation (a 1008) against defendant employee in the Office of Workers' Compensation, Parish of Lafayette, Louisiana. The city alleged that the employee violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208 by misrepresenting his travel expenses. The employee's exception of no right of action was granted, and the city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city's claim was filed by the adjuster for the self-insured risk fund covering the city. The employee relied upon La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1314 and La. Admin. Code tit. 40, § I.5545, to argue that the city's claim should be barred because its claim was filed by an insurance adjuster instead of an attorney. The court rejected this argument, observing that § I.5545 clearly stated that the presence of an attorney was required in all hearings. The use of these specific words ruled out any generalization that could be interpreted to entail the requirement of an attorney for filings. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310(A) and § I.5545, an adjuster could file the 1008 on behalf of the insurer, but counsel was required to be present and represent the company or the insurer at all hearings before the Workers' Compensation Judge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

1046 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Ralph v. City of New Orleans


NO. 2008-CA-0767


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-0767 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/15/09); 4 So. 3d 146; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 101; 45 Employee Benefits Cas. (BNA) 2381; 105 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 548



January 15, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2003-9871, DIVISION "J-13". Honorable Nadine M. Ramsey, Judge.
Ralph v. City of New Orleans, 928 So. 2d 537, 2006 La. LEXIS 1431 (La., May 5, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers filed a declaratory action against defendants city and city council in the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), seeking a declaration that the city and council acted ultra vires and without statutory authority when they provided for a registry of Domestic Partnerships. The district court granted the city's motion for summary judgment, and the taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city, a home rule city under La. Const. art. VI, § 4, allowed its employees who had registered as domestic partners to claim dependent benefits for their partners. The court held that the taxpayers were not entitled to summary judgment because their motion was premature under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 966 because the city had not filed its answer. The taxpayers contended that no law authorized the creation of the city's domestic partnership scheme, making it violative of La. Const. art. VI, § 9. The court rejected this position, noting that the ordinance did not control the making and administration of domestic partnerships but merely provided a registration mechanism. There was nothing in the ordinance that "governed" private or civil relationships in violation of art. VI, § 9; the registry ordinance did not rule domestic partnerships by right or authority, exercise a directing or restraining influence over the partnerships, or guide them. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:3062 allowed the city to contract for insurance protection for its officers and employees; therefore, the provision of health benefits was provided by law within the meaning of La. Const. art. VI, § 9.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the city.

 

1047 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morrison


No. 43,815-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


43,815 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/14/09); 999 So. 2d 1197; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 34



January 14, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by La. v. Morrison, 2009 La. LEXIS 3234 (La., Nov. 6, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 06865-F. Honorable Carl V. Sharp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Morehouse (Louisiana) of aggravated rape and was sentenced to life imprisonment without benefit of parole probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his confession was not voluntary under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:451. The court of appeal disagreed. A detective testified that defendant initially refused to sign the warning and waiver of rights form, so he wrote "refused" on the signature line. Later, defendant agreed to talk with the detectives and signed his name on the warning and waiver of rights form next to the word "refused." Defendant was not moved from room to room during the process and defendant's wife was not brought to the station until after defendant began making his statement. Defendant acknowledged that the waiver of rights form was read to him before he signed it. Defendant also admitted saying he had told the truth at the conclusion of his statement. The State established that defendant was advised of his rights and that he voluntarily waived them prior to making the statement. There was no evidence that the statement was made under the influence of fear, duress, intimidation, menaces, threats, inducements or promises. Defendant admitted he had been through the interrogation process before and that he told the detectives he knew his rights and wished to waive them.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Dotie


No. 43,819-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


43,819 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/14/09); 1 So. 3d 833; 2009 La. App. LEXIS 27



January 14, 2009, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application denied by State ex rel. Dotie v. State, 2012 La. LEXIS 2291 (La., Sept. 12, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 260,858. Honorable Jeanette G. Garrett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND ADJUDICATION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE CORRECTED TO DELETE FINE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, convicting him of possession of a firearm by a convicted felon under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1, adjudicating him as a second felony offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, and sentencing him to 20 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and convicted after police officers found drugs and a gun in his vehicle following a traffic stop. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because: (1) the officer verified that the vehicle belonged to the mother of defendant's child and defense witnesses agreed that defendant drove it 90 percent of the time, so a rational juror could find that he exercised full dominion and control over the car; and (2) a rational juror could also conclude that the large semiautomatic revolver, even enclosed in the console, was within the driver's easy reach in the compact vehicle. The district court did not err by allowing the State to file an amended bill of information after the trial had begun and denying defendant's motion for a mistrial because both bills charged defendant with possession of a firearm by a convicted felon and therefore the amendment did not charge a new offense or add a new crime. Both felonies had been disclosed to defendant in discovery. The trial court did not err by adjudicating defendant as a habitual offender because the holding in the Baker case applied retroactively.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and multiple offender adjudication were affirmed. The sentence was corrected to delete the imposition of a fine and was otherwise affirmed.

 

1049 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Orleans Parish Sch. Bd.


NO. 2008-CA-0837


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-0837 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/30/08); 2 So. 3d 1128; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1847



December 30, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 5, 2009.
Writ denied by Smith v. Orleans Parish Sch. Bd., 1 So. 3d 501, 2009 La. LEXIS 1359 (La., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION. NO. 08-1459, DISTRICT "EIGHT". HONORABLE GWENDOLYN F. THOMPSON, WORKERS' COMPENSATION JUDGE.
Smith v. Orleans Parish School Bd., 436 So. 2d 586, 1983 La. App. LEXIS 8730 (La.App. 4 Cir., 1983)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant employee filed a disputed claim for compensation with the Office of Workers' Compensation (OWC) seeking reinstatement of benefits from defendant employer. The employer filed a variety of exceptions, including lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The OWC determined that it lacked jurisdiction and dismissed the employee's case. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee's original injury was in 1980, before the enactment of the Workers' Compensation Act. She therefore filed her claim in district court and eventually entered into a consent judgment. In 2006, the employer ceased paying her benefits. The court held that the employee was not asserting a new claim, nor was she seeking modification of a prior order. She sought to enforce a prior judgment of the district court. Therefore, the district court had continuing jurisdiction to enforce its orders. Accordingly, the civil district court, not the OWC, had jurisdiction over the employee's claim. The 2005 amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.3(E) only added to the illustrative list of the types of claims in which the OWC was vested with original, exclusive jurisdiction. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.3(E), providing that the OWC was vested with exclusive jurisdiction over all claims or disputes arising out of the worker's compensation chapter, did not apply because the employee's claim arose out of prior law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the OWC dismissing the employee's case for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.

 

1050 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Piazza's Seafood World, LLC v. Odom


NO. 2007 CA 2191 AND NO. 2007 CW 2077


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 2191 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/23/08); 6 So. 3d 820; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1739



December 23, 2008, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Piazza's Seafood World, LLC v. Odom, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 112220 (M.D. La., Oct. 20, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 556,928. Honorable William A. Morvant, Judge Presiding.
Piazza's Seafood World v. Odom, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 11149 (E.D. La., June 17, 2004)



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED; EXCEPTIONS DENIED; ISSUANCE OF PRELIMINARY INJUNCTION AFFIRMED; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, granted a preliminary injunction in favor of appellee importer enjoining appellant, Commissioner of the Department of Agriculture and Forestry for the State of Louisiana's (Commissioner), authority to enforce the agency regulations regarding inspections for certain antibiotics in imported seafood. The Commissioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that subject matter jurisdiction was conferred by the Louisiana Constitution, La. Const. art. 5, § 2. The legislature could not, by statute, divest the district court of its constitutional subject matter jurisdiction to determine the legality of administrative regulations, and to issue an injunction preventing enforcement if the regulations were found to be illegally promulgated. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:963 did not divest the district court of its subject matter jurisdiction over the proceeding. Agency review of the constitutionality of the regulations was not a prerequisite to the importer's filing an action for injunctive relief since only the district court could decide the constitutionality of the regulations. The district court properly denied the Commissioner's dilatory exception raising the objection of prematurity, as well as the Commissioner's peremptory exception raising the objection of no cause of action. Because La. Admin. Code tit. 7, § 35.511, was promulgated without legislative or constitutional authority, the district court properly issued a preliminary injunction enjoining the Commissioner's authority to enforce the unlawful regulation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed; the Commissioner's application for a supervisory writ of review was denied and the case was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

State v. D. T.


08-814


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-814 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/17/08); 998 So. 2d 1258; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1695



December 17, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. D. T., 2009 La. App. LEXIS 179 (La.App. 3 Cir., Feb. 4, 2009)

Writ denied by State v. Trimble, 22 So. 3d 171, 2009 La. LEXIS 3460 (La., 2009)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Trimble v. State, 131 So. 3d 53, 2014 La. LEXIS 235 (La., 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Trimble v. Cain, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 94216 (W.D. La., June 29, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF IBERIA, NO. 06-402. HONORABLE GERARD B. WATTIGNY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AMENDED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 16th Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia (Louisiana), convicting him of four counts of aggravated rape in violation of La.R.S. 14:42 and sentencing him to four consecutive life sentences at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for raping the four victims, his young nieces and stepdaughter. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction for the aggravated rape of his stepdaughter because her testimony showed that defendant had sex with her in 1999 when she was 12 years old, not under the age of 12, as required by La.R.S. 14:42. However, the evidence was sufficient to support a conviction of forcible rape under La. R.S. 14:42.1 because the stepdaughter testified that defendant pushed her over the couch and had vaginal sexual intercourse with her, that her face was buried in the sofa during the incident, and when she pushed up from the couch and asked defendant to stop, he pushed her back down and continued. The court rejected defendant's contention that the time limitations for the institution of prosecution had lapsed with respect to the cases involving his nieces because in 1984, while the original prescriptive periods for the offenses were still running, La. Code Crim.P. art. 571 was amended to remove the time limitations on prosecution for aggravated rape. Defendant's life sentences without benefits were not excessive.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for the aggravated rape of his stepdaughter was vacated and a judgment of guilty was entered for the crime of forcible rape, and the case was remanded for resentencing on that conviction. Defendant's remaining convictions and sentences were affirmed.

State v. Otero


NO. 08-KA-188


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


08-188 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/16/08); 3 So. 3d 34; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1697



December 16, 2008, Decided

Writ denied by State v. Otero, 18 So. 3d 80, 2009 La. LEXIS 2743 (La., 2009)
Appeal after remand at State v. Otero, 31 So. 3d 1125, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 108 (La.App. 5 Cir., 2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Otero v. La., 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 163829 (E.D. La., Aug. 12, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 05-3095, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND REMANDED WITH ORDERS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, which convicted him of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64, sentenced him to 35 years' imprisonment at hard labor, and imposed an additional five years imprisonment at hard labor under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.3.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was arrested without probable cause in Orleans Parish and that any statement given thereafter was illegal and inadmissible. Defendant also claimed that the State made improper comments during its closing argument and that his sentence under § 14:64.3 was unconstitutional. The court held that because defendant was transported to Jefferson Parish pursuant to a valid arrest warrant, his argument that the Orleans arrest was illegal was moot. His confession and identification of himself from the bank's surveillance photos were admissible because they were given freely and voluntarily and not under duress or intimidation. The State's comments about fingerprint evidence was in response to defendant's closing argument raising the issue of the lack of fingerprint evidence. Although the jury did not specifically find that the crime was committed with a firearm, because the enhanced sentence did not increase the penalty beyond the maximum term, there was no due process violation in the application of § 14:64.3. Finally, pursuant to the terms of § 14:64.3 in effect at the time of the commission of the crime, defendant could not be sentenced to hard labor thereunder.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the enhanced sentence, affirmed the remainder of the judgment, and remanded to the trial court for sentencing in accordance with the provisions of §14:64.3 as written at the time of the commission of the crime.

 

1053 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. McGraw


No. 43,778-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


43,778 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/10/08); 1 So. 3d 645; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1603



December 10, 2008, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by La. v. James L. McGraw, 21 So. 3d 297, 2009 La. LEXIS 3236 (La., Nov. 6, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 05-F3310. Honorable Carl Van Sharp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana) of attempted possession of a controlled dangerous substance (hydrocodone). Defendant received the maximum sentence of two and one-half years' imprisonment at hard labor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that evidence of the driver's arrest for possession of cocaine and the marijuana found in the vehicle prejudiced the verdict by showing defendant's bad acts. The court of appeal disagreed. The central issue in the case was whether defendant had constructive possession of the hydrocodone pill. Thus, issues of defendant's knowledge and intent were necessary to the State's proof. Both the arrest of the driver for possession of crack cocaine and the discovery of the marijuana in the driver's door occurred simultaneously with the discovery of the hydrocodone. Those facts formed an integral part of the act that formed the basis for the proceedings. Moreover, facts relating to the existence of other drugs in the car had probative value and were relevant to issues of defendant's intent to possess, his exercise of dominion and control, and knowledge of the drug. The jury was free to infer that the driver's possession of cocaine exculpated defendant as he might have also placed the pill in the center console. Likewise, the jury could have inferred defendant's friends' joint enjoyment of illegal drugs.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Savoy


KA 08-716


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-716 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/11/08); 999 So. 2d 285; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1642

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 15th Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), convicting her of negligent homicide and sentencing her to five years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for the death of the 11-month old victim while in her care. The victim had a fractured skull with cerebral edema and cranial bleeding. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion for a post-verdict judgment of acquittal based on House Concurrent Resolution No. 3 (2008), which directed the Louisiana State Law Institute to study La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 814(C) to determine whether amendments were necessary to clarify the legislative intent behind that article. The court further held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because it would have supported the greater crime charged, manslaughter. The record showed that the victim died due to a major blow to his head and the only person with him during the time period in which he was injured that was capable of inflicting such a blow was defendant.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

Habeas corpus proceeding at, Magistrate's recommendation at Major v. Batson, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 108846 (E.D. La., July 10, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH, NO. 471-366, SECTION "H". Honorable Camille Buras, Judge.
State v. Major, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1877 (La.App. 4 Cir., Apr. 10, 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) of possession of a firearm by a convicted felon under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1. He was sentenced to 15 years at hard labor without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence, but the trial court suspended the imposed fine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised many issues on appeal, but the court affirmed. Given that the trial court imposed the mandatory sentence of 15 years as well as the mandatory fine permitted under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1(B) of $ 5,000 and then suspended that fine, the court found that there was no error patent. The evidence was sufficient to support the jury's finding of possession in defendant's trial. At a minimum, defendant had constructive possession of the gun that was underneath the driver's seat when he was driving. The jury chose to believe that defendant's action proved his awareness of the presence of the gun and that he had the general criminal intent under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:10(2) to possess the gun. For purposes of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 and La. Const. art. I, § 20, the court found no abuse of discretion in the trial court's sentence. The State carried its burden to prove defendant's guilt of the predicate offense and the court rejected defendant's claim that the information did not meet the technical requirements of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 483. For purposes of U.S. Const. amend. VI, ineffective assistance of counsel was not shown.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Johnson v. Dep't of Police


NO. 2008-CA-0467


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-0467 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/10/08); 2 So. 3d 501; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1823



December 10, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CITY CIVIL SERVICE COMMISSION ORLEANS. NO. 7384.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer sought review of the decision of the City Civil Service Commission for the City of New Orleans (Commission) (Louisiana), which found in favor of appellee, the New Orleans Police Department (NOPD), and affirmed his suspension and termination from his position as a police officer.


OVERVIEW: The police officer appealed the Commission's ruling affirming his suspension and termination from his position as a police officer for the sustained violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:35. The police officer was identified by the victim as the officer who punched him while he was in the custody of two other police officers. The appellate court affirmed, stating that the Commission's conclusion that the police officer violated the NOPD's rule requiring adherence to the law when he committed a simple battery on the victim was reasonable. In light of the special relationship between the members of the NOPD and the public, conduct such as the police officer's clearly interfered with the efficient operation of the NOPD, violated the trust the public must have in the police force, and justified his termination.

Ealem v. Prevost Mem. Hosp.


NO. 2008-C-0064


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-0064 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/10/08); 5 So. 3d 187; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1838



December 10, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPLICATION FOR WRITS DIRECTED TO CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 06-12248, DIVISION "D". Honorable Piper D. Griffin, Judge.
Ealem v. Prevost Mem. Hosp., 992 So. 2d 969, 2008 La. LEXIS 1806 (La., 2008)



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, denied relator hospital's exception of improper venue on plaintiffs', administrator and heirs, wrongful death claim against relator and doctor for an alleged failure to diagnose the decedent's stomach cancer. The hospital sought review.


OVERVIEW: The hospital argued that the trial court erred when it failed to find that Ascension Parish was the only proper venue for plaintiffs' suit. The hospital grounded its case on the application of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 46:1063 to the facts of the case. It argued that the statute was a specific statute which provided an exclusive venue provision. The appellate court determined that § 46:1063 was not an exclusive venue provision that superseded La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5104(B). Thus, plaintiffs' wrongful death claim could proceed in Orleans Parish because the decedent died in Orleans Parish, and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5104(B) provided that venue in a suit against a political subdivision was proper if brought in a parish in which the cause of action arose.


OUTCOME: The writ was denied.

State v. Lowe


08-669


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-669 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/11/08); 999 So. 2d 194; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1646



December 10, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Lowe v. State, 183 So. 3d 501, 2015 La. LEXIS 2510 (La., Nov. 30, 2015)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Henry Bryan Lowe D.O.C. # 398433 v. Vannoy, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 71596 (W.D. La., Feb. 9, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SIXTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF BEAUREGARD, NO. CR-741-2003. HONORABLE STUART S. KAY, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.
State ex rel. Lowe v. State, 989 So. 2d 92, 2008 La. LEXIS 1656 (La., Aug. 29, 2008)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCES AFFIRMED AS AMENDED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Thirty-Sixth Judicial District Court, Parish of Beauregard (Louisiana) convicting him of two counts of aggravated rape, two counts of sexual battery, and two counts of indecent behavior with juveniles. He was sentenced to concurrent terms of life imprisonment for each rape count, 120 months at hard labor on each sexual battery count, and 84 months at hard labor on each indecent behavior count.


OVERVIEW: The evidence established that defendant touched, kissed and/or licked the vaginas of two girls under the age of thirteen. The court held that the evidence was legally sufficient to sustain his convictions for aggravated rape under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42, because penetration was not required for oral sexual intercourse. Defendant argued that his convictions for aggravated rape, sexual battery, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.1, and indecent behavior with juveniles, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81, constituted double jeopardy. The same conduct did not constitute the basis for each offense because the rape involved oral intercourse with defendant's tongue, the battery involved touching with his hand, and the indecent behavior required proof that the crimes were performed in the presence of the other victim. The court also found that defendant's remaining pro se assignments of error including ineffective assistance of counsel lacked merit. Pursuant to the court's review for errors patent on the face of the record, La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 920, defendant's sentence was amended to reflect that dimunition eligibility was denied under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:537(A).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentences as amended. The court remanded.

 

1059 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reed


No. 43,780-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


43,780 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/03/08); 1 So. 3d 561; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1588



December 3, 2008, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Reed, 18 So. 3d 103, 2009 La. LEXIS 2809 (La., Oct. 2, 2009)
Writ denied by State v. Reed, 18 So. 3d 100, 2009 La. LEXIS 2843 (La., Oct. 2, 2009)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Reed v. State, 99 So. 3d 43, 2012 La. LEXIS 2833 (La., Oct. 12, 2012)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Reed v. Cain, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 68559 (W.D. La., Jan. 27, 2014)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Reed v. State, 2017 La. LEXIS 1622 (La., Aug. 4, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 252,217. Honorable H. Ramona Emanuel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, convicted defendant of second degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1 and sentenced him to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence did not support a finding of intent. The appellate court found that the evidence established that the victim was in a defensive posture at the time of the shooting and that the bullet did not ricochet off of any other object or surface prior to hitting her, indicating a straight-on shot. A witness testified that defendant fled the scene immediately. The victim stated that defendant had just shot her. The evidence indicated that the gun was not discharged by accident. The trier of fact could have rationally inferred the specific intent of defendant from the circumstances of the case and, therefore, could have found that the evidence negated reasonable doubt as to defendant's intent. The trial court did not err in admitting evidence of defendant's batteries of previous girlfriends as a rational trier of fact could have weighed the evidence and found that defendant's guilt had been proven beyond a reasonable doubt, even absent the testimony of the former girlfriends. The fact that the same penalty was a possibility under two different statutes was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Baylor


KA 08-141


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-141 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/26/08); 998 So. 2d 800; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1557



November 26, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. Baylor, 2012 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 382 (La.App. 3 Cir., May 30, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 281055. HONORABLE DONALD THADDEUS JOHNSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONDITIONALLY AFFIRMED, REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which convicted him of attempted carjacking, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:27 and 14:64.2, and unauthorized use of a motor vehicle, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:68.4.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for attempted carjacking and unauthorized use of a motor vehicle and the appellate court conditionally affirmed the judgment. The verdict indicated that the jury chose to believe the victim's testimony that defendant did not have permission to use the truck after the victim left defendant's residence and that credibility determination should not be second-guessed by the appellate court. Accordingly, defendant's conviction for unauthorized use of a motor vehicle was affirmed. His conviction for attempted carjacking was also affirmed because defendant dove head first through the victim's passenger window and told the victim to go. An officer also testified that it appeared to him that defendant attacked the victim and was trying to take the car. The jury was not irrational in choosing to favor the view of two police officers over that of the attempted carjacking victim. The matter was further remanded, in part for an evidentiary hearing in order for the trial court to determine whether there were reasonable ground to doubt defendant's capacity to proceed to trial and sentencing.


OUTCOME: The appellate court conditionally affirmed the judgment and remanded to the trial court for an evidentiary hearing to determine whether there were reasonable grounds to doubt defendant's capacity to proceed. Further, the trial court was ordered to correct the sentencing minutes to accurately reflect the sentences imposed and to inform defendant of the correct provisions of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8.

Guidry v. Haney


08-469


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-469 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/26/08); 999 So. 2d 1167; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1555



November 26, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Guidry v. Haney, 21 So. 3d 293, 2009 La. LEXIS 3085 (La., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARTIN, NO. 90-71567. HONORABLE GERARD B. WATTIGNY, DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. Guidry, 647 So. 2d 502, 1994 La. App. LEXIS 3380 (La.App. 3 Cir., Dec. 7, 1994)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order from the Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Martin (Louisiana), which granted respondent district attorney's exception of no right of action on a petition for a writ of mandamus seeking the production of taped interviews of petitioner's rape victim.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of aggravated rape. He later filed a petition for a writ of mandamus seeking the production of audio and video taped interviews of the victim. The district attorney filed a peremptory exception of no right of action and failure to join an indispensable party. The trial court granted the exception of no right of action. On appeal, the court found that the record did not support petitioner's assertion of newly discovered facts. The public records that he sought were recorded prior to his criminal trial and were known to him and discussed in previous filings by him. He had no right of action under La. Rev. Stat. He did not allege any of the enumerated grounds in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.3 that would support an application for postconviction relief, nor did he establish the applicability of an exception to the time limitation for filing an application for postconviction relief under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8(A)(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1062 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tassin


KA 08-752


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-752 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/05/08); 998 So. 2d 278; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1480



November 5, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Tassin, 2009 La. LEXIS 2631 (La., Sept. 18, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 117533. HONORABLE JOHN DAMIAN TRAHAN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of simple burglary and sentenced to eight years at hard labor. Subsequently, he was adjudicated a fourth felony offender under the Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, and the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette, Louisiana, vacated the original sentence and sentenced defendant to serve 20 years at hard labor without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that he was subjected to a possible life sentence and that therefore the habitual offender proceedings should have been instituted by the filing of an indictment returned by a grand jury. The reviewing court disagreed. Habitual offender proceedings under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 did not have to be instituted by grand jury indictment. The court also held that: (1) a jury trial was not required for the habitual offender proceeding; (2) the State properly introduced the court minutes showing that defendant pled guilty to the predicate offenses and was represented by counsel at each plea; (3) under La. Code Crim. Proc. art. 841, defendant waived the argument that there was insufficient evidence to prove that he was the person who had been convicted of the prior offenses; (4) defendant failed to prove that the State's pursuit of the habitual offender bill was vindictive because he produced no evidence to suggest that the State filed the habitual offender bill of information for the purpose of deterring or punishing the exercise of his legal rights; and (5) defendant was not entitled to a downward departure from the mandatory minimum sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

 

1063 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. S.L.D.


08-549


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


08-549 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/05/08); 997 So. 2d 759; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1444



November 5, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 20, 2009.
Writ denied by State v. S.L.D., 2009 La. LEXIS 3153 (La., Oct. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SIXTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF BEAUREGARD, NO. CR 120-05. HONORABLE HERMAN I. STEWART JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Thirty-Sixth Judicial District Court, Parish of Beauregard (Louisiana) of two of six counts of felony carnal knowledge of a juvenile under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:80. The trial court adjudicated defendant a fourth felony offender for purposes of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 and imposed concurrent 25 years at hard labor sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised various issues on appeal, but the court affirmed. For purposes of defendant's convictions, there was sufficient evidence to prove that defendant, who was older than 19, participated in consensual oral sexual intercourse with the victim, who was younger than 17. Because the date of the offense was not an element of the crime, the State was not required to prove the offense occurred on the date alleged in the charging instrument, for purposes of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 468. The victim testified at trial, was cross-examined by the defense, offered testimony inconsistent with a prior statement, and then specifically refuted the veracity of her prior statement. Thus, under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 801(D), her inconsistent statements were nonhearsay and the trial court was not required to perform the balancing test of La. Code Evid Ann. art. 607(D)(2). Defendant was adjudicated a fourth felony offender and the applicable sentencing provision was La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(c)(i). Defendant's sentences were in the low-range of those possible, and the court did not find that the sentences were excessive under La. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1064 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Ray v. DOL


2008/CA/0390


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2008/0390 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/03/08); 998 So. 2d 206; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1422



November 3, 2008, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE STATE CIVIL SERVICE COMMISSION. DOCKET NUMBER S-16133, THE HONORABLE JAMES A. SMITH, CHAIRMAN; BURL CAIN, VICE-CHAIRMAN; CHATHAM REED, DAVID DUPLANTIER, G. LEE GRIFFIN, ROSA B. JACKSON AND JOHN MCLURE.



DISPOSITION: MODIFIED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A hearing referee awarded appellant employee $750.00 in attorney fees, which was appealed and affirmed by appellee Louisiana State Civil Service Commission (Commission). The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee's attorney argued that an award of $750.00 for 17 hours of work amounted to an attorney fee of $44.12 an hour, which was arbitrary and capricious. He argued that the Attorney Fee Review Board established a minimum hourly rate of $100.00 and a maximum hourly rate of $400.00. The appellate court found that the conclusions reached by the hearing referee suggested that he intended to consider some of the factors established in the Rules of Professional Conduct. The record did not state how the factors were evaluated. The appellate court noted that the severity of the disciplinary action was generally not material to the amount of time an attorney spent in interviewing a client, conversing with opposing counsel, drafting pleadings or reviewing a file in preparation for a hearing. There was also merit in the employee's argument that his professional duty required him to put forth his best effort to represent his client no matter the penalty appealed from. There was no reasonable basis for a factual finding that the attorney did not expend 17 hours on behalf of the employee.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified to provide that attorney fees in the amount of $1,500 were awarded to the attorney.

 

1065 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Penton


NUMBER 2008 KA 0551


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2008 0551 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/31/08); 998 So. 2d 184; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1404



October 31, 2008, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Twenty-First Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of Tangipahoa, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 603038.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pled no contest to one count of computer-aided solicitation for sexual purposes, the Twenty-First Judicial District Court of Tangipahoa Parish, Louisiana, sentenced him to two years at hard labor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred in denying his motion to quash the indictment, arguing that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.3 was invalid on its face because it suppressed protected speech. The appellate court disagreed, holding that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.3 directly advanced a compelling state interest. It was evident beyond the need for elaboration that the state's interest in safeguarding the physical and psychological well-being of a minor was compelling. Further, the prevention of sexual exploitation and abuse of children constituted a government objective of surpassing importance. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.3 was narrowly tailored to prohibit criminal conduct, rather than protected speech. It was illegal to solicit a child for sex. This illegal conduct was not suddenly shielded from criminal liability when the pedophile hid behind a computer screen. Offers to engage in illegal transactions were categorically excluded from U.S. Const. amend. I protection. Because § 14:81.3 was not substantially overbroad, it was unnecessary to consider its application to situations other than those which Louisiana could restrict consistent with the First Amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Jones


NO. 08-KA-466


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


08-466 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/28/08); 998 So. 2d 178; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1385



October 28, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at State v. Jones, 998 So. 2d 173, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1392 (La.App. 5 Cir., 2008)
Related proceeding at State v. Jones, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 522 (La.App. 5 Cir., Apr. 13, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 06-5344, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE DONALD A. ROWAN, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), of illegal possession of a stolen vehicle valued at more than $ 500, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:69. He was sentenced to ten years at hard labor. The State filed a habitual offender bill of information. The trial judge found defendant to be a fourth felony offender and sentenced him to life in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the habitual offender bill of information was untimely and was vindictive, having been filed because his original ten-year sentence was too low. Defendant never raised the issues of timeliness or prosecutorial vindictiveness in the trial court. He also failed to file a motion to quash the habitual offender bill, which was the proper method to challenge the bill under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 531-532. The court decided that the filing of the bill was timely. At the beginning of the sentencing hearing, before defendant's original sentence was imposed, the State informed the trial court that it was filing the habitual offender bill. Therefore, defendant received fair notice that he would be facing enhanced penalties. The bill of information was timely because it was filed on the same date as the defendant's sentencing hearing on the underlying offense. However, the State failed to introduce into evidence the documentation relating to defendant's 1996 conviction for attempted possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. The court held that the State had failed to carry its burden of proving that defendant was a fourth felony offender.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's habitual offender sentence and remanded the case to the district court for further proceedings.

State v. Roberts


NO. 08-KA-391


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


08-391 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/28/08); 996 So. 2d 1147; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1379



October 28, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 06-1302, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE PATRICK J. MCCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), of two counts of distribution of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A). The trial court found defendant to be a third felony offender and sentenced defendant to life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence on one count. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found to be a third felony offender on the basis of an underlying conviction of distribution of cocaine and predicate convictions of distribution of cocaine and first degree robbery, pursuant to the habitual offender statute, La. Defendant filed to rebut this presumption by presenting any evidence showing any exceptional circumstances to justify a downward departure from the mandatory life sentence. The court held that the trial court was not required to comply with the sentencing guidelines of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 because the sentence imposed was statutorily prescribed under § 15:529.1.

State v. Bourgeois


NO. 08-KA-211


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


08-211 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/28/08); 998 So. 2d 165; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1383



October 28, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 05-3253, DIVISION "I". HONORABLE JO ELLEN V. GRANT, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, VACATED, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the enhanced sentence imposed by the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, following his conviction of possession of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967C, arguing that the sentencing judge improperly found that he was a fourth felony offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of cocaine. The matter proceeded to trial, defendant was found guilty, and the trial court imposed a five-year sentence of imprisonment at hard labor. On the same day, the State filed a bill of information alleging that defendant had three previous felony convictions. After defense counsel stipulated that defendant was the same person who pled guilty to the prior predicate offenses, the trial judge vacated the original sentence and sentenced defendant to imprisonment at hard labor for 20 years. In conducting a plain error review, the court held that, where the trial court did not advise defendant of his right to a formal hearing, of his right to have the State prove its case under the multiple offender statute by proving defendant's identity as the person who pled guilty, and of his right to remain silent, defendant was not informed of his statutory rights under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(D). Without such advice, defendant's acknowledgment or confession of his prior felony convictions was invalid.


OUTCOME: The district court's ruling on defendant's multiple offender adjudication was reversed, defendant's enhanced sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1069 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wright


No. 43,633-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


43,633 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/22/08); 997 So. 2d 133; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1351



October 22, 2008, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 74,779. Honorable Ford E. Stinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster (Louisiana) of 23 counts of pornography involving juveniles, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.1. He was adjudicated as a second felony offender and sentenced to a total of 40 years at hard labor, without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension. Additionally, defendant was ordered to register as a sex offender for life. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in not requiring the State to designate which precise count of his recent convictions was to be subjected to the enhancement authorized by the habitual offender statute. The court rejected this contention because there was no contemporaneous objection either at the habitual offender hearing or sentencing hearing. Further, the error was immaterial and not prejudicial because the State could have enhanced all of defendant's convictions. Defendant next argued that his sentence was excessive for his non-violent voyeuristic compulsion. The court held that the trial court complied with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 in the imposition of sentence by examining defendant's prior criminal history of two counts of carnal knowledge of a juvenile and three counts of video voyeurism. The trial court did not err in deciding that defendant was a grave risk to the safety of the community and that he was desperately in need of correctional treatment in a custodial environment. Based upon the nature of the offenses and his criminal history of sex offenses involving juveniles, there was no abuse of discretion in the imposition of the maximum sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences.

Holmes v. LSU/E. A. Conway Med. Ctr.


No. 43,662-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


43,662 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/22/08); 997 So. 2d 605; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1332



October 22, 2008, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. M011-2007. Honorable Wilson Rambo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana, granted appellee hospital an exception of prescription dismissing it from appellant parents' wrongful death action filed before a medical review panel. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents claimed that the suit was timely filed within one year of their knowledge that the hospital was covered by the Medical Malpractice Act (MMA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.47, and the facts which gave rise to the malpractice claim against the hospital. The appellate court found that, when met with an exception of prescription filed in the district court during a pending medical panel review under the MMA, the plaintiff was required to prove the defense of contra non valentem as allowed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628. The defense was necessary because the hospital's actions and the baby's death occurred almost two years before the MRP letter which commenced the action against the hospital. The parents had the burden of proof at the hearing on the exception of prescription to establish evidence of their late discovery of the hospital's negligence, which they failed to do. Section 9:5628 was not unconstitutionally vague and deprive the parents of their day in court. The constitutionality of a statute had to be first questioned in the trial court and specially pleaded with the grounds for the claim particularized.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Tipton v. Campbell


NO. 2008-CA-0139, CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2008-CA-0140


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-0139 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/24/08); 996 So. 2d 27; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1290



September 24, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 4, 2008.
Writ denied by Tipton v. Campbell, 2009 La. LEXIS 265 (La., Jan. 9, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NOS. 2003-15925 C/W 2007-8096, DIVISION "I-14". Honorable Piper D. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Patients' Compensation Fund (PCF) and the patient sought review of the decision of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which, in part, granted the State's motion for summary judgment involving the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B)(1) in a medical-malpractice case and failure to obtain an informed consent arising out of a tummy tuck. The patient had also been awarded damages from the PCF.


OVERVIEW: The patient filed an action against the doctor alleging malpractice and failure to obtain an informed consent. After settling with the doctor for less than $100,000, the patient proceeded to trial against the PCF and was awarded damages totaling $1,797,548. The trial court granted the PCF's posttrial motions and lowered the damages but denied the PCF's motion for a new trial. The patient raised the issue of the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B)(1) and the State intervened to address that issue and filed a motion for summary judgment, which the PCF adopted and which the trial court granted. The PCF and the patient appealed and the appellate court affirmed. The appellate court was unable to say that the jury was manifestly erroneous in finding that the increased risk of a wound problem was a material risk of the surgery that was not disclosed. The patient, corroborated by her uncle, testified that the doctor did not discuss the risks with her. Additionally, La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 1003 was not applicable because the authenticity of an original affidavit by a former employee of the doctor was questioned by the patient's counsel at trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
