State v. Jarrell


2007 KA 1720


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007-1720 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/12/08); 994 So. 2d 620; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1183



September 12, 2008, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court Parish of St. Tammany, State of Louisiana. Number 352175/6; District J. The Honorable William J. Knight, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED UNDER BILL OF INFORMATION # 352176; CONVICTION, HABITUAL OFFENDER ADJUDICATION, AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED UNDER BILL OF INFORMATION # 352175.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the 22nd Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana) of one count of second-offense possession of marijuana and one count of possession of oxycodone. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that an officer's expert testimony should have been excluded because it was irrelevant and more prejudicial than probative. The court of appeal disagreed. Defendant's ownership of the OxyContin recovered from the trailer was the central fact at issue in the case. The defense claimed the State's case was based on guilt by association, and specifically denied that defendant had confessed his ownership of the OxyContin recovered from the trailer. The State's theory was that not only had defendant confessed his ownership of the OxyContin, he had further stated that the police had interrupted him and the other men around the table as they were about to "shoot the half a pill of Oxycontin." The officer identified the OxyContin as a highly concentrated form of the drug and indicated that the spoon and unused hypodermic recovered from the trailer along with the OxyContin were consistent with the preparation of the drug for injection. The testimony made the existence of the defendant's alleged statements more probable, and thus, was relevant. The officer's specialized knowledge assisted the jury in understanding the evidence and determining facts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1073 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Slavich v. State


2007 CA 1149


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 1149 (La.App. 1 Cir. 08/21/08); 994 So. 2d 85; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1161



August 21, 2008, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Slavich v. State, 2008 La. LEXIS 2694 (La., Nov. 21, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, In and For the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Docket No.416,804. Honorable Timothy Kelley, Judge Presiding.
Slavich v. State, 904 So. 2d 710, 2005 La. LEXIS 2089 (La., June 17, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, lessees of state water bottoms for the purpose of harvesting oysters, sued defendant, State of Louisiana, Department of Wildlife and Fisheries (DWF), and asserted that it breached its obligations under the lease. The Nineteenth Judicial District Court, In and For the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana granted the lessees' motion for partial summary judgment and denied DWF's motion for summary judgment. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: Despite specific language by the legislature regarding the retroactivity of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 49:214.5 and 56:427.1, the lessees asserted that the retroactive application of the statutes in the instant case was unconstitutional. The court found that the retroactive application of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§. 49:214.5 and 56:427.1 created no contractual impairment of a constitutional dimension under La. Const. art. XII, § 10, was justified by a significant and legitimate purpose, and was reasonable for the public policy of coastal restoration, which justified the retroactive application of the statutes with regard to the lessees' contractual rights. However, the trial court erred when it found that the lessees' vested rights in their cause of action were disturbed by the retroactive application of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 49:214.5 and 56:427.1 in violation of the due process clauses of the state and federal constitutions because the property rights of an oyster lessee were exclusively defined in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 56:423, and the rights granted in § 56:423(B) had never been recognized as anything other than rights granted against third parties to the leases, not against the state.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The lessees' motion for summary judgment was denied and summary judgment was granted in favor of DWF. The lessees' claims were dismissed with prejudice. All costs of the appeal were assessed to the lessees.

 

1074 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Strother


No. 43,363-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


43,363 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/20/08); 990 So. 2d 130; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1145



August 20, 2008, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Strother, 8 So. 3d 580, 2009 La. LEXIS 1550 (La., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 74643. Honorable Parker Self, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster, Louisiana, that convicted him of molestation of a juvenile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2(A) and that sentenced him to 12 years in prison at hard labor under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2(A), arguing that his conviction was unsupported by sufficient evidence and that his sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: On review, the court held that, where the 14-year-old victim became intoxicated at a party supervised by the 38-year-old defendant, where the victim awakened to find herself in defendant's bed and defendant having sex with her, and where the trial court found the victim's testimony to be credible and accepted her version of events over that of defendant despite the victim's intoxication at that time, the victim's testimony provided sufficient evidence to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant committed a lewd or lascivious act upon the victim with the specific intent to gratify his sexual desire. Further, where defendant was the only adult present at a party attended by minors and created the situation that led to the lewd act by furnishing the victim with alcohol and by requiring her to stay at his house once she began drinking, the evidence established beyond a reasonable doubt defendant's use of his position of supervision or control to facilitate the commission of the crime under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81(A). As such, the sentence imposed under the harsher scheme provided by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81(C) was legal and supported by the record.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the sentence were affirmed.

 

1075 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pena


NO. 43,321-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


43,321 (La.App. 2 Cir. 07/30/08); 988 So. 2d 841; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1067



July 30, 2008, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 146006. Honorable Bruce M. Bolin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED. SENTENCE AFFIRMED AS AMENDED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, that convicted him of possession with intent to distribute marijuana in a quantity exceeding 60 pounds in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(F)(1), arguing that the district court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence because the reasons given to justify the stop of his vehicle were mere pretext.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped along an interstate because his window tint was illegal, his license plate was improperly displayed, and he was not wearing a seat belt. During the stop, the trooper discovered that defendant did not have a driver's license and that the vehicle was not registered. After defendant gave inconsistent answers to questioned posed by the trooper, the trooper learned that defendant had been convicted of felony marijuana possession and weapons charges in Texas. The trooper requested consent to search the vehicle, but defendant refused to consent. The trooper called for a K-9 unit, and the dog alerted the trooper to the presence of marijuana in the vehicle's trunk. On review, the court held that the trooper had a valid, reasonable suspicion that a traffic violation had occurred at the inception of the stop where the license plate was partially obscured and the windows were tinted. Once defendant's behavior gave rise of a suspicion of unlawful activity, the trooper called for a canine search. Once the dog alerted on the truck of the vehicle, the trooper had probable cause to search the vehicle for contraband.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed. However, the court discovered an error patent. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(F)(1), the district court erred in sentencing defendant to serve his entire sentence without benefit of parole probation. Because defendant was eligible for either after serving the minimum sentence, the sentence was amended to provide that defendant would be eligible for parole or probation after serving five years.

Williams v. Fahrenholtz


NO. 2008-CA-0961


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008-0961 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/25/08); 990 So. 2d 99; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1046



July 25, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 2, 2008.
Reported at Williams v. Fahrenholtz, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1044 (La.App. 4 Cir., July 25, 2008)
Writ denied by Williams v. Fahrenholtz, 986 So. 2d 671, 2008 La. LEXIS 1569 (La., 2008)
Writ denied by Vallery v. Oliver L. Dow & Assocs., 992 So. 2d 1038, 2008 La. LEXIS 2430 (La., 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Fahrenholtz v. Williams, 129 S. Ct. 627, 172 L. Ed. 2d 609, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 8719 (U.S., 2008)
Related proceeding at Fahrenholtz v. Dardenne, 2009 U.S. App. LEXIS 16521 (5th Cir. La., July 27, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2008-7459, DIVISION "J-13". Honorable Nadine M. Ramsey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant candidate sought review of a judgment of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), disqualifying him as a candidate in the primary election for the office of United States House of Representatives based on violations of the Campaign Finance Disclosure Act (CFDA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1481 et seq. The trial court overruled the candidate's peremptory exception of no cause of action under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 927.


OVERVIEW: The candidate asserted that candidates for federal office were exempt from the CFDA; however, the trial court found that the candidate was governed by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18: 463(A)(2)(a). On review, the court affirmed, finding that the trial court properly found that the candidate falsely certified on his notice of candidacy that he did not owe any outstanding fines, fees, or penalties pursuant to the CFDA as provided in § 18:463(A). The CFDA did not impose substantial qualifications upon the right to hold office. Rather, the Act enforced legitimate state interests in governing campaign finance and a duty to protect the integrity of the political process as permitted under U.S. Const. art. I, § 4, cl. 1. Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 18:1274 and 18:461(A)(1), the candidate for the primary election was required to make a certification under § 18:463(A). Therefore, the objection to candidacy was properly filed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1401(A), and a false certification was ground for disqualification under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:492(A)(5). The court found sufficient evidence to establish a prima facie case of disqualification of the candidate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the disqualification. However, since the court was equally divided on the correctness of the trial court's ruling, the decree was issued as a separate per curiam opinion.

State v. Mead


No. 42,674-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,674 (La.App. 2 Cir. 07/23/08); 988 So. 2d 740; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1043



July 23, 2008, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Mead, 16 So. 3d 470, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1381 (La.App. 2 Cir., July 1, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 211,460. Honorable Leon Lewis Emanuel, III, Judge.
State v. Mead, 988 So. 2d 740, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2088 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After being convicted of public intimidation, defendant filed an appeal from a first ruling of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, holding that his life sentence without the benefit of probation or suspension of sentence was not excessive. Defendant also requested reconsideration of his sentence to a downward departure from the mandatory minimum life sentence without benefits.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court ruled that the life sentence without benefits was not excessive, defendant filed an appeal. Thereafter, the court ordered the trial court to hold a hearing addressing defendant's waiver of counsel and request for self-representation regarding his previous Johnson hearing. The trial court found that the record failed to reveal that defendant made a clear and unequivocal waiver of his right to counsel and that he was entitled to a new Johnson hearing. A new hearing was held and the trial court again determined that the life sentence was not excessive. Accordingly, the appeal from the trial court's first ruling was moot. In addition, the court held that despite its belief that defendant should not have been found guilty, in order for the court to depart downward from the mandatory minimum sentence under the Louisiana Habitual Offender Law, defendant had to establish a favorable factual basis with respect to reasons why he fell within those rare circumstances. Also, defendant had to present evidence consistent with the guidelines of State v. Johnson. Because defendant failed to do so his sentence could not be changes.


OUTCOME: The court denied the request and dismissed the appeal.

State v. Smith


NO. 2007-KA-1432


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2007-1432 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/02/08); 989 So. 2d 816; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1019



July 2, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 9, 2008.
Writ denied by State v. Smith, 2009 La. LEXIS 1866 (La., Mar. 3, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 463-518, SECTION "A". Honorable Jerome M. Winsberg, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) convicted the defendant of one count of armed robbery, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64, and on the basis of the fact that the instant conviction and his two prior convictions were crimes of violence, imposed the mandatory sentence of life imprisonment--which exceeded the statutory maximum for the charged offense--on the defendant as a third offender. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Neither the defendant's sentence nor the statute describing the sentences to be imposed for second and subsequent offenses, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, violated the Sixth Amendment of the U.S. Constitution. Apprendi specifically excluded multiple offender proceedings from its holding requiring facts that increased a criminal penalty beyond a statutory maximum to be submitted to a jury. Furthermore, it was questionable whether the issue of the right to a jury trial had been preserved for future review, as the issue was not raised at the defendant's multiple offender hearing nor prior to the hearing. No motion to quash the multiple bill was ever filed, and no mention of the issue was made in the motion to reconsider the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, multiple offender adjudication, and sentence.

Ferguson v. Sugar


NO. 2005-CA-0921 CONSOLIDATED WITH: NO. 2005-CA-0922


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-0921 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/25/08); 988 So. 2d 816; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 999



June 25, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 13, 2008.
Adhered to, On rehearing at McGrail v. Sugar, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1147 (La.App. 4 Cir., Aug. 13, 2008)
Writ denied by McGrail v. Sugar, 996 So. 2d 1118, 2008 La. LEXIS 2838 (La., Dec. 12, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NOS. 98-12110 C/W 2000-11573, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE CAROLYN GILL-JEFFERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a patient and her husband, challenged a judgment of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, that granted the exception of prescription asserted by appellees, a psychiatrist, a psychiatric center, and their insurance companies, and dismissed the medical malpractice action filed by the patient and her husband.


OVERVIEW: The patient received care from the psychiatrist, and their doctor-patient relationship ended in 1988. When the patient began treating with another psychiatrist years later, she allegedly discovered that her current mental health problems stemmed from the care she had received from her former psychiatrist. She and her husband filed suit in 1998, claiming that the psychiatrist had falsely imprisoned her and held her in isolation in the psychiatric center by inducing her parents to believe she suffered from a disorder that required prolonged hospitalization. The district court dismissed the claim against the psychiatrist, the psychiatric center, and their insurers after finding that the claims were time barred. On review, the court held that the malpractice claim was not only prescribed on its face but was also barred by the three-year peremptive period of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628. This statute set forth an absolute three-year period beyond which medical malpractice claims could not be filed, and the period could not be tolled for any reason, including fraud or willful concealment. Because the patient's claim was extinguished, the district court properly dismissed the lawsuit.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

State v. Perkins


NO. 2008-KA-0078


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2008 0078 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/25/08); 988 So. 2d 793; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1005



June 25, 2008, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH NO. 412-242, SECTION "H". Honorable Camille Buras, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Louisiana sought review of an order from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which denied its motion to reconsider sentence after granting defendant's motion to reconsider sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of crack cocaine. On January 25, 2002, the trial court adjudged defendant a four-time felony offender and sentenced him to the minimum sentence of 20 years in prison. On February 22, 2002, defendant filed a motion to reconsider sentence, which was denied. Defendant filed a motion to correct an illegal sentence, which was denied. On March 2, 2007, defendant filed a motion to reconsider sentence. The trial court granted the motion. The trial court denied the State's motion for reconsideration of sentence. On appeal, the court held that the trial court lacked jurisdiction in 2007 to modify defendant's original sentence. The court noted that while the substantive nature of defendant's sentence did not appear to be commensurate with the crime committed, the trial court was without a procedural mechanism to properly modify defendant's sentence. The trial court erred when it failed to grant the State's motion to reconsider sentence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's denial of the State's motion to reconsider sentence. The court reversed the trial court's 2007 resentencing of defendant.

 

1081 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


SEMO, Inc. v. Bd. of Comm'rs for the Atchafalaya Basin Levee Dist.


NO. 2007 CA 2571


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 2571 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/06/08); 993 So. 2d 222; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 875; 171 Oil & Gas Rep. 149



June 6, 2008, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 17th Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of Lafourche, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 83410. Honorable John E. LeBlanc, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lessee instituted a concursus proceeding in the 17th Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafourche (Louisiana), against defendants lessor and its successor, both state agencies. The lessee deposited royalties owed under its mineral lease with the lessor into the registry of the district court. The district court ordered the funds paid to the lessor's successor. The lessor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The lessor was a levee district created in 1890. In 1938, the state conveyed certain property to the lessor. The lessor sold the property but reserved mineral rights. In 1968, the Louisiana legislature created the successor, a new levee district, which overlapped the lessor's territory. In 1989, the lessor entered into a mineral lease with the lessee. In 1997, the legislature enacted La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 38:291P(3), which caused all rights and property owned by the lessor to be transferred to the successor. The court agreed with the district court that the successor district, not the lessor, was entitled to the royalties from the mineral lease. When the legislature enacted § 38:291P(3), the lessor owned a servitude consisting of the right to explore and produce minerals on the property. That servitude was clearly included in the items transferred pursuant to § 38:291P(3). The lessor's right to obtain mineral royalties attributable to the servitude was transferred with the servitude. The provisions for the creation of new levee districts in La. Const. art. VI, § 38, were not applicable to the successor, because its organization was specifically sanctioned by art. VI, § 38(A).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision ordering the royalties paid to the lessor's successor.

 

1082 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Borden


NO. 2007-KA-396


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


07-396 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/27/08); 986 So. 2d 158; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 813



May 27, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 1, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 02-6205, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE PATRICK J. MCCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant's motions to quash and to suppress evidence, the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court of Jefferson Parish, Louisiana, convicted defendant of aggravated rape of a known juvenile and indecent behavior with a known juvenile. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment at hard labor on the rape count and to seven years on the indecent behavior count, to be served consecutively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to support a guilty verdict to the charge of indecent behavior with a juvenile under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81, based merely upon the presence of an infant in the same room while he and his concubine engaged in the videotaped sexual activity. The appellate court disagreed, finding that defendant clearly touched and held his infant daughter in the course of his sexual activity with his girlfriend. The fact that they engaged in sexual activity in the presence of their infant daughter so that the child was in a position to see or sense that sexual acts were taking place formed a sufficient basis to support the conviction. The fact that defendant picked up and held the child while he continued to engage in sexual activity compelled the conclusion that he had the requisite intent to complete the offense. Since the child-victim on the rape charge, the "declarant" in the videotaped interview, testified at trial following the admission of the tape, and was subject to cross-examination, the tape's admission was not a violation of the Confrontation Clause. Defendant's life sentence was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed, and the matter was remanded to the trial court with an order that defendant be informed in writing of both his sex offender registration requirements and his notification requirements.

Roy v. Alexandria City Council


CW 2007-1322


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-1322 (La.App. 3 Cir. 05/07/08); 984 So. 2d 191; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 659



May 7, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Roy v. Alexandria City Council, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 973 (La.App. 3 Cir., June 18, 2008)
Writ dismissed by Roy v. Alexandria City Council, 2008 La. LEXIS 2045 (La., Oct. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON SUPERVISORY WRITS FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 229,053. HONORABLE HARRY FRED RANDOW, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a city mayor, brought suit against defendants, the city's council members, in the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), seeking a judgment declaring a city ordinance invalid and seeking an injunction preventing the council members from acting under the ordinance. The trial court granted a preliminary injunction. The council members made peremptory exceptions, which were denied, and the members sought review.


OVERVIEW: City of Alexandria Ordinance 231-2007 allowed the council to enter into contracts for legal services to be provided to the council. The council members argued that the city was a necessary party to the action. The court held that the city council could not sue or be sued. The council was neither a natural person nor a juridical person under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 24. However, the individual members of the council could be sued as natural persons. The injunctive relief sought by the mayor and granted by the trial court was directed to the individual council members and it restrained them from entering into an invalid contract on behalf of the city. The court found that the city was not a necessary party under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 641, because complete relief could be accorded to existing parties, and the city's interest was protected by the inclusion in the suit of representatives of its two branches of government, the mayor and council members. A dismissal would deprive the mayor of his only adequate remedy. Although La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1880 required the city to be a party, the mayor and council members were already parties.


OUTCOME: The court denied the council members' writ application.

Jackson v. Vidalia Riverfront Dev. Dist.


2007-1569


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-1569 (La.App. 3 Cir. 05/07/08); 982 So. 2d 346; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 654



May 7, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 3, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CONCORDIA, NO. 42859. HONORABLE KATHY JOHNSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hotel owner filed a petition against defendants, a town, a development district, and an authority, in the Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Concordia (Louisiana), seeking declaratory judgment and injunctive relief arising out of the levy of a hotel occupancy tax and the enactment of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4709.1, which the owner deemed unconstitutional. The trial court denied the owner relief, and the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The town's riverfront development authority adopted a resolution pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4709.1 authorizing the occupancy tax to fund a convention center. The owner contended that the tax was imposed without approval of the voters in direct violation of La. Const. art. VI, §§ 29 and 32 (1974). The court found that the owner failed to meet the burden of showing clearly and convincingly that the statute was unconstitutional. La. Const. art. VI, § 19 expressly permitted the legislature to create special districts. La. Const. art. VI, § 29 was inapplicable to the district because it was limited in application by its express language to local governmental subdivisions and school boards. The district was a special district and a political subdivision created by legislative act in accordance with La. Const. art. VI, §§ 19 and 30. The court found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4709.1 was constitutional and that the district had the authority to impose the tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

In re Medical Review Panel Proceedings of Ouder


2007 CA 1266


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 1266 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/02/08); 991 So. 2d 58; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 717



May 2, 2008, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Docket No. 2006-14423, Division "B". Honorable Elaine W. DiMiceli, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of the decision of the 22nd Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), which dismissed her medical-malpractice claims against defendants, a doctor and a medical center.


OVERVIEW: The patient appealed a judgment that sustained exceptions raising the objection of prescription and dismissed her medical malpractice claims against the doctor and the medical center. The appellate court affirmed, stating that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.47(A)(1)(e) held that the failure to pay the filing fees within the time period rendered the request for review of a malpractice claim invalid, and such an invalid request did not suspend the time within which suit must have been instituted. The operative date upon which prescription began to run in the current case was April 23, 2004. Her initial complaint was sent via a letter dated March 8, 2005. The Patient's Compensation Fund notified her attorney that filing fees had to be paid within 45 days or the complaint would not suspend the time within which suit must be instituted. The fees were not paid and the patient was advised that her case was no longer considered filed. The invalid request for review of her malpractice claim did not suspend the time within which suit must be instituted. Her second complaint filed on June 29, 2005, beyond the one-year period for filing a medical malpractice claim, was prescribed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Am. Home Assur. Co. v. La Worker's Comp. Second Injury Bd.


NUMBER 2007 CA 2105


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 2105 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/02/08); 991 So. 2d 500; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 719



May 2, 2008, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by Am. Home Assur. Co. v. LA Worker's Comp. Second Injury Bd., 2008 La. LEXIS 2975 (La., Oct. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 543,371. Honorable Curtis A. Calloway, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an employer and its insurer, challenged the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, granting a peremptory exception raising the objection of prescription on a workers' compensation reimbursement claim in favor of defendant, the Louisiana Workers' Compensation Second Injury Board (Board), as well as a judgment denying the motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: On March 8, 2000, the employee was injured during the course and scope of his employment with the employer, and the first weekly compensation benefit was paid on April 20, 2000. On June 19, 2000, a reimbursement claim was filed with the Board, which was approved on February 1, 2001. The Board awarded reimbursement for all weekly indemnity benefits actually paid and payable in excess of the first 104 weeks of payments, provided that proper proof of payment was submitted. On May 11, 2006, the insurer sought reimbursement from the Board for compensation payments made in connection with the March 8, 2000 work accident through March 30, 2006. The Board concluded that the request for compensation benefits paid from March 8, 2002 through May 16, 2005 was untimely under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1378, because the proof of payment was submitted to the Board more than one year after the payments were made and were thus prescribed at the time of the submission to the Board. The appellate court ruled that at the time proof of payment was submitted to the Board, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1378 limited reimbursement to those claims submitted within one year of the date the payment was made.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1087 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Pipeline Tech. VI, LLC v. Ristroph


2007 CA 1210


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 1210 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/02/08); 991 So. 2d 1; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 738



May 2, 2008, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Pipeline Tech. VI, LLC v. Ristroph, 992 So. 2d 1037, 2008 La. LEXIS 2414 (La., 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ristroph v. Pipeline Tech., 2009 U.S. LEXIS 1811 (U.S., Mar. 9, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 18th Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberville, State of Louisiana. Case Number 63573; Division D. The Honorable William C. Dupont, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pipeline company brought an action to expropriate a servitude across defendant landowner's property. The 18th Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberville (Louisiana), dismissed the action with prejudice but denied the landowner's claim for attorney fees and costs. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 19:201 allowed attorney fees to a landowner in an expropriation proceeding instituted by the state or a state agency where the final judgment was that the state or agency could not acquire the property in question. The landowner argued that when the state delegated to the company the authority to expropriate private property under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 19:2(8), the company became an "agent" of the state. The court disagreed, reasoning that because the types of private entities with the power to expropriate were listed separately in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 19:2 from the state and its subdivisions, the implication was that these entities were not "agents" or "agencies" of any governmental body. The landowner also argued that La. Const. art. I, § 4, which guaranteed a property owner compensation "to the full extent of his loss," guaranteed his right to attorney fee reimbursement. However, the court noted that this provision provided attorney fees only to a landowner whose property was "taken."


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1088 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Bunge N. Am., Inc. v. Bd. of Commerce & Indus.


NUMBER 2007 CA 1746 CONSOLIDATED WITH NUMBER 2007 CA 1747 AND NUMBER 2007 CW 1705


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 1746 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/02/08); 991 So. 2d 511; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 735



May 2, 2008, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Bunge N. Am., Inc. v. Bd. of Commerce & Indus., 2008 La. LEXIS 2698 (La., Nov. 21, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 509,022 c/w 510,652. Honorable Timothy E. Kelley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: JUNE 11, 2004 JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; JUNE 11, 2007 JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A parish tax assessor appealed a Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, summary judgment dismissing the assessor's suit to nullify a company's state contract. The assessor's supervisory writ application for review of the trial court's denial of his cross-motion for summary judgment was referred to the appellate court. The company appealed an interlocutory overruling of its peremptory and declinatory exceptions.


OVERVIEW: The contract granted the company a 5-year exemption under La. Const. art. VII, § 21(F) from industrial ad valorem taxes on an addition to its plant. The assessor stated a cause of action challenging the exemption because he was not estopped from maintaining the action by remaining passive until the contract was executed. The assessor stated a cause of action to direct the state to enable him to place the exempt-property list on the parish assessment rolls because a writ of mandamus was proper under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 3863 to compel the state to determine the value of the property. The assessor demonstrated sufficient interest, both in his individual and official capacities, to sustain his. The assessor's suit was timely under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2032. The constitutional question brought the action within the trial court's original jurisdiction. The assessor's allegations about the correctness of the exemption did not have to be reviewed by the state under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1989, et seq. before undergoing judicial review. The assessor failed to present competent evidence to prevent dismissal of his suit or to supports his summary judgment motion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment overruling the peremptory and declinatory exceptions, affirmed the summary judgment dismissing the assessor's suit, and denied the assessor's supervisory writ application.

 

1089 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Manuel v. State


CA 2007-1620


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2007-1620 (La.App. 3 Cir. 4/30/08); 982 So. 2d 316; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 952



April 30, 2008, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Manuel v. State, 989 So. 2d 107, 2008 La. LEXIS 1730 (La., Aug. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF EVANGELINE, NO. 68791-A. HONORABLE JOHN LARRY VIDRINE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline, Louisiana, granted judgment in favor of defendant State of Louisiana by dismissing plaintiffs', alcoholic beverages retailers, claim that bans on certain practices relating to the wholesale and retail of alcoholic beverages within Louisiana were unconstitutional violations of the Sherman Act and the Interstate Commerce Clause of the United States Constitution. The retailers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The retailers argued that the trial court erred in failing to declare the "challenged practices" unconstitutional. The appellate court found that the Commerce Clause basis for the Sherman Act ( Sherman Act), 15 U.S.C.S. § 1, was narrowed, or "qualified," by the 21st Amendment. The State had met any procedural burden to raise the 21st Amendment. All six bans were within the core of the State's power to regulate the transportation, distribution, sale, and consumption of alcoholic beverages under the 21st Amendment. By denying market incentives--the price differential across geographic areas--that would give rise to a bootleg market, Louisiana regulators avoided the creation of a bootleg market and distribution system. All of the retailers' Sherman Act claims were subject to dismissal as the bans were restraints imposed unilaterally by government and did not qualify as concerted action. No showing was made that the bas took place in or substantially affected interstate commerce. No discrimination against interstate commerce, and no discrimination in support of economic protectionism, was alleged.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1090 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


In re Successions of Gurtner


NO. 2007-CA-1065


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2007-1065 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/09/08); 982 So. 2d 952; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 549



April 9, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 13, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM ST. BERNARD 34TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NO. 103-689, DIVISION "D". Honorable Kirk A. Vaughn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sister and appellee siblings filed a petition for possession, a detailed descriptive list, affidavits of death and heirship, and a judgment of possession. The judgment of possession was rendered. The sister petitioned to nullify/amend the judgment of possession and to reopen succession. The St. Bernard 34th Judicial District Court (Louisiana) granted summary judgment in favor of the siblings. The sister appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the death of the parties' father, the parties filed a detailed descriptive list that included a credit union account. The judgment of possession placed all the heirs in possession of the property comprising the estate. In the sister's petition to nullify/amend the judgment of possession and to reopen succession, she requested that the account be excluded from the descriptive list and the judgment of possession because it allegedly was erroneously included as an asset of the estate. The appellate court determined that the district court properly found that it was not possible to reopen the succession and amend the judgment of possession under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. arts. 2004 and 3393 because (1) the case did not involve property that was overlooked or omitted from the judgment of possession, (2) "other proper cause" was not judicially recognized to remove assets from the estate, and (3) no allegation of ill practices was made. The statutory requirements of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 6:653.1(A) were not met, because the decedent did not submit an affidavit to the credit union declaring that the sister was within the mandatory degree of kinship to be recognized as a beneficiary.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the district court's judgment.

 

1091 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schneider


KA 07-943


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-943 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/02/08); 981 So. 2d 107; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 483



April 2, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Schneider, 2008 La. LEXIS 2787 (La., Dec. 12, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CONCORDIA, NO. 05-2565. HONORABLE LEO BOOTHE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Concordia (Louisiana) of dogfighting. Defendant was sentenced to serve five years at hard labor and pay a $ 2,500 fine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeal disagreed. The State presented the testimony of an animal welfare agent who physically examined the dogs, and the testimony of an expert in the field of dogfighting who reviewed photographs of the dogs. Both witnesses testified that several of the forty-three dogs found at defendant's residence had injuries indicative of illegal dogfights. Some of the injuries were old, and some were considered recent. One dog had injuries that were received during a fight that had occurred within the last month. Some dogs had signs of old injuries and scarring. The expert testified that there was no doubt in her mind that several of the dogs had been fought in illegal dogfights. Further, the State presented several items that were seized from defendant's residence that were consistent with dogfighting or training dogs to fight, including two used break sticks, two treadmills, one of which had possible blood splatter on it, a trap used to catch small animals, and voluminous dogfighting memorabilia.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1092 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


United Teachers of New Orleans v. State Bd. of Elem. & Secondary Educ.


2007 CA 0031


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 0031 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/26/08); 985 So. 2d 184; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 546



March 26, 2008, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 541,768, Division "F". Honorable Timothy E. Kelley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, sustained the defendants', State Board of Elementary and Secondary Education (BESE), the Louisiana Department of Education, the Recovery School District (RSD), and the Orleans Parish School Board (OPSB), peremptory exception pleading the objection of no cause of action and dismissing plaintiffs', teacher's union and residents, claims with prejudice. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs challenged the constitutionality of Act 35 of the First Extraordinary Session of 2005 (Act 35), which was passed by the Louisiana Legislature in the wake of Hurricanes Katrina and Rita. Plaintiffs challenged the ruling sustaining the State defendants' exception raising the objection of no cause of action. The appellate court found that Act 35 did not alter or impair the contractual rights between the union and OPSB as set forth in the collective bargaining agreements (CBAs). The RSD was not obligated to apply those CBAs in the schools it supervised and operated. Act 35 was not passed in an attempt to impact public sector labor relations, and any impact it may have had was secondary and unintentional. It constituted a legitimate exercise of the State's police power to protect the general welfare of its people. While the union may have believed that it would have continued to negotiate with OPSB or the RSD on future CBAs once the current CBAs expired, this expectation was not reasonably based on any statutory, jurisprudential, or contractual authority. The trial court did not err in denying the plaintiffs' motion for leave of court to amend the petition.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1093 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jarreau


NO. 2007-KA-1052


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2007-1052 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/26/08); 982 So. 2d 876; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 458



March 26, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 2, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 403-391, SECTION "H". Honorable Camille Buras, Judge.
State v. Jarreau, 921 So. 2d 155, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2859 (La.App. 4 Cir., Dec. 14, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which sentenced him to 10 years in prison as a third offender for simple possession of cocaine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of simple possession of cocaine. The trial court found him to be a third offender and sentenced him to life in prison. His sentence was later modified to 10 years in prison as a third offender. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court imposed an excessive sentence. The court found that under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1A(2)(b)(ii), the mandatory sentence for his third offender adjudication was life in prison. The trial court more than adequately complied with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 in giving its reasons for sentence. Although defendant was found with only cocaine residue, the trial court imposed the 10-year sentence based on his prior criminal record, which dated back to arrests as early as 1967 and continued through the 1990s, with incarceration for the last prior offense lasting until the mid 1990s. Defendant had prior convictions for possession of an unregistered firearm and second-degree battery. The trial court gave adequate reasons for the sentence, and a comparison of sentences of similar crimes did not show that the 10-year sentence was disproportionate to the crime and defendant's criminal history.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

City of Hammond v. Parish of Tangipahoa


2007 CA 0574


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 0574 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/26/08); 985 So. 2d 171; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 537



March 26, 2008, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 21st Judicial District Court, Parish of Tangipahoa, Louisiana. Docket No. 2006-0003196, Division "D". Honorable M. Douglas Hughes, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: JUNE 6, 2007 MOTION TO SUPPLEMENT THE RECORD IS DENIED. OCTOBER 22, 2007 MOTION TO SUPPLEMENT THE RECORD IS GRANTED. PORTION OF JUDGMENT DENYING DECLARATORY AND INJUNCTIVE RELIEF IS AFFIRMED. PORTIONS OF JUDGMENT ORDERING SPECIFIC ACTIONS TO BE TAKEN BY THE PARISH COUNCIL AND GRANTING A WRIT OF MANDAMUS ARE REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, developers and a parish, challenged a decision of the 21st Judicial District Court, Parish of Tangipahoa (Louisiana), which ruled in favor of appellee city, ordered the developers to present plans at a public hearing before a parish council, denied injunctive relief, denied declaratory judgment, and entered mandamus relief ordering the council to review and revise its ordinances. Motions to supplement the record were before the court.


OVERVIEW: This case involved a 300-unit apartment complex planned by the developers for construction in an unincorporated area of the parish. The city opposed the development and ultimately the matter went to court. The trial court ordered the developers to obtain approval from the council rather than the planning commission and ordered the parish to review and revise ordinances. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part on appeal. Because Tangipahoa Parish Ordinance Number 07-59 did not actually cure any of the perceived problems raised by the city in this litigation, its passage did not moot this controversy. The planning commission had authority to approve or disapprove subdivision projects, and according to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:101.1, the act of approving or disapproving a subdivision plat was statutorily recognized and defined as a legislative function. Thus, a writ of mandamus under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. arts. 3862, 3863, should not have been issued to compel the parish, the parish council, and/or the planning commission to promulgate new or revised ordinances and procedures affecting the approval process for subdivision projects, which was a purely legislative function.


OUTCOME: The court denied one motion to supplement the record, but granted the other one. The court affirmed the judgment insofar as it declined to enter declaratory judgment and denied injunctive relief. The court reversed the judgment insofar as it (1) ordered the developers to submit plans to the council, (2) ordered the council to hold a public hearing, and (3) issued mandamus relief and the related orders.

 

1095 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dunbar


NO. 2006-KA-1030


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2006-1030 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/19/08); 981 So. 2d 51; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 466



March 19, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Dunbar v. Louisiana, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 28090 (E.D. La., Feb. 15, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 456-998, SECTION "F". Honorable Dennis J. Waldron, Judge.
State v. Dunbar, 978 So. 2d 899, 2008 La. LEXIS 410 (La., 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, which convicted him of unauthorized use of a motor vehicle and sentenced him to 12 years of imprisonment. The case was on remand from the Louisiana Supreme Court for the consideration of two pretermitted issues.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence. The appellate court pretermitted two assignments of error. The supreme court then remanded the case for consideration of these alleged errors. In affirming the conviction and sentence, the appellate court held that there was no error in the denial of defendant's motion to quash the habitual offender bill of information. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 did not unconstitutionally allow sentencing enhancements without a jury determination. The ruling in Apprendi made an exception for prior convictions. Next, the 12-year sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive under La. Const. art. I, § 20. Due to the fact that defendant was adjudicated a third-felony habitual offender, he was subject to a maximum sentence of 20 years. The trial judge here gave three pages of reason for his sentence; defendant was driving without headlights, drove away at a high rate of speed, he had another conviction involving a vehicle, and he lied while testifying. Based on defendant's age, his criminal history, the circumstances of the offense, and the factors under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1, the sentence was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

State v. Gauthier


NO. 2007-KA-0743


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2007-0743 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/12/08); 978 So. 2d 1161; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 361



March 12, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 20, 2008.
Rehearing denied by State v. Gauthier, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 596 (La.App. 4 Cir., Apr. 9, 2008)
Writ denied by State v. Gauthier, 2008 La. LEXIS 2853 (La., Dec. 19, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 439-741, SECTION "H". Honorable Camille Buras, Judge.
State v. Gauthier, 941 So. 2d 642, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2634 (La.App. 4 Cir., Sept. 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of simple battery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34 and intimidation of a witness in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:129.1. The State then filed a multiple bill charging defendant as a second offender. The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana) vacated the original sentence and resentenced defendant. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in connection with his assault on his girlfriend. The trial court ultimately found that defendant was a second offender. The court affirmed on appeal. The court found no patent error regarding the competency of defendant at the time of his multiple billing. There was a competency hearing prior to trial and the trial court determined that defendant was competent, he was found competent to represent himself, there was no objection by counsel as to any failure to find him competent to proceed with the multiple offender proceeding, and appellate counsel did not raise this issue, and thus defendant did not show any prejudice. Furthermore, the court had already affirmed findings of defendant's competency in this case and there was no indication that defendant's condition deteriorated post-trial and prior to his multiple billing. The trial court imposed a term of seven and one-half years following defendant's adjudication as a second offender and the maximum the trial court could have imposed was 10 years and the minimum was two and one-half years under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:129.1, 15:529.1. The sentence was not excessive under La. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1097 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Arabie


NO. 07-KA-806


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


07-806 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/11/08); 982 So. 2d 136; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 376



March 11, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 9, 2008.
Writ denied by State v. Arabie, 2008 La. LEXIS 2676 (La., Nov. 21, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 06-3972, DIVISION "B". HONORABLE CORNELIUS E. REGAN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Jefferson Parish, Division "B" (Louisiana), found defendant guilty of aggravated rape and two counts of aggravated incest of a juvenile under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:42, 14:78.1. He was sentenced to life in prison for the rape and 25 years on each incest count. The sentences were ordered to run concurrently and without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to prove that an aggravated rape occurred. He contended there was no evidence of penetration and maintained the evidence only showed that he licked the victim and touched her, which was insufficient to show penetration. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:42(A)(4) and 14:41(A) and (C), the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of aggravated rape because (1) oral sexual intercourse did not require penetration; and (2) the victim's testimony alone was sufficient to establish the elements of a sexual offense. A life sentence for aggravated rape was mandated by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42(D)(2)(b) unless the State decided to seek the death penalty under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42(D)(2)(a). Defendant did not urge a downward deviation at the time of sentencing. In his motion to reconsider, he simply asserted his sentence was unconstitutionally excessive. At no time did defendant argue or present any evidence showing any exceptional circumstances to justify a downward departure from the mandatory life sentence. Thus, he failed to carry his burden of proof that his life sentence for aggravated rape was unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment, but remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to provide written notification of the general sex offender and child predator registration requirements to defendant, to determine his ability to pay the victim's reasonable costs of counseling that result from the offense based on his financial resources and future ability to pay, and to correct the commitment.

3525 N. Causeway Blvd. Corp. v. Penney


NO. 07-CA-883


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


07-883 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/11/08); 982 So. 2d 195; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 387



March 11, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 9, 2008.
Writ denied by 3525 N. Causeway Blvd. Corp. v. Penny, 983 So. 2d 905, 2008 La. LEXIS 1292 (La., May 30, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 637-299, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant tax debtor sought review of an order from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which awarded summary judgment to plaintiff purchaser in an action to confirm a tax sale.


OVERVIEW: The parish gave notice to the tax debtor of its intent to sell her property at a tax sale for unpaid taxes. The property was sold. The purchaser of the property brought an action to confirm the tax sale. The tax debtor answered the petition, and filed a reconventional demand to annul the tax sale. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court rendered summary judgment in favor of the purchaser, confirming the tax sale. On appeal, the court found that the tax debtor did not meet her burden of proving that the tax sale was invalid for failure to notify the mortgage holder. There was no proof that the mortgage holder requested notice, as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2180.1(A), and the mortgage holder was not a party to the suit. Further, the notice given was sufficient to meet due process requirements. The sheriff sent a certified letter to the tax debtor, at the correct address. The sheriff's office received the return receipt back from the post office. Although the notice misspelled the tax debtor's name, the return receipt's signature contained the correct spelling.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


 

1099 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ayche


NO. 07-KA-753


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


07-753 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/11/08); 978 So. 2d 1143; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 381



March 11, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Ayche, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 592 (La.App. 5 Cir., Apr. 14, 2008)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Ayche v. State, 999 So. 2d 1140, 2009 La. LEXIS 1171 (La., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 04-6318, DIVISION "J". HONORABLE STEPHEN J. WINDHORST, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Jefferson Parish, Division "J" (Louisiana), found defendant guilty of possession of cocaine under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(C). After a hearing, the trial court found that defendant was a fourth felony offender. The trial court then vacated the original sentence and sentenced him to 30 years' imprisonment at hard labor without the benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Testimony was presented that after experienced detectives received narcotics complaints defendant was observed in a high-crime, high-drug area in what appeared to be a hand-to-hand narcotics transaction. Upon the approach of the detectives, who were wearing clothing that identified themselves as officers, defendant fled. The experienced officers' observation of an apparent drug deal in a high drug crime area followed by defendant's flight upon the approach of two police officers gave the officers the requisite reasonable suspicion to pursue and detain him under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 215.1 and the Fourth Amendment. Also, the discarded bags of narcotics were properly seized as abandoned property. Thus, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress the evidence under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 703(D). Further, the trial court noted the pattern of cocaine possession and believed that defendant deserved a stiff sentence. Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant to 30 years' imprisonment given defendant's criminal history and the sentence was not excessive under the Eighth Amendment or La. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, but remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to amend the minutes and commitments to correct discrepancies and to send defendant written notice of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief applications.

Forbes v. Cockerham


2005 CA 1838 CONSOLIDATED WITH 2005 CA 1839


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 1838 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/07/08); 985 So. 2d 86; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 321



March 7, 2008, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by Forbes v. Cockerham, 2008 La. LEXIS 1823 (La., Sept. 19, 2008)
Writ granted by Forbes v. Cockerham, 2008 La. LEXIS 1840 (La., Sept. 19, 2008)
Reversed by Forbes v. Cockerham, 2009 La. LEXIS 18 (La., Jan. 21, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 415,247 c/w 415,255. Honorable Timothy E. Kelley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT NOTWITHSTANDING THE VERDICT REVERSED ALTERNATE JUDGMENT GRANTING NEW TRIAL REVERSED JUDGMENT RENDERED ON JURY VERDICT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for damages arising from an automobile accident that occurred on the highway, plaintiff injured passenger appealed a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, granting a judgment notwithstanding the verdict (JNOV) or in the alternate a new trial for defendant, the Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development (DOTD), and absolving DOTD from liability for the accident.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was a nine-year-old passenger in a vehicle that struck a patched area of the roadway, skidded off the highway into a ditch, rolled over to its side, and then struck a number of trees growing near the back of the ditch. Plaintiff sued the DOTD for negligence, alleging failure to properly maintain the road and that the road failed to comply with applicable design standards; as a result, the roadway, shoulders, and recovery zone were allegedly deficient. The jury returned a verdict finding the driver 60% at fault and DOTD 40% at fault. The trial court erred by granting a JNOV for DOTD and amending the judgment to reflect a finding that DOTD was 0% at fault. The Court of Appeal of Louisiana reinstated the jury's verdict. There was conflicting testimony concerning the driver's consumption of alcohol before the accident. However, this did not absolve the DOTD from fault. The presence of a tree 10.52 feet from the edge of the roadway was a significant contributing factor to the collision and plaintiff's injuries. The jury did not abuse its discretion by awarding plaintiff $ 12,650,234.00 in damages. There was no error in the jury instructions.


OUTCOME: The JNOV was reversed. The alternative judgment granting a new trial was reversed, and the judgment rendered on the jury verdict for plaintiff was reinstated.

Fountain v. Lavigne


NO. 2007-CA-0716


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2007-0716 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/05/08); 980 So. 2d 136; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 325



March 5, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 8, 2008.
Writ denied by Fountain v. Lavigne, 983 So. 2d 902, 2008 La. LEXIS 1308 (La., May 30, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM FIRST CITY COURT OF NEW ORLEANS. NO. 06-50740, SECTION "C". HONORABLE SONJA M. SPEARS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of an order from the City Court of New Orleans (Louisiana), which granted defendant insurer's peremptory exception of prescription in a negligence action against the insurer and defendant insured.


OVERVIEW: On February 17, 2005, plaintiff was operating a vehicle when a vehicle driven by the insured collided with her. On April 6, 2005, the insurer made a payment to plaintiff for her property damage sustained in the collision. On April 6, 2006, plaintiff fax-filed a suit against defendants to recover for the injuries and damages caused by the collision. The insurer filed a peremptory exception of prescription. The trial court granted the exception. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred in not applying the Mallett rationale to the case. The insurer's unconditional payment of the property damage claim was an acknowledgement under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3464 sufficient to interrupt prescription. No circumstances existed warranting departure from the general rule of retroactivity of judicial decisions. The court could find no compelling reason based upon the history, purposes, effect, and operation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:661 to depart from the general rule of retroactivity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Savoie

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-914 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/05/08); 982 So. 2d 119; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 299



March 5, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 25, 2008.
Writ denied by State v. Savoie, 992 So. 2d 1011, 2008 La. LEXIS 1947 (La., 2008)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Savoie v. Cain, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 187451 (W.D. La., Dec. 3, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 105492. HONORABLE GLENNON P. EVERETT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted with aggravated rape in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42. He was convicted in the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of LaFayette (Louisiana) of attempted aggravated rape. Defendant filed a pro se motion for an out-of-time appeal, which was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in the attempted aggravated rape of an elderly woman. The court affirmed on appeal. Because defendant did not have the right to counsel at a certain pretrial hearing, it was unnecessary to further consider whether defendant was represented, and if not, whether he waived the right to representation. Ann. art. 841(A), defendant did not object to the admission of crime laboratory reports and thus failed to preserve his right to challenge the evidence post-verdict. Defendant did not raise a speedy trial issue at any time prior to the appeal, and this was rendered moot upon conviction. There were no errors patent found.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Stevens


07-976


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-976 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/05/08); 978 So. 2d 535; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 317



March 5, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 25, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF IBERIA, DOCKET NO. 06-1933. HONORABLE GERARD B. WATTIGNY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 16th Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia (Louisiana), convicting him of felony communication of false information of planned arson in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:54.1 and misdemeanor aggravated assault in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:37, and sentencing him to eight years at hard labor and six months in the parish jail, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for threatening to set the victim's home on fire after a fight with his girlfriend. On appeal, the court held that there was a misjoinder of offenses in the bill of information under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 493 because defendant was entitled to a jury trial for the felony charge and was not entitled to a jury trial on the misdemeanor charge; however, because defendant failed to file a motion to quash the bill of information, he waived any objection to the error. The court severed the misdemeanor conviction from the appeal and ordered defendant to file a writ of review regarding that conviction. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's felony conviction because: (1) defendant's statement to a deputy that he did not mean what he said to the victim and his girlfriend clearly indicated that he knowingly made a false statement; (2) the jury was entitled to conclude that a reasonable person hearing defendant's threat to trap the occupants in the home and burn the home down would have taken the threat seriously; and (3) La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:54.1 did not require that the offense occurred in a public setting.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

K.A.E.M. v. J.M.C.


CW07-1279


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-1279 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/05/08); 979 So. 2d 613; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 294



March 5, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
WRIT APPLICATION FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 2005-3245, DIVISION C. HONORABLE GUY ERNEST BRADBERRY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED; STAY RECALLED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent alleged biological father filed a rule for custody. Relator mother filed exceptions to the rule for custody and a motion to declare null or dissolve a restraining order. The Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, Division C, Louisiana, ruled that the matter could proceed as an ordinary custody proceeding and denied the exceptions. The mother sought supervisory writs from the court. The court stayed all proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that an acknowledgment of paternity signed in Oklahoma was valid and that the alleged father had timely brought his action to establish paternity. The mother alleged that the acknowledgment of paternity signed in Oklahoma was invalid and that the trial court erred in refusing to retroactively apply the amendments to La. Civ. The alleged father filed his petition for custody within the two-year period under the old law and five days before the new law became effective. He acknowledged paternity in writing and lived with the child and the mother for three years. The court found that the Oklahoma acknowledgment was valid. The retroactive application of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 198 would have unconstitutionally stripped the alleged father of a vested right to establish paternity under the circumstances of the case.


OUTCOME: The writ application was denied. The ruling of the trial court was affirmed. The stay order was recalled such that the matter could proceed as an ordinary custody proceeding in the trial court.

Delta Chem. Corp. v. Lynch


NO. 2007-CA-0431


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2007-0431 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/27/08) 979 So. 2d 579; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 333



February 27, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 1, 2008.
Writ denied by Delta Chem. Corp. v. Lynch, 983 So. 2d 904, 2008 La. LEXIS 1290 (La., May 30, 2008)
Writ denied by Delta Chem. Corp. v. Lynch, 983 So. 2d 898, 2008 La. LEXIS 1312 (La., May 30, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2001-19425, DIVISION "I-14". Honorable Piper D. Griffin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation filed a defamation suit against appellees, the Louisiana State Inspector General (IG), among others, based on reports prepared and published by the IG regarding the corporation's attempt to obtain a brand name contract. The denial of the State's special motion to strike was reversed. On remand, the Civil District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, awarded the IG attorney's fees and costs. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the corporation raised several issues challenging the award of attorney fees. The appellate court found that the corporation was given an opportunity to refute the IG's findings of fact and opinions in the draft report before the final report was published on the IG's website. Although the IG may have arrived at some derogatory opinions, the facts on which those opinions were based were not defamatory; they simply were the facts as discovered by his office. The appellate court found no evidence of malice, actual or implied, on the part of the IG. Thus, there was no reason not to apply the law of the case doctrine. Further, La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 971B mandated an award of reasonable attorney fees and costs. The appellate court was allowed, and even required, to determine if the amount awarded was reasonable, thereby considering whether "mitigating factors" were applicable. The IG could recover only those fees associated with the motion to strike. The appellate court found the award was excessive, and the evidence submitted by the IG supporting the attorney's fees and costs was completely inadequate.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the matter was remanded to the trial court for a determination of attorney's fees.

State v. Scallion


07-966


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-966 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/20/08); 976 So. 2d 822; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 213



February 20, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 31, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE TENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF NATCHITOCHES, NO. C10142-2. HONORABLE DEE A. HAWTHORNE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION REVERSED AND SET ASIDE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After her motion to suppress evidence was denied, defendant pleaded guilty in the Tenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Natchitoches (Louisiana) to possession of oxycodone. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to grant her motion to suppress evidence because there were no exigent circumstances justifying the warrantless entry into the home. The court of appeal agreed. The officers could not see into the residence because of the texture of the glass. The officers could only see the forms of individuals moving back and forth in what was described as panicked movements. Based on the totality of the actual information available to them at that time, law enforcement officers could not reasonably have concluded that the reason for the movement was the destruction of evidence or arming of the occupants. Because the officers lacked probable cause to believe that the destruction of evidence was imminent, or their safety was at risk, there were no exigent circumstances that justified the forced entry into the residence. Any evidence discovered by law enforcement as a result of the warrantless entry, therefore, could not be considered in determining whether there was probable cause for a search warrant to be issued and could not be admitted into evidence under the plain view doctrine.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed and set aside.
