State v. Fuller


NO. 07-KA-319


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


07-319 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/19/08); 980 So. 2d 45; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 228



February 19, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 9, 2008.
Writ denied by State v. Fuller, 2008 La. LEXIS 2075 (La., Oct. 10, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 05-3763, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE PATRICK J. MCCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) of armed robbery with a gun, adjudicated a second-felony offender, and sentenced to 198 years and five years, both without benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the State failed to prove his identity as the offender beyond a reasonable doubt. The court of appeal disagreed. The State offered the testimony of the store clerk and a detective. The clerk testified that he had three opportunities prior to the robbery to view the perpetrator in the well-lit store. On each of those occasions, the robber stood directly in front of the clerk and a brief conversation took place. The clerk stated that the perpetrator did not have anything covering his face and was not wearing sunglasses or a hat. After the robbery, the clerk was was able to give a detailed description of the perpetrator and told the investigating officer he got a good look at the robber. Four days later, the clerk was shown a photographic lineup and immediately positively identified defendant as the perpetrator. He also identified defendant in court as the person who robbed him. The detective testified that after defendant confessed to the robbery, he prepared a photographic lineup with the defendant's picture and showed it to the clerk. The detective stated that the clerk, without hesitation, identified defendant as the robber.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by Ramos v. State, 2013 La. App. LEXIS 646 (La.App. 3 Cir., Apr. 3, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-FIFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF GRANT, NO. 6242. HONORABLE W. PEYTON CUNNINGHAM, JR., JUDGE PRO TEMPORE.
Ramos v. State, DOTD, 1990 La. App. LEXIS 628 (La.App. 3 Cir., Mar. 14, 1990)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant swimmer challenged a judgment of the 35th Judicial District Court, Parish of Grant (Louisiana), granting appellee Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development (DOTD) summary judgment under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 966 in the swimmer's premises liability action.


OVERVIEW: The swimmer was injured when he fell from a rope swing at a swimming hole, rendering him a quadriplegic. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred by granting the DOTD summary judgment because it was not entitled to recreational use immunity under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 9:2791, 9:2795 (1986), as the statutes were inapplicable to public lands and did not grant immunity to the state, its agencies, or subdivisions, because the statutes were silent as to governmental immunity. Questions also existed as to whether the DOTD's inspections of its rights-of-way should have including the swimming area and revealed any potential defects, including the rope swing positioned over shallow water.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting the DOTD summary judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

Hebert v. La. Licensed Prof'l Voc. Rehab. Counselors


07-610


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-610 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/23/08); 974 So. 2d 824; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 46



January 23, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 3, 2008.
Reversed by, Vacated by Hebert v. La. Licensed Prof'l Voc. Rehab. Counselors Bd. of Examiners, 981 So. 2d 21, 2008 La. LEXIS 1100 (La., May 9, 2008)
Vacated by, Remanded by Hebert v. La. Licensed Prof'l Voc. Rehab. Counselors Bd. of Exam'rs, 981 So. 2d 21, 2008 La. LEXIS 1099 (La., May 9, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, DOCKET NO. 20064643. HONORABLE BYRON HEBERT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette, Louisiana, granted appellee rehabilitation expert's motion to strike under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 971 and dismissed appellant vocational rehabilitation counselor's claims for mandamus and damages against the expert and appellee Louisiana Licensed Professional Vocational Rehabilitation Counselors Board of Examiners. The counselor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the legislature did not enact La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 971 to bar parties seeking redress for violations of their First Amendment rights by the State, and others acting in concert with the State, from filing legitimate civil rights suits. The counselor's complaint attacked the Board's authority on the behest of the expert and under color of state law to sanction him for commenting on the substandard quality of the expert's services. By imposing sanctions under La. Admin. Code tit. 46, § LXXXVI.1604, Canon 4(A)(7), the Board not only impeded the free flow of information but imposed a code of silence among professional counselors to the detriment of injured employees. The Board's sweeping ban which covered all speech which the Board may define as "disparaging" was not narrowly tailored to avoid unnecessarily circumscribing protected expression. It did not serve a compelling state interest. The counselor's petition contained facts sufficient to show he may be successful in asserting a claim against the expert and the Board for violating his First Amendment right. The counselor had to amend his pleadings to particularize his claims.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing the counselor's claims against the expert was reversed and remanded to allow the counselor to amend his pleadings; the judgment dismissing the Board on an exception of venue was reversed.

State v. Kennedy


Nos. 42,850-KA, 42,851-KA Consolidated Cases


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,850 (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/09/08); 974 So. 2d 203; 2008 La. App. LEXIS 24



January 9, 2008, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 133130 and 133134. Honorable John M. Robinson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On guilty pleas, defendant was convicted in the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier (Louisiana) of attempted aggravated rape and attempted aggravated incest. He was sentenced to 35 years in prison at hard labor and 10 years in prison at hard labor, respectively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised various issues, but the court affirmed. It was clear from the recitation of the facts presented by the State that defendant was admitting to conduct that was adequate to support the convictions. The State's recitation of facts was more properly categorized as imprecise than inadequate, and the conduct admitted to by defendant supported the convictions, although the facts were not accurate as to the victim named in the bill of information that initiated the proceeding in which the plea was obtained. Nothing established a lack of awareness as to the nature of the offense. At best, the record established that the trial court failed to inform defendant of the nature of the charges in violation of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 556.1 and that the trial court failed to inquire into whether counsel explained the offenses to him. The court could not conclude that noncompliance with Article 556.1 warranted setting aside the plea. By not filing a motion for reconsideration of sentence under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1(A)(2), defendant was limited to review on the question of excessiveness under La. Const. art. I, § 20. Defendant's sentences were not excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1112 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


NO. 2007-KA-0533


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2007-0533 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/28/07); 975 So. 2d 73; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2412



December 28, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 28, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 445-293, SECTION "J". Honorable Darryl A. Derbigny, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of possession of cocaine, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967. Defendant was sentenced. At a multiple bill hearing, defendant was adjudicated a fourth felony offender. The Criminal District Court Orleans Parish, Louisiana, set aside defendant's original sentence and sentenced defendant to twenty years at hard labor without benefit of probation or parole, with credit for time served. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the trial court erred when it imposed the sentence to be served without benefit of parole because La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:967, 15:529.1 did not prohibit parole eligibility. The court did not need to take action to correct the trial court's failure to specify that defendant's sentence be served without benefit of suspension of sentence because the correction was statutorily effected. Defendant argued that the trial court should have granted his motion for mistrial when an officer testified that he found a zip-lock bag of green vegetable matter during the search incident to arrest. The trial court did not err when it denied defendant's request for a mistrial, under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 771, because the discovery of the marijuana was part of the res gestae, and the officer's testimony was used to establish the facts leading up to, and including, defendant's arrest. The sentence was not excessive because defendant was adjudicated a fourth felony offender, he was sentenced to the minimum sentence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(c)(i), and defendant did not produce any evidence to rebut the presumption of constitutionality.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Pearson


NO. 07-KA-332 C/W 07-KA-333 & 07-KA-539


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


07-332 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/27/07); 975 So. 2d 646; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2346



December 27, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 4, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 05-5424, DIVISION "N". HONORABLE HANS J. LILJEBERG, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES VACATED AND REMANDED (McGowan and Pearson). SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED (Little).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, convicting them of looting during a declared state of emergency in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.5(C) and sentencing them to 15 years at hard labor without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted for taking beer and wine from a grocery store in the aftermath of Hurricane Katrina. On appeal the court held that § 14:62.5(C) did not violate the constitutional doctrine of separation of powers because the governor's ability to declare a state of emergency as referenced in § 14:62.5(C) had a clearly stated legislative policy in the Louisiana Homeland Security and Emergency Assistance and Disaster Act (HSEDA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 29:721 et seq., and the standards and limits surrounding the governor and parish president's ability to declare a state of emergency in accordance with the legislative will was sufficiently set forth in the HSEDA. One defendant's sentence was vacated because the trial court did not rule on her motion for post-verdict judgment of acquittal before sentencing as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 821. The court held that defendants' maximum 15-year sentences were excessive because they were not the most egregious offenders of the crime of looting, as all defendants were first-time offenders, two were employed at the time of trial, and they did not attempt to run from the police officer and were compliant with his requests.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions were affirmed, but their sentences were vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing.

 

1114 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Carter v. Honorable Judges


07-823


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-823 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/19/07); 972 So. 2d 457; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2279



December 19, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 22, 2008.
Writ denied by Carter v. Honorable Judges, 976 So. 2d 703, 2008 La. LEXIS 482 (La., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 2006-5029. HONORABLE TED R. BROYLES, DISTRICT JUDGE AD HOC.
Carter v. Jones, 967 So. 2d 615, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1907 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judge sought a judgment declaring that attorney fees for which he sought payment were incurred by him in his official capacity as a judge and ordering the judges of the court to pay those attorney fees from the judicial expense fund. The Fourteenth Judicial District Court of Calcasieu Parish, Louisiana, denied the judge's request. The judge appealed and sought mandamus relief.


OVERVIEW: On review, the judge raised several issued challenged the denial of his requested relief on grounds that he was not entitled to recover attorney fees because La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5108.1, which provided for the indemnification of public officials for their actions, contemplated that the public official seeking indemnification was sued, not filing suit, and because he did not prevail in the proceedings for which he sought attorney fees. The appellate court found that pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:996.10, the payment of expenses of the court and/or the judges was permissive, as it provided that the judicial expense fund "may be used" for any purpose or purposes connected with, incidental to or related to the proper administration or function of the said court or the offices of the individual judges. Therefore, the judges did not have a legally-imposed duty to pay the judge's attorney fees, and he was not entitled to mandamus relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1115 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Boyte


No. 42,763-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,763 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/19/07); 973 So. 2d 900; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2273



December 19, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Boyte, 2008 La. LEXIS 1434 (La., June 20, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 03-F1340. Honorable C. Wendell Manning, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana) of malfeasance in office in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:134. He was sentenced to five years imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the public works director and was in charge of maintenance and operations of roads. He was convicted of malfeasance of office and the court affirmed. The State carried its burden in connection with defendant's conviction under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:134, given that (1) defendant had no authority to order one to exert his labor and use office equipment to perform tree trimming services on private property, and this act was plainly a violation of defendant's duty not to misuse public employees and property for purposes of La. Defendant served for years as the public works director and fell within the ambit of § 42:1461 and the State's proof of defendant's duties was sufficient. OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1116 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. C.D.


07-1001


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-1001 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/05/07); 971 So. 2d 496; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2216



December 5, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 8, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CONCORDIA, NO. 06-085J. HONORABLE LEO BOOTHE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: ADJUDICATION VACATED AND MATTER REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a juvenile delinquency case, the Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Concordia (Louisiana), adjudicated defendant juvenile a delinquent child pursuant to an adjudication hearing on the offense of oral sexual battery. At the dispositional hearing, the trial court committed defendant to the custody of the Louisiana Department of Public Safety and Corrections, Office of Youth Development, for a period of four years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim stated that defendant placed his sexual organ in her mouth. There was no indication in the record that defendant had notice that the uncertified medical records of another victim from a separate case were going to be introduced. Thus, defendant had no responsibility to subpoena the doctor who treated that victim. Also, the doctor did not live in Louisiana and refused to honor her subpoena and testify. Neither the State nor defendant could enforce an apparent out-of-state subpoena. Based on those facts, defendant's statutory and constitutional rights to confrontation were violated. Thus, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:3714(A), the trial court erred by allowing the medical records to be admitted into evidence. Furthermore, the error was not harmless because the medical records provided the only physical evidence in a case contingent upon credibility, and the trial court specifically relied on those medical records in its oral reasons for judgment. Finally, pursuant to La. Code Evid. Ann. arts. 803(4), (6), and 804(A), (B)(5), the medical records were not admissible under the medical treatment, business records, or initial complaint exceptions to the hearsay rule.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and vacated the trial court's delinquency adjudication and disposition in the juvenile case and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Hall


No. 42,767-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,767 (La.App. 2 Cir. 11/21/07); 969 So. 2d 827; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2105



November 21, 2007, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 223,516. Honorable Ramona L. Emanuel, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, adjudicating him a fourth felony offender and sentencing him to the statutory minimum of 20 years at hard labor without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in a bench trial of unauthorized entry of a place of business, adjudicated a fourth felony habitual offender and sentenced to eight years at hard labor, without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. The sentence was reversed and remanded. On remand, the trial court held a hearing at which defendant and his counsel were present for resentencing. The appellate court ruled that there was no abuse of discretion in the trial court's decision not to order a presentence investigation, especially when none was requested, and there was no reason why the trial court should have taken evidence that defendant's many offenses were non-violent property crimes. The trial court in no way prohibited defendant from making any argument in favor of a downward departure and gave no indication that the trial court would not have allowed evidence to be presented in favor of any such argument. Also, the only factor argued by defendant, aside perhaps from his age, was the non-violent nature of his prior crimes, a factor that prior precedent rejected as a sole basis for rebutting the presumption of constitutionality necessary for departing from the minimum sentence.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, a criminal court clerk and state officials, filed exceptions of no cause of action, and the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, granted appellees' exceptions resulting in the dismissal of appellant candidate's claim. The candidate appealed.

State v. Calloway


2007 KA 0012


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 0012 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/07/07); 978 So. 2d 374; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2071



November 7, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at State v. Calloway, 984 So. 2d 709, 2008 La. LEXIS 1153 (La., 2008)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Calloway, 2009 La. LEXIS 13 (La., Jan. 21, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 32nd Judicial District Court In and For the Parish of Terrebonne. Trial Court No. 463,064. Honorable John R. Walker, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the 32nd Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana), which convicted her of the illegal possession of stolen things having a value greater than $500, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:69. She was sentenced to three years imprisonment at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, along with her son, was charged with illegal possession of stolen things having a value greater than $ 500. A jury found the son not guilty and defendant guilty. She was sentenced to three years imprisonment at hard labor. The appellate court reversed defendant's conviction and sentence, stating that a rational trier of fact could not have concluded that the evidence as admitted excluded a reasonable hypothesis that defendant had no knowledge that the vehicles she purchased after Hurricane Katrina were stolen. While defendant did pay a reduced price for the vehicles, uncontroverted trial testimony established that at the time of purchase, both vehicles had damage that would have lowered their prices, including water damage to one of the vehicles. The evidence further suggested that the disparity between the estimated value of the vehicles when defendant first saw them (already damaged) right around the time of the hurricane and the price she paid for them was not so great that it should have been readily apparent to an unsophisticated buyer such as herself. Defendant also testified that when she purchased the vehicles, it never crossed her mind that they were stolen.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the conviction and sentence.

 

1120 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Wong v. Hoffman


NO. 2005-CA-1483


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-1483 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/07/07); 973 So. 2d 4; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2151



November 7, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 10, 2008.
Writ denied by Wong v. Hoffman, 976 So. 2d 724, 2008 La. LEXIS 293 (La., Feb. 1, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2003-1728, DIVISION "A-5". Honorable Carolyn Gill-Jefferson, Judge.
Curole v. Curole, 848 So. 2d 591, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2149 (La.App. 5 Cir., June 26, 2002)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a client, sued defendants, her attorneys, their law firm, and their liability insurer, alleging four specific instances of legal malpractice. The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), dismissed the legal malpractice claims on the basis of peremption, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 9:5606, and granted summary judgment in favor of defendant, upholding the constitutionality of § 9:5605. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court agreed with plaintiff that the trial court erred by dismissing her petition as perempted. The petition was filed within a year of the third and fourth alleged incidents of malpractice, and, on the face of the petition, those claims were timely filed within the terms of the statute. Moreover, the trial court's reliance upon the continuing representation principle to support the dismissal of those claims was legal error. Each separate act of malpractice had to be considered to be a separate cause of action with its own one-year and three-year peremptive period. Having thus determined that two claims were not perempted from the face of the petition, the court next decided if the trial court erred by dismissing her other two claims that occurred more than one but less than three years prior to the date she filed suit. As to both claims, the court found that plaintiff could not have reasonably been expected to have known at the time of the incidents that malpractice had occurred. Plaintiff's suit, which was filed within a year of her consultation with the new attorney and within three years of the incidents, was timely with respect to her other two claims.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment granting the exception of peremption and dismissing plaintiff's suit, and the court remanded the matter to that court for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

Harrison v. Minardi


07-514


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-514 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/31/07); 968 So. 2d 1221; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1979



October 31, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF EVANGELINE, NO. 68,579. HONORABLE THOMAS F. FUSELIER, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of an order from the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana), which dismissed his medical malpractice claims against defendant physician for failure to post a cash or surety bond as provided in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.47(I)(2)(c).

Ann. § 40:1299.47(I)(2)(c) that the plaintiff in a medical malpractice suit post a cash or surety bond. The patient's attorney alleged that the patient was indigent and unable to post a cash or surety bond. The trial court granted the patient 30 days to post a cash or surety bond and stated that the patient's failure to comply with the order would result in dismissal of his claims against the physician. 1122 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Colton


07-252


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-252 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/31/07); 968 So. 2d 1239; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1995



October 31, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Colton, 2008 La. LEXIS 992 (La., Apr. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SIXTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF BEAUREGARD, NO. CR-216-06. HONORABLE HERMAN I. STEWART, JR., PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS AMENDED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Thirty-Sixth Judicial District Court, Parish of Beauregard (Louisiana), found defendant guilty of distribution of cocaine under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967. The State filed a habitual offender bill, and the trial court conducted a hearing, finding defendant to be a fourth offender. The trial court sentenced defendant to life imprisonment. The trial court denied his motion to reconsider the sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his life sentence was excessive. The trial court found that defendant was a fourth habitual offender; thus, a life sentence was mandated by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1A(1)(c)(ii). In order to rebut the presumption that the mandatory minimum sentence of life was constitutional, defendant had to clearly and convincingly show that he was exceptional. However, defendant failed to show that he was exceptional. Defendant testified at the habitual offender hearing, but he focused on claiming that he was innocent of the underlying offense. At the end of his testimony, he admitted being a drug user, and claimed to be an addict, but denied having sold drugs since 1993. The appellate court found defendant's unsupported claim that he was merely a drug user, rather than a drug distributor, was negated by his most recent conviction. Also, defendant's bare claim that he was a nonviolent addict would not render the mandatory minimum sentence of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 excessive because a nonviolent criminal history could not be the major reason for a downward deviation. Thus, defendant's life sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction. The appellate court also amended his sentence to delete the trial court's statements regarding diminution eligibility. Finally, the appellate court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions to make an entry in the minutes reflecting the appellate court's amendment.

State v. Rideout


No. 42,689-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,689 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/31/07); 968 So. 2d 1210; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1975



October 31, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Rideout v. Rader, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 99099 (W.D. La., Sept. 14, 2009)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Rideout v. State, 18 So. 3d 87, 2009 La. LEXIS 2714 (La., 2009)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Rideout v. State, 57 So. 3d 325, 2011 La. LEXIS 541 (La., 2011)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Rideout v. Warden, Dixon Corr. Inst., 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 118317 (W.D. La., July 18, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 244,529. Honorable Ramona L. Emanuel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of aggravated rape and molestation of a juvenile. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to prove that the sexual acts occurred in Caddo Parish or that the victim was under age thirteen. The court of appeal disagreed. The State raised in its pre-trial motion defendant's Bossier Parish sexual misconduct as allowable other crimes evidence. If that same evidence of defendant's Bossier Parish actions with the victim represented the only evidence of aggravated rape, making prosecution in Caddo Parish improper, defendant was obliged to raise venue through the pre-trial motion to quash. No special jury instruction was therefore required because the substance of defendant's arguments related to venue. Moreover, the victim testified that defendant molested her in Shreveport while he was moving into the apartment. Defendant leased the apartment on September 9, 2004. The evidence adduced at trial clearly showed that the baby was born on June 29, 2005. Conception occurred between August 25, 2004 and October 6, 2004, in advance of the victim's thirteenth birthday. Therefore, it was clear that defendant's sexual misconduct with the victim occurred in Caddo Parish before she turned 13.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hines


NO. 07-KA-312


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


07-312 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/30/07); 970 So. 2d 1134; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2035



October 30, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 11, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 05-5755, DIVISION "N". HONORABLE HANS J. LILJEBERG, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED, REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, which convicted him of looting under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.5 and sentenced him to 14 years of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with looting when he was observed taking furniture from a store after a hurricane struck the state. He entered a plea of guilty and was sentenced to 14 years in prison. This appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court determined that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62.5(A) was not unconstitutionally vague because it provided adequate notice of the proscribed conduct and its consequences to persons of reasonable intelligence. The phrase "normal security" in § 14:62.5(A) prohibited the unauthorized entry into a home, place of business, or other structure and the removal of property when the home, business, or structure was compromised by reason of a hurricane, other forces of nature, or civil unrest. After defendant admitted that he was a second felony offender, his underlying sentence was vacated, and he was sentenced to 14 years in prison. Due to the fact that a plea agreement was entered, defendant was precluded from raising an appellate argument based on the alleged excessiveness of the sentence under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.2(A)(2). Finally, it was noted that defendant might have received an improper indeterminate sentence.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, but the case was remanded to the district court for clarification of defendant's sentence upon resentencing.

 

1125 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zeigler


No. 42,661-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,661 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/24/07); 968 So. 2d 875; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1941



October 24, 2007, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 03F2288. Honorable Benjamin Jones, Judge.
State v. Zeigler, 945 So. 2d 946, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2894 (La.App. 2 Cir., Dec. 20, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of distributing cocaine. On remand, the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana) sentenced defendant as a fourth felony offender to 30 years at hard labor without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence, the first two years of which was to be served without benefit of parole. Defendant sought review of his sentence for excessiveness.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(c)(i), the trial court had imposed the mandatory minimum sentence on defendant where the State had presented evidence that he was a fourth felony offender. In sentencing defendant, the trial court was cognizant of the sentencing considerations of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 as it had noted his limited education, his age, his young children, and his role in the cocaine distribution. However, there was no justification for a sentence less than the mandatory minimum where defendant had presented no evidence that his circumstances were exceptional or that he was the victim of the legislature's failure to assign sentences meaningfully tailored to his culpability, the gravity of his offense, or the circumstances of his case. Because defendant had not shown that his case was exceptional and warranted a rare departure from the mandatory minimum sentence under the Habitual Offender Law, the trial court properly sentenced defendant within the statutory range prescribed for a fourth offender under the Habitual Offender Law.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.

State v. Dew


No. 42,392-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,392 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/17/07); 968 So. 2d 288; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1900



October 17, 2007, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Eleventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of DeSoto, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 0613248. Honorable Robert E. Burgess, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by bill of information with DWI 4th, contrary to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98(E). The Eleventh Judicial District Court for the Parish of DeSoto, Louisiana,, without objection from either side, charged the jury that six possible verdicts were available to them. The jury returned with a verdict of attempted DWI 4th. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The possible six verdicts that were available to the jury were: (1) Guilty of DWI 4th; (2) Guilty of Attempted DWI 4th; (3) Guilty of DWI 3rd; (4) Guilty of DWI 2nd; (5) Guilty of DWI; and (6) Not guilty. The issue on appeal was whether attempted DWI was a crime. The appellate court believed that it was. The appellate court noted that the record was crystal-clear that defendant committed the crime of DWI 4th offense. The appellate court concluded that it was no moment that attempted DWI required the additional harmonization of the attempt statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:27, with DWI, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98. No objection was made at trial to the proposed charge, which arguably waived any objection on appeal. The jury cut defendant a huge break with an obvious compromise verdict. The appellate court concluded that just because the verdict was unusual and undeserved, however, did not mean that the verdict was illegal.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Miller v. Ellender

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at, Sub nomine at La. United Bus. Ass'n Self Insurers Fund v. Ellender, 968 So. 2d 1132, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1905 (La.App. 3 Cir., Oct. 17, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION - # 3, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 04-6024. CHARLOTTE L. BUSHNELL, WORKERS' COMPENSATION JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, self-insured fund, challenged the judgment of the workers' compensation judge for the Office of Workers' Compensation No. 3, Parish of Calcasieu, Louisiana, finding that she lacked subject matter jurisdiction over claims stemming from a workers' compensation agreement between the fund and appellee, employer, involving a workers' compensation claim filed by appellee, employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed a disputed claim for workers' compensation alleging that he was injured while in the course and scope of his employment with the employer. The employee filed an amended disputed claim adding the fund. As such, the fund asserted that the workers' compensation agreement between it and the employer did not provide coverage. Prior to trial, a settlement agreement was reached in which the fund paid the employee $ 10,000 and he released all parties. The fund reserved its right to assert its coverage issue. Before the submission of any evidence, the workers' compensation judge held that since this was an allegation of insurance fraud, subject matter jurisdiction was lacking. The appellate court ruled that the workers' compensation judge erred in finding that subject matter jurisdiction was lacking. The settlement of the employee's claim did not divest the Office of Workers' Compensation of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Carter v. Jones


CA 07-297


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-297 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/17/07); 967 So. 2d 615; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1907



October 17, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Carter v. Honorable Judges, 972 So. 2d 457, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2279 (La.App. 3 Cir., Dec. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 2006-195. HONORABLE ANNE LENNAN SIMON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff district court judge sought review of an order from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which denied him relief in an action against defendants, a court clerk and judges, challenging the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:587 and a local rule that designated two of the court's nine divisions as family and juvenile divisions.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:587, the judges of a district court voted unanimously to enact a local rule that designated two of the court's nine divisions as family and juvenile divisions. However, the judge directed the clerk to assign one-ninth of all family and juvenile cases to his division. The other judges in the district issued an order forbidding such case reassignments. The judge brought an action against defendants, challenging the constitutionality of § 13:587. The trial court denied relief to the judge. On appeal, the court held that § 13:587 did not constitute an unconstitutional delegation of the legislature's exclusive authority to establish courts of limited jurisdiction. Section 13:587 did not violate La. Const. art. 5, § 15(A) or La. Const. art. 2, § 2. Further, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:587 did not restrict unconstitutionally the judge's exercise of general jurisdiction. Section 13:587's non-random allotment procedures had to prevail as an exception to the prohibitions against non-random allotment contained in La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 253.1, as the former was the more specific of two statutes that touched upon the same subject matter.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1129 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martin


NO. 2007-KA-0791


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2007-0791 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/17/07); 970 So. 2d 9; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2101



October 17, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 26, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 462-792, SECTION "J". HONORABLE DARRYL A. DERBIGNY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of attempted simple burglary of an inhabited dwelling, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:62.2 and 14:27. The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), sentenced him to six years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to convict him and that the sentence he received was excessive. The jury could have inferred that defendant had the specific intent to commit the crime of simple burglary of an inhabited dwelling where he was found standing on the victim's back porch without her permission, the screen next to the latch was torn, a glass pane near the door that led inside was broken, and defendant was holding a tool when confronted by the police. Moreover, the screened-in porch was an inhabited dwelling because the placement of the roof of the porch was not dispositive of whether the porch was part of the house and there was evidence that the porch was completely screened, the outside door leading to the porch was locked, and there were doors on the porch leading inside the house. The trial court had not imposed an excessive sentence given defendant's extensive juvenile record.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Dale v. Secy. of State


NUMBER 2007 CE 2020


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 2020 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/11/07); 971 So. 2d 1136; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1929



October 11, 2007, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket Number 559,775. Honorable Wilson Fields, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: OCTOBER 4, 2007 JUDGMENT DENYING PRELIMINARY INJUNCTION AFFIRMED; REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a candidate, a taxpayer, and a prospective candidate, sued defendants, the Louisiana Secretary of State and a clerk, seeking to enjoin the reopening of the qualifying period for a sheriff's election and challenging the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:469. The Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, denied plaintiffs' preliminary injunction request. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the qualifying period for the office of sheriff closed, the incumbent died before the election. Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:469, the qualifying period for the primary election was reopened for three days and additional candidates qualified. Plaintiffs alleged that § 18:469 violated the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of the Louisiana Constitution, La. Const. art. 1, §§ 2 and 3, based on the additional monies that would have to be spent. The appellate court determined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying a preliminary injunction because plaintiffs failed to establish a prima facie case that they would prevail on the merits on their constitutional challenges since, inter alia, (1) La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:469 served a legitimate government purpose of promoting candidacy, (2) regarding the prospective candidate's claims involving time requirements, he did not challenge the relevant statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:465, and (3) taxpayers' financial burden did not justify injunctive relief. The trial court did not err in failing to consider the declaratory judgment request, but the request was entitled to expedited treatment on remand.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment denying plaintiffs' request for preliminary injunction and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CITY CIVIL SERVICE COMMISSION ORLEANS. NOS. 7104 C/W 7119 C/W 7089 C/W 7099 C/W 7101 C/W 7115 C/W 7272 C/W 7284 C/W 7117 C/W 7118 C/W 7113 C/W 7114.
Reed v. Dep't of Police, 964 So. 2d 373, 2007 La. LEXIS 2245 (La., 2007)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS VACATED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police department challenged a decision from the New Orleans, Louisiana, Civil Service Commission (CSC), which determined that the discipline imposed against appellee police officers was illegal due to the lack of a pre-termination hearing.


OVERVIEW: The officers had abandoned their posts or failed to report for duty after a hurricane struck. The officers contended that the failure to conduct a pre-termination hearing constituted a violation of due process under the United States Constitution and La. Const. art. I, § 2. The CSC determined that the discipline imposed upon the officers was illegal, and this appeal followed. In vacating the decision of the CSC, the appellate court held that due process required an opportunity for a hearing before the deprivation of a significant property interest. The officers had a property interest in employment because they had received the position, and they were guaranteed to continued employment unless certain exceptions applied. However, there were situations where a postdeprivation hearing was enough to satisfy due process requirements. Due process had a flexible standard that called for such procedural protections as the particular situation demanded. The emergency situation in the city after the hurricane constituted an extraordinary or truly unusual situation. The voiding of the disciplinary action in this case would have had a negative impact on those that remained at their posts.


OUTCOME: The decision from the CSC was vacated. The cases were remanded for the receipt of additional evidence as necessary to resolve the cases and render a judgment on the merits.

Coulee Kinney Drainage Dist. v. Broussard


07-175


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


07-175 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/03/07); 966 So. 2d 1191; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1813



October 3, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF VERMILION, NO. 81362-J. HONORABLE KRISTIAN D. EARLES, DISTRICT COURT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff drainage district sued defendant landowner, seeking a declaratory judgment regarding access to a drainage ditch. The Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Vermilion, Louisiana, rendered judgment in favor of the drainage district, cast the landowner with the costs associated with an expert witness fee, and denied the landowner compensation for the drainage district's use of the legal servitude. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner denied the drainage district access to a drainage ditch which formed the northern boundary line of the landowner's property. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 38:113, 38:1764, and 38:1804, the appellate court determined that the trial court properly found that the drainage ditch was a natural drain and that the drainage district had the authority to clean and maintain the ditch because the evidence in the record clearly established that the drainage ditch was a natural drain which formed part of the natural drainage scheme in the geographical area which had been in existence for decades. Under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1920, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in assessing the costs of court against the landowner, including the expert witness fee, because the drainage district prevailed in its declaratory judgment suit. Finally, the trial court did not err in failing to award the landowner compensation for the drainage district's use of a construction servitude, because the record was void of any evidence to support the allegation that the landowner was damaged, or the amount of any damages alleged.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgments.

Fransen v. City of New Orleans


NO. 2006-CA-1325


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2006-1325 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/03/07); 970 So. 2d 1; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1919



October 3, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, in part, Rehearing denied by, in part Fransen v. City of New Orleans, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2352 (La.App. 4 Cir., Dec. 12, 2007)
Rehearing denied by Fransen v. City of New Orleans, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2321 (La.App. 4 Cir., Dec. 18, 2007)
Writ granted by Fransen v. City of New Orleans, 976 So. 2d 1275, 2008 La. LEXIS 475 (La., 2008)
Writ granted by Fransen v. City of New Orleans, 976 So. 2d 1275, 2008 La. LEXIS 436 (La., 2008)
Affirmed in part and vacated in part by, Remanded by Fransen v. City of New Orleans, 2008 La. LEXIS 1526 (La., July 1, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2002-5170, DIVISION "N". HONORABLE ETHEL SIMMS JULIEN, JUDGE.
Fransen v. City of New Orleans, 862 So. 2d 142, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3301 (La.App. 4 Cir., Nov. 19, 2003)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of an order from the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which awarded summary judgment to defendants, a city, United Governmental Services of Louisiana, and law firms, and held that New Orleans, La., Ordinance No. 18637 was constitutional in an action challenging the assessment of penalties, interest, and attorney fees in connection with the collection of taxes.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers did not pay their property taxes timely. Once the taxes were paid, the taxpayers received notice that they each owed additional penalties, interest, and attorney fees for making the late tax payments. The taxpayers brought a suit against defendants, challenging the assessment of the penalties, interest, and attorney fees. The taxpayers asked for partial summary judgment declaring Ordinance 18637 unconstitutional. Defendants asked for summary judgment declaring the ordinance constitutional. The trial court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court found that Ordinance 18637 violated La. Const. art. VII, § 25 in that it allowed the taxing unit or its authorized agent to file suit to collect the delinquent tax, and to recover costs and attorney fees. The offending portions of Ordinance 18637 were so interrelated with the remainder of the ordinance that they could not be severed. While the city's home rule charter granted it the right "to lay and collect taxes," the 30 percent penalty assessed against the taxpayers was actually a legal fee disguised as a penalty. The assessment of attorney fees was inconsistent with La. Const. art. VII, § 25.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment upholding the constitutionality of Ordinance 18637. The court declared Ordinance 18637 unconstitutional. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Brown


NO. 42,188-KA, NO. 42,189-KA, NO. 42,190-KA (consolidated cases)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT

September 26, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Brown, 978 So. 2d 347, 2008 La. LEXIS 910 (La., 2008)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Brown v. Warden, La. State Penitentiary, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 121486 (W.D. La., July 28, 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Brown v. Warden, La. State Penitentiary, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 121487 (W.D. La., July 28, 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Brown v. Cain, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 158573 (W.D. La., Oct. 20, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 227,770; 228,307; 243;370. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; ADJUDICATIONS AS A HABITUAL OFFENDER AND SENTENCES AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, convicting him, in three consolidated cases, of illegal use of a weapon during a crime of violence, three counts of possession of a firearm by a convicted felon, possession with intent to distribute a Schedule II controlled dangerous substance (CDS), and illegal carrying of weapons while in possession of a CDS.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction of possession of a CDS and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon because the police officer's testimony established that the contraband was inside the vehicle with defendant and therefore was within his dominion and control. There was sufficient evidence of defendant's intent to distribute the contraband because, given that the officer found $ 2,696 in defendant's pocket, 19.75 grams of powder cocaine in the vehicle's glove compartment, a gram of marijuana in the ashtray, and a loaded firearm and digital scales in the vehicle, there was no reasonable hypothesis that the possession of the cocaine was for personal use. The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction of possession of a firearm by a convicted felon because the State presented evidence that defendant pleaded guilty to armed robbery in 1994 and a police officer testified that defendant's fingerprints taken in open court matched the fingerprints on the back of the bill of information for the armed robbery charge. The trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

State v. Russell


No. 42,479-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,479 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/26/07); 966 So. 2d 154; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1781



September 26, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Russell, 977 So. 2d 897, 2008 La. LEXIS 539 (La., 2008)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Russell v. State, 18 So. 3d 1280, 2009 La. LEXIS 2935 (La., 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Russell v. Cooper, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 41772 (W.D. La., Mar. 4, 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Russell v. State, 199 So. 3d 1144, 2016 La. LEXIS 1780 (La., 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Thirty-Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Red River, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 99657. Honorable Lewis O. Sams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with second degree murder; however, a jury for the Thirty-Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Red River (Louisiana) found defendant guilty of the responsive verdict of manslaughter under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31. Defendant was sentenced to 40 years at hard labor. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: There was no reasonable hypothesis that defendant acted in self-defense because (1) he testified at trial that he initiated the confrontation with the victim; (2) the testimony revealed that he believed the victim had previously engaged in inappropriate behavior with his daughter, which provided defendant with motive for the murder but did not support his claim of self-defense; (3) defendant's story at trial that he allowed the victim to come within arms-length while wielding a machete was simply not logical; (4) the State presented testimony that there were no signs of a physical struggle at the site of the alleged confrontation and shooting; (5) defendant admitted that for over a week he lied to both his mother and the police about the victim's disappearance, which was evidence of consciousness of guilt, not self-defense; (6) the State presented much evidence of concealment, which tended to prove guilty knowledge and cut against a claim of self-defense; and (7) defendant's version of the killing at trial was contradictory in significant respects to his prior statements to police. Thus, the evidence supported the jury's verdict finding him guilty of manslaughter.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Roshell


No. 42,398-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,398 (La.App. 2 cir. 09/26/07); 966 So. 2d 770; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1784



September 26, 2007, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 228787. Honorable Ramona L. Emanuel, Judge.
State v. Roshell, 916 So. 2d 1268, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2572 (La.App. 2 Cir., Dec. 14, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, convicting him of armed robbery (among other counts), and adjudicating him to be a second felony offender and sentencing him to 80 years hard labor without the benefit of probation, parole or suspension of sentence, with the sentence to run concurrently with defendant's other sentences.


OVERVIEW: On remand, defendant was adjudicated a second felony offender and was sentenced to 80 years hard labor for armed robbery. Defendant asserted that there was a complete lack of aggravating factors warranting the 80-year sentence and that the trial court did not consider all factors in making its sentencing determination. The appellate court ruled that defendant's sentence was not so disproportionate to the seriousness of the offense as to shock one's sense of justice. The minimum sentence for armed robbery for a second felony habitual offender was 49 1/2 years' imprisonment at hard labor, and the maximum sentence was 198 years under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:529.1 and 14:64. Defendant committed four crimes of violence against three different city employees while they were on duty, including shooting one of the victims in the back of the head simply because he said he did not have any money. Defendant had a prior criminal history, including crimes of violence.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Harris


NO. 07-KA-124


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


07-124 (La.App. 5 Cir. 09/25/07); 968 So. 2d 187; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1775



September 25, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 7, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 05-5812, DIVISION "O". HONORABLE ROSS P. LADART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; MATTER REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) of looting following Hurricane Katrina. Defendant was sentenced to serve five years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeal disagreed. A detective was "absolutely positive" that the three individuals he saw looting were the same three who ran and were subsequently apprehended and identified as defendant and his accomplices. Another detective testified that he removed the merchandise from the garbage can used to transport the stolen items. He counted them, and recorded the items and amounts on a note pad he carried with him. Those notes were offered into evidence and were contained in the record. He also photographed the items, although in preparation for trial, only the photos from the first arrest could be located. The detective also explained that the vast amounts of merchandise collected that day from looters, and lack of manpower, prevented the items from being taken to police headquarters and processed. The testimony of police officers faced with snipers, citizens in dire need, and numerous looters, was clear, consistent, and positive regarding the identity of the looters, and the exact items looted. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. The sentence was vacated and the matter was remanded to the trial court for re-sentencing.

State v. Castillo


NO. 2007 CE 1865


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 1865 (La.App. 1 Cir. 9/24/07); 971 So. 2d 1081; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1765



September 24, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Castillo, 964 So. 2d 349, 2007 La. LEXIS 2079 (La., 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Castillo v. Louisiana, 128 S. Ct. 896, 169 L. Ed. 2d 748, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 225 (U.S., Jan. 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge. State of Louisiana. District Court No. 559,161. The Honorable Kay Bates, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, candidate, challenged the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, declaring that the candidate was disqualified as a candidate for Governor of Louisiana, pursuant to the petition objecting to the candidacy filed by appellee, parish district attorney.


OVERVIEW: The record established that in 2001, the candidate was convicted of two felony counts of attempted extortion. After serving three years and ten months at hard labor, on October 4, 2006, the candidate was discharged from his sentence and received an automatic first offender pardon pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:572B(1). The candidate had not sought, nor had he received, a pardon from the Governor for the State of Louisiana. The candidate argued that pursuant to La. Const. art. I, § 20, he was entitled to hold public office. The appellate court ruled that to the extent that La. Const. art. I, § 20, could be construed to conflict with La. Const. art. I, § 10, the latter and more recent and more specific provision prevailed. Also, the candidate asserted that as a first offender, he was entitled to an automatic pardon upon completion of his sentence, pursuant to La. Const. art. IV, § 5(E)(1). The appellate court ruled that the automatic pardon provision under La. Const. art. IV, § 5(E)(1) did not restore the candidate's right to hold public office.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Deculus v. Welborn


NO. 2007 CE 1836


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 1836 (La.App. 1 Cir. 9/19/07); 970 So. 2d 1057; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1696



September 19, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by Deculus v. Welborn, 964 So. 2d 348, 2007 La. LEXIS 1975 (La., Sept. 24, 2007)
Affirmed by Deculus v. Welborn, 964 So. 2d 930, 2007 La. LEXIS 2076 (La., Oct. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge. State of Louisiana. District Court No. 559,067. The Honorable Donald R. Johnson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff objectors challenged a decision from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, which dismissed their petition objecting to defendant candidate's eligibility for election.


OVERVIEW: After a senator resigned during a term, the candidate was elected to fill the vacancy. He was subsequently elected to serve second and third consecutive terms of office. When he announced an intention to run for a fourth time, the objectors filed a petition, which stated that the candidate was ineligible to do so. The petition was dismissed, and this appeal followed. In reversing, the appellate court determined that the trial court had subject matter jurisdiction over this case because La. Const. art. III, § 7(A) had no bearing on its authority to challenge a candidate's qualifications. In fact, the trial court had jurisdiction under La. Const. art. V, § 16(A) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1403. Next, the term limits for the candidate were set out in La. Const. art. III, § 4(E). Because the candidate had served for more than two and one-half terms in three consecutive terms, he was prohibited by law from being a candidate here. To the extent that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:601 was interpreted in derogation of the clear language of the Louisiana Constitution, it was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and judgment was entered in favor of the objectors.

State v. Henry


No. 42,416-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,416 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/19/07); 966 So. 2d 692; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1715



September 19, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Henry v. State, 989 So. 2d 95, 2008 La. LEXIS 1699 (La., 2008)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Henry v. State, 2014 La. LEXIS 426 (La., Feb. 14, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 242,742. Honorable Roy L. Brun, Judge.
State v. Henry, 601 So. 2d 40, 1992 La. App. LEXIS 2392 (La.App. 2 Cir., 1992)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED. SENTENCE AMENDED, AND, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of illegal possession of Schedule IV controlled dangerous substance. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeal disagreed. The circumstances indicated that defendant was aware that he was in possession of a controlled dangerous substance. At the time the Xanax pills were found, defendant was in a vehicle with a person under investigation for narcotics distribution through a neighborhood known as a high-crime area with narcotics traffic. Both officers testified that defendant admitted the pills were his and stated that he got them from a friend for his mouth pain. They further testified that defendant had a crack pipe when he was searched and that he originally agreed to assist them in narcotics investigations to avoid arrest. When defendant was arrested two weeks later, he stated that he traded a rock of crack cocaine to people in exchange for the pills, which he believed to be pain medication for his mouth. Given defendant's statement that he traded a rock of crack cocaine for the pills that he believed were pain medication, the evidence was sufficient from which a rational fact finder could have determined that defendant knew the pills were a controlled dangerous substance.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was amended to 25 years at hard labor without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

1141 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Roberts


No. 42,417-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,417 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/19/07); 966 So. 2d 111; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1714



September 19, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Roberts v. State, 21 So. 3d 277, 2009 La. LEXIS 3106 (La., 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Roberts v. David Wade Corr. Ctr., 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 123328 (W.D. La., Aug. 8, 2013)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Roberts v. State, 138 So. 3d 641, 2014 La. LEXIS 1031 (La., 2014)
Related proceeding at Roberts v. Emanuel, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 66086 (W.D. La., Apr. 27, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 242,253. Honorable Leon Emanuel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED AND, AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of molestation of a juvenile. The trial court found defendant to be a third-felony habitual offender and sentenced him to 20 years at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeal disagreed. Defendant testified that he was born August 31, 1979, and the victim was between the ages of six and seven years old when these incidents of sexual abuse occurred; thus, the State presented sufficient evidence to show that defendant was over the age of seventeen, that the victim was under the age of seventeen and that the age difference was more than two years. The testimony of the child from the video described many lewd and lascivious acts committed upon her by defendant. The child testified that defendant threatened to kill her if she told. That constituted evidence that defendant committed the acts through a threat of great bodily harm. Further, defendant lived with the child, the child called defendant "daddy," and defendant committed many of the lewd and lascivious acts while the child was in his care. Those facts supported the conclusion that defendant accomplished the acts by use of influence by virtue of being in a position of control or supervision over the child. Accordingly, the State presented sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was amended to delete the denial of parole eligibility. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

1142 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dudley


NO. 2006 KA 1087


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006 1087 (La.App. 1 Cir. 9/19/07); 984 So. 2d 11; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1695



September 19, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ dismissed by State v. Dudley, 25 So. 3d 783, 2009 La. LEXIS 3376 (La., Nov. 20, 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Dudley v. Cain, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 47793 (M.D. La., Feb. 11, 2014)
Related proceeding at State v. Dudley, 2017 La. App. LEXIS 1231 (La.App. 1 Cir., July 7, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Case No. 04-02-0314. The Honorable Michael R. Erwin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AND SENTENCES ON COUNTS II - X AFFIRMED; CONVICTION AND SENTENCE ON COUNT XI VACATED; CONVICTION, HABITUAL-OFFENDER ADJUDICATION, AND SENTENCE ON COUNT XII AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the 19th Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) found defendant guilty of Medicaid fraud, theft, and money laundering under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:70.1, 14:67, and 14:230. He was adjudged a second-felony habitual offender and sentenced to 50 years at hard labor. Defendant appealed his convictions and his habitual-offender sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions for Medicaid fraud and money laundering did not violate the double jeopardy prohibition in the Fifth Amendment or La. Const. art. I, § 15 because the evidence required to support the finding of guilt of Medicaid fraud (the fraudulent billing) did not also support the conviction for money laundering (concealing or disguising the nature or source of proceeds derived from the Medicaid fraud). However, the evidence required to support the finding of guilt of theft - the taking of money (proceeds derived from Medicaid fraud) by means of fraudulent conduct, practices, or representations (the fraudulent billing) - did involve the same evidence required to support the Medicaid fraud convictions and the money laundering conviction. Thus, defendant's theft conviction violated double jeopardy. However, the evidence was sufficient to convict him of Medicaid fraud and money laundering. Furthermore, his habitual-offender sentence was proper because he had previously been convicted of a felony. Finally, the sentence imposed on him was not grossly disproportionate to the severity of the offense; thus, it was not unconstitutionally excessive under La. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences for Medicaid fraud, vacated defendant's conviction and sentence for theft, and affirmed defendant's conviction, habitual-offender adjudication, and sentence for money laundering.

 

1143 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Livingston Parish Law Enforcement Dist.


2007 CA 0628 CONSOLIDATED WITH 2007 CA 0629 CONSOLIDATED WITH 2007 CA 0630


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 0628 (La.App. 1 Cir. 9/14/07); 970 So. 2d 996; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1647



September 14, 2007, Judgment rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 21st Judicial District Court Parish of Livingston, Louisiana. Docket Nos. 108118, 108119, and 108120, Division "A". Honorable Wayne Ray Chutz, Judge Presiding.
Jones v. Livingston Parish Law Enforcement Dist., 904 So. 2d 93, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1811 (La.App. 1 Cir., June 9, 2005)



DISPOSITION: MOTION GRANTED; APPEAL DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sued defendant political subdivisions, alleging that ordinances that rededicated a certain percentage of sales and use taxes for debt service on bonds issued to finance a retail outlet were unconstitutional and contravened statutory authority. Plaintiffs appealed a decision of the 21st Judicial District Court Parish of Livingston, Louisiana, dismissing their consolidated challenges. Defendants moved to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The Supreme Court of Louisiana had held that the failure to challenge the bond resolution within 30 days of its publication barred all challenges to the bonds, their security, and the means of payment, but it had pretermitted consideration of the appellate court's ruling that timely filed challenges to the legality of the elections were not barred by La. Rev. Stat. § 33:9038.34(L). The Supreme Court's pretermitting discussion was not an approval of the appellate court's ruling. Reconsideration of the previously raised issues was appropriate as the appellate court had previously declined to exercise its supervisory jurisdiction and it had to consider the Supreme Court's decision in the bond validation suit. Since plaintiffs' claims did not challenge the election, La. Const. art. VI. § 35(A) did not apply. The Supreme Court's decision in the bond validation suit was conclusive as to the validity of the bonds, the tax, the pledge of revenues, and any other provisions of the bonds; it had clearly stated that plaintiffs had failed to timely exercise the right to contest the bond resolution and its security provisions. Thus, the appellate court lacked jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss the appeal was granted. Each party to the appeal was to bear its own costs.

State v. Harper


2007 KA 0299


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2007 0299 (La.App. 1 Cir. 9/5/07); 970 So. 2d 592; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1606



September 5, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Harper, 976 So. 2d 173, 2008 La. LEXIS 344 (La., 2008)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Harper v. Douzat, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 10960 (E.D. La., Jan. 10, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 32<nd> Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne, State of Louisiana. Number 452,769. The Honorable Timothy C. Ellender, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION, HABITUAL-OFFENDER ADJUDICATION, AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the 32nd Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana), which convicted him of simple kidnapping in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:45, sentenced him as a third-felony habitual offender, and denied his motion for reconsideration of his 7-year sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of simple kidnapping and was found to have been a third-felony habitual offender; he was sentenced to imprisonment at hard labor for seven years. He appealed after his motion for reconsideration of sentence was denied. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that the evidence was sufficient. The victim testified that defendant placed the knife to her throat and forced her from the kitchen to the bathroom, to the yard, and from the yard to her own residence. The victim further testified that defendant continued to hold the knife to her throat and threatened to "blues" her, which the victim testified meant that defendant would do anything possible to her. And, while the prior inconsistent statements of two witnesses in the case were admissible to attack credibility under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 607(D)(2), such nonhearsay statements were also admissible for their assertive value as well. Defendant was exposed to a maximum sentence of 10 years for his conviction under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:45(B) and 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(i), and he was sentenced to 7 years. It was clear that the sentence imposed was well within the statutory limits.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
