Adams v. Bd. of Comm'rs


NO. 2005-CA-1159


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-1159 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/29/07); 966 So. 2d 660; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1748



August 29, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 2, 2007.
Writ denied by Adams v. Bd. of Comm'rs, 969 So. 2d 633, 2007 La. LEXIS 2889 (La., 2007)
Related proceeding at Hugel v. Southeast La. Flood Prot. Auth. - East, 2011 U.S. App. LEXIS 12122 (5th Cir. La., June 14, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2000-19878, DIVISION "J-13". HONORABLE NADINE M. RAMSEY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, original lessees and their successors-in-interest, appealed a judgment from the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, denying their claim for declaratory relief regarding lease option agreements executed between the lessees and defendant lessor, the Board of Commissioners of the Orleans Parish Levee District, that extended the terms of their existing leases of public marina land.


OVERVIEW: The original leases contained reversionary clauses under which improvements such as boathouses vested in the District when the leases expired. To avoid reversion, various lessees negotiated lease options at different times, resulting in some lessees obtaining a more favorable future rental rate than the suing lessees. The trial court held that the suing lessees' lease options were void for failure to specify the rental amount as required by La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2668. On appeal, the court agreed. A decision in a separate but related case upholding the validity of the more favorable lease options was inapplicable, as those leases did specify a rental rate. The suing lessees' equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, and La. Const. art. 1, § 3, were not violated because the first lessees to accept the option offer were legitimately treated differently from the suing lessees, as the earlier leases contained statutory or constitutional infirmities. The reversionary provision did not result in a taking without just compensation under La. Const. art. 1, § 4(B)(1) because the lessees received the bargained-for benefit of using the boathouses for the lease period.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Ross


No. 42,399-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT

August 29, 2007, Judgment Rendered

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, convicting him of attempted second-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:30.1, 14:27, and sentencing him to 50 years at hard labor without benefits.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for shooting at the victim during a drive-by shooting, along with two co-defendants. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support his conviction and that the State negated any reasonable probability of misidentification. The court held that the State proved beyond a reasonable doubt the free and voluntary nature of defendant's two statements to police and that he knowingly and intelligently waived his Miranda rights. The first statement, made while defendant was being treated in the hospital, was clearly non-custodial. The court held that the senselessness, danger, and reprehensible nature of defendant's crime clearly justified his 50-year sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Cox


No. 42,232-KW


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,232 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/22/07); 963 So. 2d 1080; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1573



August 22, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Cox, 967 So. 2d 526, 2007 La. LEXIS 2642 (La., Nov. 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 147,422. Honorable Jeffrey Stephen Cox, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, which denied her motion to suppress evidence in a driving while impaired (DWI) case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for speeding on a parish road by a state trooper. Her actions were in violation of a parish ordinance, but she was operating at less than the presumptive state highway speed limit established by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:61. She was arrested for DWI after the trooper noticed signs of impairment. Defendant filed a motion to suppress evidence under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 703, which argued that the initial stop was illegal. This was based on the fact that the speeding charge was quashed due to the lack of violation under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 32:61-64. The motion was denied, and this appeal followed. In affirming, the appellate court found that the trooper's actions here were objectively reasonable due to the fact that defendant was traveling over the posted speed limit. Moreover, suppression of the trooper's observations of impairment immediately after the stop would not have satisfied a rational societal objective. Finally, it was unnecessary to the validity of the stop to determine the powers of the trooper to enforce local government traffic laws, although the appellate court noted that they had such powers.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

Hayes v. La. State Penitentiary


2006 CA 0553


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006 0553 (La.App. 1 Cir. 8/15/07); 970 So. 2d 547; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1521



August 15, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Hayes v. La. State Penitentiary, 2008 La. LEXIS 200 (La., Jan. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the Office of Workers' Compensation Administration. District 5, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 02-00715. Honorable Jason G. Ourso, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer challenged a judgment of the Office of Workers' Compensation Administration, District 5, State of Louisiana, holding that appellee employee's accident occurred on or about January 20, 1997 and awarding the employee supplemental earnings benefits (SEB), medical benefits, penalties, attorney fees, legal interest, and costs.


OVERVIEW: The employee, the food director at a state penitentiary, fell and injured his back while on a loading dock directing a supply truck. On appeal, the court held that there was no showing that the employee made any wilful misrepresentation or false statement in order to obtain workers' compensation benefits in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208(G) because the employee stated that he had told his supervisors that he owned a tire business, that he never paid himself a salary, that the business operated at a loss, and therefore the employee did not believe that he had any earnings to report. The workers' compensation judge's (WCJ) determination that the employee's testimony was credible and its finding that accident occurred on January 20, 1997 was reasonably supported by the record. The record also provided reasonable support for the WCJ's finding that a causal connection between the accident and the disabling condition was shown. The provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1221(3)(d)(iii) were inapplicable because there was no evidence of the employee's intention to permanently withdraw from the work force, given his self-employment in his used tire business.


OUTCOME: The judgment for the employee was affirmed.

State v. Barrett


No. 42,303-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,303 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/15/07); 963 So. 2d 1072; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1525



August 15, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Barrett, 976 So. 2d 174, 2008 La. LEXIS 389 (La., 2008)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Barrett v. La. State Penitentiary, 2014 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 22097 (W.D. La., Jan. 28, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 246,317. Honorable Jeanette G. Garrett, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of simple burglary. Thereafter, he was adjudicated a fourth felony offender. He was sentenced to 40 years at hard labor, with credit for time served, to run consecutively with any other sentence. Defendant was also ordered to pay restitution to the victim in the amount of $ 500. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeal disagreed. Defendant was discovered in a back corner area of the business, lying between two rafters with a plywood board on top of him. After defendant followed the officer's verbal commands, he was placed under arrest. Defendant was led down from the attic space whereupon the owner informed the arresting officers that defendant was not an employee nor did he have permission to be inside the building. The owner testified that defendant did not have permission to be inside the business and he further testified that there were valuable pieces of equipment inside the building, including hand tools, power tools, computers, and small electrical equipment that could easily have been picked up and carried out. The owner testified that after the burglary, he noticed that two tires had been removed from inside the building and that the tires would have had to have been removed for defendant to gain entry into the building. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to sustain the conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Johnson


No. 42,323-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,323 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/15/07); 962 So. 2d 1126; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1552

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Johnson, 976 So. 2d 166, 2008 La. LEXIS 336 (La., 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Johnson v. State, 187 So. 3d 996, 2016 La. LEXIS 766 (La., 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 219,715. Honorable Roy L. Brun, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of three counts of molestation of a juvenile. He was adjudicated a third felony habitual offender on the first count and sentenced to 30 years on count one and 15 years on counts two and three, imposed consecutively and without benefits. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in imposing unconstitutionally excessive sentences, particularly by ordering that the sentences be served consecutively. The court of appeal disagreed. The record indicated that defendant knew he had a problem, yet he continued to molest the children on numerous occasions over a span of years, and the abuse started when the children were very young. The consecutive sentences imposed were justified by the record, and accordingly, there was no abuse of the trial court's discretion in imposing the consecutive sentences. Additionally, the trial court did not err in allowing hearsay evidence to impermissibly bolster the victims' testimony and ease the State's burden of proof. The officer's testimony was not hearsay because the declarants actually testified at the trial, were subject to cross-examination, and the evidence was offered to rebut a defense challenge to the implication that the victims' testimony contained exaggerated descriptions of events in order to bolster the State's case.


OUTCOME: The parts of defendant's sentences that imposed a sentence without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence were deleted. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Grefer v. Alpha Tech.


NO. 2002-CA-1237


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-1237 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/08/07); 965 So. 2d 511; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1602



August 8, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 12, 2007.
Writ denied by Grefer v. Alpha Tech., 967 So. 2d 523, 2007 La. LEXIS 2688 (La., 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Exxon Mobil Corp. v. Grefer, 553 U.S. 1014, 128 S. Ct. 2054, 170 L. Ed. 2d 810, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 3513 (2008)
Class certification denied by Pollard v. Alpha Tech., Chevron U.S.A., Inc., 31 So. 3d 576, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 116 (La.App. 4 Cir., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 97-15004, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE CAROLYN GILL-JEFFERSON, JUDGE.
Exxon Mobil Corp. v. Grefer, 549 U.S. 1249, 127 S. Ct. 1371, 167 L. Ed. 2d 156, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 2656 (2007)



DISPOSITION: AMENDED, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), entered judgment for plaintiff property owners in an action against defendant oil company awarding them $ 56 million in compensatory and general damages and $ 1 billion in punitive damages. The court affirmed and reduced the punitive damages. The United State Supreme Court granted the oil company's petition for a writ of certiorari, vacated the judgment, and remanded for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: The property owners sued the oil company to recover damages for the contamination of a 33-acre tract of land with radioactive material. Between 1968 and 1992, an oil field service company had leased the land from the owners for its business operations, which included the cleaning, inspecting, testing, threading, transporting, and storage of oil well tubulars for the oil company and others. The Court remanded the case for further consideration in light of its decision in the Phillip Morris case. On review, the court held that the jury instructions concerning punitive damages were constitutional under the due process clause because the trial court set forth a correct statement of the law and none of the factors included in the instructions, including reprehensibility, punishment, deterrence, harm to the owners, and the oil company's financial condition, were objectionable or prohibited. The record contained sufficient evidence to support the jury's finding that the oil company had engaged in wanton and reckless conduct supporting a punitive damage award. However, the court held that the $ 1 billion award was excessive, and reduced it to $ 112 million, twice the general damage award.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment rendered in favor of the property owners was amended, in part, to reduce the $ 1 billion award for punitive damages to $ 112,290,000 to comply with the Due Process Clause. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed. Furthermore, the trial court's judgment denying the oil company's exception of prescription was affirmed.

 

1152 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. McGuffie


No. 42,069-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,069 (La.App. 2 Cir. 8/01/07); 962 So. 2d 1111; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1487



August 1, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. McGuffie, 2008 La. LEXIS 445 (La., Feb. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 03-F1339. Honorable C. Wendell Manning, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED. SENTENCE VACATED AND CASE REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana, convicting him of malfeasance in office in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:134 and sentencing him to five years at hard labor with the first three years to be served without benefit of suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an assistant parish administrator for the police, was convicted for using a parish employee, vehicle, and equipment for tree trimming work on his private property. On appeal, the court held that defendant's argument that the trial court erred by allowing a police officer to testify regarding taped interviews of defendant, when the tapes, transcribed notes, and investigating officer's notes were lost, was without merit because defendant conceded at trial that the State complied with discovery and disclosed the missing tapes prior to trial. However, the court held that defendant's sentence was excessive under La. Const. art. 1, § 20 because: (1) there was no indication that defendant exhibited any prior pattern of misusing public resources; (2) the offense also involved another employee's control and actions; (3) defendant was a 58-year-old first time offender with no criminal record; (4) defendant had a serious medical condition and his incarceration would involve an astronomical expense; and (5) the offense was far from the most egregious act of malfeasance or abuse of public position, as the actual out-of-pocket expenses to the parish amounted to less than $ 300.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed but his sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing.

 

1153 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Taylor


NO. 06-KA-558


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


06-558 (La.App. 5 Cir. 07/30/07); 966 So. 2d 631; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1467



July 30, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 9, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 04-103, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE PATRICK J. MCCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Taylor, 876 So. 2d 76, 2004 La. LEXIS 1929 (La., June 4, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) of possession with intent to distribute marijuana within one thousand feet of a school. Defendant's motion for a new trial was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the officer did not have reasonable suspicion to conduct an investigatory stop, nor did he have probable cause for an arrest. The court of appeals disagreed. An officer was dispatched regarding a man sitting on a gray pickup truck selling narcotics. When the officer arrived, he saw a gray truck with defendant sitting on the truck's open tailgate eating crabs. Defendant gave the officer his identification, and the officer called in defendant's personal information to determine if he had any outstanding warrants. While the officer was speaking to defendant, defendant appeared nervous, and his hands shook badly. Defendant would not make eye contact with him. The officer decided, for his own safety, to conduct a pat-down search of defendant's outer clothing for weapons. As defendant turned to comply with the order, he moved his hand toward his left pants pocket. Fearing defendant might be reaching for a weapon, the officer grabbed his hand, and placed him in handcuffs. The officer then felt what he believed were bags of narcotics. The officer reached into defendant's pocket and retrieved seven small bags containing what appeared to be marijuana.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1154 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Derkins


NO. 07-KA-151


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


07-151 (La.App. 5 Cir. 07/30/07); 966 So. 2d 623; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1464



July 30, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 9, 2007.
Writ denied by State v. Derkins, 2008 La. LEXIS 194 (La., Jan. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 04-4269, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE CHARLES V. CUSIMANO, II, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of the distribution of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A) and sentenced him as a second offender to 20 years at hard labor without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for the distribution of cocaine, but the appellate court affirmed. The jury was presented with the direct testimony of an agent that he purchased one off-white rock object from defendant. The agent subsequently identified defendant both in a photographic lineup and in court as the person who sold him the drugs. The transaction was videotaped and played for the jury. Finally, the substance that the agent bought from defendant was tested and proved positive for the presence of cocaine. The jury also heard the evidence regarding the discrepancies in the time of the stop and the time of the transaction, as well as any conflicting testimony about the description of defendant. In reaching the guilty verdict, the jury obviously found the State's witnesses to have been more credible, a determination that was solely within the province of the trier of fact. The jury could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was guilty of the distribution of cocaine. Additionally, defendant was precluded from raising the issue of the admission of the crime lab report for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment and ordered the district court to supplement the appellate record with the ruling on defendant's motion to reconsider sentence.

 

1155 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


S. Silica of La., Inc. v. La. Ins. Guar. Ass'n


NUMBER 2006 CA 2023


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006 2023 (La.App. 1 Cir. 7/13/07); 966 So. 2d 45; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1449



July 13, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Concurring Opinion Dated October 24, 2007. As Amended October 25, 2007.
Review granted by Southern Silica of La., Inc. v. La. Ins. Guar. Ass'n, 969 So. 2d 615, 2007 La. LEXIS 2853 (La., 2007)
Reversed by S. Silica of La., Inc. v. La. Ins. Guar. Ass'n, 979 So. 2d 460, 2008 La. LEXIS 792 (La., Apr. 8, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Docket Number 517,372. Honorable Kay Bates, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, RENDERED, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, granted summary judgment in favor of defendant Louisiana Insurance Guaranty Association (LIGA) on plaintiff mining companies' suit for declaratory judgment seeking a judicial determination to resolve whether the 2004 amendments to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386 applied to the companies' accrued and pending claims retroactively. The companies appealed.


OVERVIEW: The companies argued that the trial court failed in retroactively applying the amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386(A). The appellate court noted that the amendment to § 22:1386 created a new obligation or liability vis-a-vis the companies' solvent insurers by requiring that they provide coverage and pay claims for periods of alleged exposure for the insurer's policy years when they had no contractual obligation or statutory duty to provide coverage. The amendments effected a substantive change in the law with regard to payment of claims. By retroactive application of the statute, the legislature impaired the private contractual rights of the companies and it insurers by requiring the companies to assert claims against their solvent insurers, who could have provided insurance up to thirty years from the date of the alleged exposure for a brief period of time, and to demand coverage for claims for a period where insurers had no contract and did not receive premiums. Retroactive application of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386 would deprive the companies of vested property rights acquired, asserted, and accrued as well as duties owed by LIGA prior to the passage of the legislation.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded and judgment was declared that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386 did not apply retroactively in the matter.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF CALCASIEU, DOCKET NO. 97-4329. HONORABLE J. DAVID PAINTER, DISTRICT JUDGE. ON REMAND FROM THE LOUISIANA SUPREME COURT, DOCKET NO. 2006-2968.

DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, claimants, challenged the judgment of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Calcasieu, Louisiana, determining the constitutionality of the limitation on recovery in medical malpractice actions found in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B), in the action with defendants, State of Louisiana, Louisiana Patient's Compensation Fund Oversight Board and medical center.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court previously held the $ 500,000 statutory limit on recovery of damages in medical malpractice actions was unconstitutional in failing to provide the claimants an "adequate remedy." OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and remanded with instructions to allow the claimants to specially plead the unconstitutionality of the statute and for full litigation of the issues at a contradictory hearing.

State v. Horton


No. 42,199-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,199 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/20/07); 962 So. 2d 459; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1315



June 20, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Horton, 2008 La. LEXIS 199 (La., Jan. 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 238,749. Honorable Ramona Emanuel, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with pornography involving juveniles, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.1. After a jury trial, he was found guilty and sentenced to seven years at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. He appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took his computer (the tower portion containing the hard drive) to a store. He instructed a computer technician there to install a new hard drive, but not to remove the old hard drive; he also agreed to a suggestion that the computer be physically cleaned. Defendant challenged the private search of his computer by the store's employees, and moved to quash the bill of information that charged him with pornography involving juveniles, claiming that the statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.1, was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. Defendant alleged that the district court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence obtained from the search of his computer which was subsequently used to obtain a warrant for the search of his residence. He contended that his right to privacy under La. Const. art. I, § 5 was violated by the unauthorized private search of his computer by the employees who, in turn, reported their findings to police. Nevertheless, defendant was not constitutionally protected from a reasonable search by the store employees. Further, defendant's sentence was not disproportionate to the offense.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentences were affirmed.

 

1159 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


NUMBER 2006 CA 2024


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006 2024 (La.App. 1 Cir. 6/8/07); 965 So. 2d 866; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1184



June 8, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Johnson v. State, 967 So. 2d 507, 2007 La. LEXIS 2563 (La., Nov. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Nineteen Judicial District Court. In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 541528. Honorable Curtis A. Calloway, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of an order from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which granted an exception of no cause of action filed by defendants, the State of Louisiana, the Governor of Louisiana, the Attorney General for the State of Louisiana, and the Secretary of State and Chief Election Officer for the State of Louisiana, in an action attacking the system for electing judges.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a black voter, filed a petition for declaratory and injunctive relief against defendants. Plaintiff attacked the system for electing judges to the Baton Rouge City Court on the basis that it violated the equal protection and due process clauses of the Louisiana Constitution. The trial court granted defendants' exception of no cause of action. On appeal, the court concluded that plaintiff did not have a cause of action under Louisiana law to contest the election of judges to the Baton Rouge City Court on the basis of the one-person, one-vote principle. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1952(4)(b) and (c), which established that five Baton Rouge City Court judges would be elected from two election districts, was facially neutral, and did not discriminate against black voters on its face. The mere fact that the State failed to pass redistricting legislation in light of updated census data was insufficient to state a cause of action for purposeful discrimination. Plaintiff failed to state a cause of action under La. Const. art. I, § 2. No Louisiana case or statute gave a voter the right to demand that judicial election districts be reassessed and redrawn at regular intervals.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1160 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lonzo


NO. 06-KA-945


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


06-945 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/29/07); 960 So. 2d 290; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1064



May 29, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication August 8, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 04-7311, DIVISION "J". HONORABLE STEPHEN J. WINDHORST, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "J" (Louisiana), denied defendant's motion to quash the bill of information. Defendant withdrew her plea of guilty and pled guilty as charged, reserving her right to appeal the denial of her motion to quash. Defendant subsequently filed a motion for appeal that was granted.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(E) was unconstitutionally vague. However, the appellate court found that former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(E)(5) was not unconstitutionally vague. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(B)(3) was a penalty provision for violations of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A), which provided that it was unlawful for any person knowingly or intentionally to possess marijuana with the intent to distribute it. The language of former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(E)(5), when read in conjunction with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A) and (B)(3) as required, was sufficiently clear. Thus, the State did not err by using defendant's prior conviction for possession with the intent to distribute marijuana as a predicate offense to enhance her current charge of possession of marijuana to second offense possession of marijuana. Because former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(E)(5) clearly and unambiguously provided that a conviction for possession with intent to distribute marijuana could be considered as a prior conviction for second or subsequent offenders, the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to quash the bill of information.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Mickel


NO. 07-KA-47


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


07-47 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/29/07); 961 So. 2d 516; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1094



May 29, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication August 8, 2007.
Writ denied by State v. Mickel, 973 So. 2d 732, 2008 La. LEXIS 38 (La., 2008)
Writ denied by Mickel v. Cain, 2013 La. LEXIS 2095 (La., Sept. 27, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 03-5247, DIVISION ''N''. HONORABLE HANS J. LILJEBERG, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Jefferson Parish (Louisiana) of armed robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his challenge for cause of a potential juror should have been granted because the juror demonstrated bias in favor of the prosecution and his views towards defendant's failure to testify at trial suggested an inability to render judgment according to law. The court of appeal disagreed. A complete reading of the voir dire showed that the juror was a victim of crime and had several friends who were either prosecutors or police officers. He admitted his bias toward the State. However, when questioned by the trial judge, the juror stated that he would do his best to give defendant his day in court and weigh the evidence in a fair and impartial way. The juror also stated that he understood that the State had the burden to prove defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The juror, although exhibiting a pro-prosecution bias, demonstrated his willingness and ability to be impartial in reviewing the evidence and deciding the case. When asked if he would find defendant guilty because he did not testify, the juror stated affirmatively that he would not. Therefore, the trial court did not err by denying the challenge for cause.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded for the trial court to correct the minute entry to conform with the transcript.

State v. Lee


2005 KA 0456


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 0456 (La.App. 1 Cir. 5/16/07); 964 So. 2d 967; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1035



May 16, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Lee, 976 So. 2d 109, 2008 La. LEXIS 156 (La., 2008)
Writ denied by State v. Lee, 977 So. 2d 896, 2008 La. LEXIS 492 (La., 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Lee v. Louisiana, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 6598 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 18<th> Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of West Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana Trial Court No. 034925, Division "B". Honorable Robin Free, Judge Presiding.
State v. Lee, 877 So. 2d 997, 2004 La. LEXIS 2385 (La., July 30, 2004)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 18th Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of West Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, convicting him of second-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for killing the victim by cutting her throat. On appeal, the court held that the eleven to one jury verdict was not unconstitutional because under both state and federal jurisprudence, a criminal conviction by a less than unanimous jury did not violate a defendant's right to trial by jury specified by the Sixth Amendment. The trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress DNA evidence because there was a reasonable and sufficiently individualized suspicion that defendant may have been involved in other crimes to justify the issuance of the subpoena duces tecum to take the DNA sample from him. The means and procedure employed in obtaining the sample were not unreasonable, as an officer swabbed defendant's cheeks in his home and defendant was not taken into custody at that time. Even though the trial court erred by admitting into evidence several of defendant's prior crimes, the error was harmless the evidence against defendant, including the DNA evidence linking him to the instant crime, his proximity to the crime scene, a boot print, knife wounds, and a telephone call from the victim's phone to defendant's former place of employment.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Trackling


NO. 2007-KA-0068


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2007-0068 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/16/07); 958 So. 2d 1209; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1118



May 16, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 19, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM Criminal District Court Orleans Parish. NO. 431-778, Section "H". Honorable Camille Buras, Judge.
State v. Trackling, 930 So. 2d 60, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 940 (La.App. 4 Cir., Feb. 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's conviction and five-year sentence for attempted sexual battery was reversed on appeal. On certiorari review, the matter was reversed and remanded for further consideration. Upon the State's filing of a multiple bill of information, the Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, adjudicated defendant as a fourth offender, vacated the original sentence, and resentenced him to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended his life sentence as a multiple offender was constitutionally excessive as to him because of his speech problems and limited intellectual functioning. The appellate court disagreed, finding that while defendant committed his offense after the effective date of the amendments reducing the mandatory minimum sentence for habitual offenders, a life sentence was still the minimum that could be imposed under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(i)(ii) because the instant felony conviction and two of his prior felony convictions were crimes of violence under La. Rev. Stat. 14:2(13). Furthermore, no evidence was presented to show there were mitigating factors that overwhelmed the presumption that the legislatively-mandated sentence was appropriate. A report generated for the competency hearing did not indicate that defendant suffered from any problems that prevented him from avoiding criminal conduct, and his criminal history could not be explained by either his disability or his lack of intelligence. The record clearly established that defendant was a sexual predator whose victims included children and who had a propensity for violence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Ragas


NO. 07-KA-3


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


07-3 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/15/07); 960 So. 2d 266; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1029



May 15, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication August 8, 2007.
Writ denied by State v. Ragas, 973 So. 2d 732, 2008 La. LEXIS 36 (La., 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ragas v. Louisiana, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 6510 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 03-7911, DIVISION "J". HONORABLE STEPHEN J. WINDHORST, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State ex rel. Ragas v. State, 916 So. 2d 1040, 2005 La. LEXIS 2603 (La., Dec. 9, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, convicting him of armed robbery, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64, and sentencing him to 30 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: An individual wearing black clothing and a mask robbed a restaurant. The gun left at the scene was traced to defendant's wife, who had reported the gun stolen. During a police interview, the wife admitted that defendant forced her to falsely report the gun stolen, and admitted that a week after she reported the theft, defendant told her he committed the robbery. The appellate court ruled that the evidence was sufficient for the jury to conclude that defendant was armed with a dangerous weapon. The restaurant manager testified defendant had a bag over his hand pointing at her when he ordered her to open the safe, and she automatically assumed there was a gun in the bag because of the way defendant was holding it. The manager did exactly what defendant wanted because she was scared, nervous, and shaking. Defendant clearly created an "atmosphere of intimidation." Defendant's wife's gun was found in front of the safe, and it was not there prior to the robbery. Also, defendant admitted in his statement to the police that he left the gun in the restaurant after the robbery. Furthermore, the 30-year sentence was not constitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Ford


No. 41,949-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,949 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/09/07); 957 So. 2d 311; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 885



May 9, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Ford, 2008 La. LEXIS 34 (La., Jan. 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 130,476. Honorable Parker Self, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to one count of attempted first degree murder. The Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana, sentenced defendant to serve 45 years at hard labor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Before taking the guilty plea, the trial court ascertained that defendant was 20 years old, had a 10th-grade education, and the ability to read, write, and understand the English language. Defendant asserted that the trial court's colloquy was insufficient because it only informed him of his right to cross-examine, and he asserted that the right of confrontation included the right to see as well as cross-examine the witnesses against him. The appellate court ruled that while the trial court and State should be advised that the better practice was to inform defendant of his right to a trial by jury at the time he pled guilty, the record supported a finding that defendant was aware of his right to a trial by jury and that his guilty plea was made with the knowledge that he was waiving his right to a trial by jury when he pled guilty. It was common sense that cross-examination was an adversarial act and necessarily included the right to see the witness. The circumstances in the case reflected an understanding and waiver of the right of confrontation. Also, defendant's sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Franklin


No. 42,055-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


42,055 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/09/07); 956 So. 2d 823; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 901



May 9, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Amended by, Rehearing denied by State v. Melecia, 956 So. 2d 823, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1281 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2007)
Writ denied by State v. Melecia, 2008 La. LEXIS 86 (La., Jan. 11, 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana) of two counts of forgery and one count of felony theft. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain her conviction for felony theft. The court of appeal disagreed. The State proved by direct evidence, including witness testimony and physical evidence, that defendant took something of value ($ 120,000) from the bank without its consent and had the intent to deprive the bank of the money permanently. Two different bank officials testified that defendant admitted that she took the $ 120,000 in increments from the vault and spent it all. Further, defendant admitted at trial that she falsified general ledger entries to conceal the $ 120,000 shortage, which shortage was verified by an audit. The evidence indicated that defendant was the vault teller and had access to the funds missing from the vault. There was also direct evidence that the vault count on Friday was based on the general ledger entries, which defendant herself admitted at trial that she, as vault teller, falsified to reflect that the $ 120,000 shortage did not exist. Both tellers who participated in the "intervening" count testified that they did not take the money.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
