Wingrave v. Hebert


NO. 2006-CA-1240


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


06-1240 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/9/07); 964 So. 2d 385; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1107



May 9, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication September 27, 2007.
Rehearing granted by Wingrave v. Hebert, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1478 (La.App. 4 Cir., July 25, 2007)
Writ denied by Wingrave v. Hebert, 2007 La. LEXIS 2509 (La., Nov. 2, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM Civil District Court, Orleans Parish. NO. 99-17291, Division "B". Honorable Rosemary Ledet, Judge.
Wingrave v. Hebert, 852 So. 2d 3, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2210 (La.App. 4 Cir., July 16, 2003)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff terminated employee sought review of an order from the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which awarded summary judgment to defendants, an employer, a fiance, and employees, in an action for damages for embarrassment, emotional distress, marital problems, embarrassment in the community, loss of reputation, and defamation.


OVERVIEW: The employee received a telephone call from a coworker at his home after a work function and a night of drinking. The employee and the coworker were romantically involved at the time. Unbeknownst to either the employee or the coworker, the coworker's fiance had illegally tapped her telephone and recorded the conversation. During the conversation, the employee allegedly threatened his supervisor because of a negative evaluation. The finance contacted the supervisor and informed her of the threat. The employee was terminated. The employee brought an action against defendants. The trial court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court found that genuine issues of material fact existed as to whether defendants knew or had reason to know that the information regarding the threat was obtained in violation of the Louisiana Electronic Surveillance Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1303. Further, there were genuine issues of material fact as to whether the employee's statements constituted a matter of public concern. Whether "any reasonable person" would consider the statements threatening was a factual determination to be made by the trier of fact.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1168 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Hooks v. Kennedy


2006 CA 0541 and 2006 CW 0100


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006 0541 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/04/07); 961 So. 2d 425; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 826



May 4, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Hooks v. Kennedy, 2007 La. LEXIS 2579 (La., Nov. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and For the Parish of East Baton Rouge State of Louisiana. Docket No. 496,445. Honorable Timothy E. Kelley, Judge Presiding.
Hooks v. Kennedy, 913 So. 2d 833, 2005 La. LEXIS 2498 (La., Sept. 27, 2005)



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED; PEREMPTORY EXCEPTION RAISING THE OBJECTION OF NO CAUSE OF ACTION SUSTAINED, AND CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees property owner et al. brought a class action suit against appellant State, seeking just compensation for property taken and a declaration that Louisiana's Unclaimed Property law, La. rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:151 et seq., was unconstitutional. The Nineteenth Judicial District Court of East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, certified a class and denied the State's exception of no right of action as to the owner. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State challenged the judgment of certification and filed a writ application objecting to the trial court's denial of its exceptions. Even accepting all the petition's well pled allegations of fact as true, the appellate court held that the threshold assertion of the certified class, that a "taking" occurred when the State exercised its statutory custodial rights, was not based on well pled facts, but on a legal conclusion, clothed as fact. The correctness of that conclusion was contradicted by the Louisiana Uniform Unclaimed Property Act of 1997, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:151 et seq., and the jurisprudence. The State's exercise of its statutorily imposed custody, and the legislature's decision to award owners only the interest provided for in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:163, did not equate to a "taking." In the absence of any actionable "taking," there was no basis to claim a constitutionally mandated payment of "just compensation." As such, the appellate court concluded that the trial court erred in denying the State's exception of no cause of action.


OUTCOME: The State's exception of no cause of action was granted and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1169 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tensley


No. 41,726-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,726 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/04/07); 955 So. 2d 227; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 640



April 4, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Tensley, 969 So. 2d 629, 2007 La. LEXIS 2822 (La., 2007)
Appeal after remand at State v. Falcon, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1821 (La.App. 2 Cir., Oct. 28, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 03-F1297. Honorable Benjamin Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana) found defendant boyfriend guilty of second degree murder while engaged in cruelty to a juvenile and received a mandatory life sentence. In a motion for a post verdict judgment of acquittal, defendant mother's conviction for second degree murder was reduced to manslaughter. Both defendants appealed. The State appealed the granting of defendant mother's motion.


OVERVIEW: The evidence was sufficient to convict defendants of second degree murder while engaged in cruelty to a juvenile under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 14:30.1 and 14:93 because (1) the medical evidence established that blunt force trauma was continually visited upon the child for a lengthy time period; (2) witnesses had on more than one occasion instructed defendants that something was wrong with the child; (3) the medical evidence of the child's painful traumatic events established the neglect and mistreatment element of the crime; (4) after the child was taken to the hospital in a comatose state, defendant mother twice made an incriminating statement to defendant boyfriend, who then put his hand over her mouth and told her to shut up; and (5) each defendant's statement that the other defendant gave proper care to the child and that the child exhibited no alarming symptoms of injury until the morning of his death raised the inference that both were directly and intentionally involved in abusing the child. However, the conflict of interest concerning the attorney's prior representation of both defendants violated their constitutional rights; thus, their convictions had to be reversed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed defendants' convictions and remanded the case to the trial court.

 

1170 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. H.B.


KA 06-1436


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


06-1436 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/04/07); 955 So. 2d 255; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 662



April 4, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 15, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ACADIA, NO. 67,176. April 4, 2007, Decided HONORABLE KRISTIAN DENNIS EARLES, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for one count of forcible rape, and two counts of aggravated rape of the victims - three children. The State amended all charges to second degree sexual battery, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.2. He pled guilty to all three amended charges. The Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Acadia (Louisiana), sentenced him to serve 10 years for each offense and ordered that the sentences run consecutively. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Because defendant committed the offenses against different victims on different dates, the appellate court found that, even though the offenses were joined in the same bill of indictment, they did not constitute the same act or transaction and were not part of a common scheme or plan. Moreover, because defendant was originally facing two counts of aggravated rape and one count of forcible rape, he received a substantial sentencing benefit. The 15-year maximum sentence for aggravated sexual battery under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.2 was immensely more lenient than the minimum sentence of life imprisonment for an aggravated rape conviction under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42 or the maximum sentence of 40 years for a forcible rape conviction under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42.1. Also, by pleading guilty to second degree sexual battery, defendant admitted that he acted with the specific intent to inflict serious bodily injury on the victims, thereby belying his assurance at sentencing that he had no intent to hurt the victims. Thus, the trial court did not err in ordering that defendant's sentences run consecutively, and his sentences were not excessive under La. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction; however, the appellate court amended defendant's sentences to reflect that he was not eligible for diminution of sentence pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:537 and instructed the trial court to note the amendment in the court minutes. In all other respects, defendant's sentences were affirmed.

 

1171 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Richard v. Bd. of Supervisors


2006 CA 0927


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006 0927 (La.App. 1 Cir. 3/28/07); 960 So. 2d 953; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 562



March 28, 2007, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court In and For the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 450,606, Division "H". Honorable William A. Morvant, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED IN PART AS AMENDED; REVERSED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND JUDGMENT RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant appealed the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court In and For the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Division "H" (Louisiana), finding that defendant university employee violated the claimant's civil rights but awarded her only nominal damages of $1.00 and finding that defendant board of supervisors did not retaliate against her. Defendant university appealed the assessment of nominal damages against it and its employee.


OVERVIEW: After roughly five years on the job where the claimant received positive evaluations, she (1) was threatened with termination by her employer, (2) learned that her employer had reported her difficulties at the university peace officer basic training academy to other potential academies, and (3) experienced mental and emotional problems to the extent that she required medical attention for extensive stress, a condition that incapacitated her from working for at least one month beginning in January 1998 and for another beginning in April 1998. Thus, she showed actual injuries that resulted directly from the employee's letter, which caused a violation of the claimant's rights pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Accordingly, she was entitled to compensation for her injuries. In addition, Louisiana's public universities, including Louisiana State University (through its Board of Supervisors), were to be treated as arms of the State. As such, the university was not a person vulnerable to suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Thus, the jury's verdict against it had to be reversed. Finally, the claimant proved that the board of supervisors retaliated against her, and she was entitled to compensation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court amended the trial court's judgment to award the claimant $10,000 in damages and $10,000 in attorney's fees for the employee's violation of her civil rights; as amended, that portion of the judgment was affirmed. The trial court's judgment against the board of supervisors as an entity was reversed and she was award $5,000 in damages and $5,000 in attorney's fees. However, her claims against the university were dismissed.

 

1172 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dowden


No. 41,939-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,939 (La.App. 2 Cir. 03/28/07); 954 So. 2d 300; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 578



March 28, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Dowden, 2007 La. LEXIS 2557 (La., Nov. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 240,562. Honorable John D. Mosely, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of armed robbery. The court added an additional 5 years to defendant's sentence, to be served consecutively for defendant's use of a firearm. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeal disagreed. The victim's testimony was clear that a shotgun was used in the commission of the crime, and that testimony was corroborated to some extent by a witness's testimony that the victim, who appeared very shaken, told her immediately after the robbery that he was robbed at gunpoint. As for the description of the firearm, it was possible that the victim mistook the sawed-off shotgun as having two barrels because the barrel was sawed off to approximately the same length as the tube that held the shotgun shells. As a person unfamiliar with guns, the victim could have made that mistake, especially if there had been a magazine extension on the gun. Although there were inconsistencies in the victim's version of how the robbers entered his apartment, much of defendant's argument concerned inconsistencies with respect to the initial police report, which was not entered into evidence. The trial court, as the finder of fact, was within its discretion to credit the victim's testimony that a firearm was used and to discredit defendant's testimony in that regard.


OUTCOME: The additional 5-year sentence imposed for use of a firearm during the robbery was vacated. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

1173 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wilson


NO. 2006-KA-1421


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2006-1421 (La.App. 4 Cir. 3/28/07); 956 So. 2d 41; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 731



March 28, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 31, 2007.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Wilson v. State, 988 So. 2d 253, 2008 La. LEXIS 1588 (La., 2008)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Wilson v. Leblanc, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 123872 (E.D. La., Apr. 1, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 453-910, SECTION "L". HONORABLE TERRY ALARCON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, convicted and sentenced defendant on one count of unauthorized entry of an inhabited dwelling. The State filed a multiple bill, defendant's original sentence was vacated, and he was resentenced to 20 years at hard labor as a fourth offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction and raised several claims concerning his multiple offender adjudication. The appellate court found that the State established that defendant entered the victim's home early in the morning by breaking a window in a bedroom and, although the victim testified that she had ended her relationship with defendant a few weeks before the first burglary, defendant did not live in the residence. Given the circumstances of the case, as compared to other similar cases, the appellate court found the evidence was sufficient for the trial court to find that defendant entered the victim's house without authority. The appellate court also found that the State could bring the prior charges against defendant via a bill of information, even though he was exposed to a life sentence, because the allegations in the bill were not substantive charges but instead were merely prior convictions to be used to enhance his sentence. Defendant failed to preserve for review his other complaints regarding the multiple offender bill. Defendant's sentence was not excessive as he received the minimum sentence for a fourth offender.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1174 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Sharp v. Belle Maison Nursing Home, Inc.


NUMBER 2006 CA 1107


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006 1107 (La.App. 1 Cir. 3/23/07); 960 So. 2d 166; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 541



March 23, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in full at Sharp v. Belle Maison Nursing Home, Inc., 953 So. 2d 207, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2099 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 21st Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Tangipahoa State of Louisiana. Suit Number 2004-002568. The Honorable Zorraine M. Waguespack, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 21st Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Tangipahoa, Louisiana, granted defendant coroner's peremptory exception in plaintiff family members' negligence action against the coroner for failing to take an x-ray of the decedent's injured knee and failing to order and/or conduct an autopsy on the decedent. The family members appealed.


OVERVIEW: The family members argued that the coroner was legally obligated to perform an autopsy under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:1563(B)(1) because there was a reasonable probability that the violation of a criminal statute by the nursing home staff contributed to the decedent's death. The appellate court found that the allegations of the family members' petition did not give rise to any cause of action against the coroner. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:1563(B)(1) did not impose a duty on the coroner to conduct an autopsy for the benefit of private individuals, and therefore, the failure to conduct an autopsy did not give rise to a cause of action for damages to private individuals such as the family members. The coroner's agent investigated the decedent's death, noted the condition of her left leg, and was apprised that her physician concluded that she died from a heart attack. The family members failed to allege facts to show that there was a basis for the coroner to believe that there was a reasonable probability that the violation of a criminal statute contributed to the decedent's death.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1175 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Devall v. Starns


2006 CA 2155


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006-2155 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/21/07); 960 So. 2d 75; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 491



March 21, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Writ denied by Devall v. Starns, 959 So. 2d 513, 2007 La. LEXIS 1569 (La., June 22, 2007)



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT RENDERED DECLARING THE CITY OF CENTRAL INCORPORATED AS OF JULY 11, 2005.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a representative of city incorporators, sought to have upheld the incorporation's validity under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 33:1-7, challenging a decision of the 19th Judicial District Court Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which found that a judgment rendered prior to the incorporation, declaring a provision barring the incorporation to be unconstitutional and contrary to state law, was null and void.


OVERVIEW: Previously, residents of the then-unincorporated area of the parish obtained a judgment that a section of the parish's government plan was unconstitutional. That section provided that no additional city, town, or village could be incorporated in the parish; the trial court found that section of the plan to be null and void. Thereafter, a special election was held, and the city was incorporated. Subsequently, the trial court entered an order nullifying the previous judgment, finding that it was a "friendly," if not collusive, proceeding. However, it did not rule on the validity of the election. Petitioners attacked the trial court's ruling that the earlier judgment was a nullity; moreover, they argued that, even if it was a nullity, it could not serve as a basis to invalidate the incorporation. The state appellate court agreed. After 1984, pursuant to La. Const. art. VI, § 8, the section of the government plan in issue was unconstitutional. Thus, even if the effect of the judgment nullifying the previous judgment was to put that section back on the books, it was not enforceable, pursuant to La. Const. art. VI, § 2, because it conflicted with the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The appellate court entered a judgment declaring the city incorporated.

 

1176 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Historic Restoration, Inc. v. RSUI Indem. Co., L.L.C.


NO. 2006-CA-1178


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2006-1178 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/21/07); 955 So. 2d 200; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 729



March 21, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication May 25, 2007.
Writ denied by Historic Restoration, Inc. v. RSUI Indem. Co., 959 So. 2d 497, 2007 La. LEXIS 1517 (La., June 22, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM Civil District Court, Orleans Parish. NO. 2006-4990, Division "D-16". Honorable Lloyd J. Medley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance company sued appellee indemnity company and alleged that the indemnity company failed to comply with Emergency Rule 23 promulgated after Hurricanes Katrina and Rita. The Civil District Court, Orleans Paris, Louisiana granted the insurance company's motion for a preliminary injunction seeking to enjoin the indemnity company from changing the terms and conditions of its existing insurance policy. The indemnity company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The indemnity company asserted an assignment of error regarding the trial court's finding of an alleged violation of Emergency Rule (ER) 23, by granting injunctive relief. The appellate court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it granted the insurance company's motion for a preliminary injunction enjoining the indemnity company from changing the terms and conditions of its existing insurance policy where: (1) given the multiplicity of possible losses, including insurance, mortgage, and partnership agreements, goodwill, reputation, and competitive edge in the marketplace, the possible harm was egregious and therefore, the harm to the insurance company could not have been measured by pecuniary standards once the contracts were violated and the insurance company's reputation was lost; (2) the harm to the insurance company outweighed the inconvenience to the indemnity company; (3) the public interest was served by issuing preliminary injunctions for violations of ER 23; and (4) the indemnity company violated ER 23 by increasing the premium without substantiating the increase with its method of using objective criteria with standards prior to the hurricanes.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1177 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


06-1247


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


06-1247 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/07/07); 953 So. 2d 91; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 410



March 7, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Williams, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 811 (La.App. 3 Cir., Apr. 25, 2007)
Writ denied by State v. Williams, 2007 La. LEXIS 2650 (La., Nov. 21, 2007)
Writ granted by, Reversed by State v. Williams, 2007 La. LEXIS 2726 (La., Dec. 7, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CONCORDIA, NO. 06-021MH, HONORABLE SHARON MARCHMAN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of Concordia (Louisiana), convicting her of filing a false record in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:133 and sentencing her to five years at hard labor, with all but 18 months suspended, and five years of supervised probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of filing a false absentee ballot. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because: (1) the ballot affidavit included a certification of truth that had to be signed by the voter; (2) signing as a witness that a signed certification of truth was sworn to and subscribed in the signer's presence, when in fact it was not, constituted a false representation for purposes of the statute; (3) La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:306(E)(2) was controlling; and (4) the purported witnesses themselves admitted that they did not actually see the voter sign the ballot affidavits. However, the court held that defendant's five-year sentence with only 18 months not suspended was excessive because the trial court did not give adequate consideration to defendant's health, age, and personal history by not imposing a longer period of suspension. The trial court's concern that defendant would commit a similar crime was adequately addressed by the five-year period of probation imposed, during which time defendant would risk serving the entire incarceration portion of her sentence should she engage in further criminal activity.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, but her sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing and for a hearing on whether she was indigent.

 

1178 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Houston v. Springville Cemetery Ass'n


No. 41,869-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,869 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/28/07); 953 So. 2d 905; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 313



February 28, 2007, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Writ denied by Houston v. Springville Cemetery Ass'n, 955 So. 2d 1285, 2007 La. LEXIS 1177 (La., May 11, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff husband challenged a judgment of the Thirty-Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Red River, Louisiana, which ruled in favor of defendant cemetery in the husband's action to enjoin the cemetery's orders to remove certain structures from the husband's family gravesite.


OVERVIEW: The husband's wife was buried in the cemetery, and the husband erected an arbor and canopy structure over the entire family plot with the cemetery's approval. Citing complaints, the cemetery three years later told the husband to remove the structures and told him that a water hydrant used by the husband was being relocated. On appeal, the court found that under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 8:202, the cemetery was private property subject to the special public use involving cemeteries. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 8:204 enumerated the special authority that the cemetery had over the use, care, control, management, restriction and protection of the cemetery as private property subject to public use. The cemetery had authority to regulate the uniformity, class and kind of all markers, monuments and other structures within the cemetery, as recognized in § 8:204(2). The cemetery's action were taken in a reasonable manner with advance notice provided to the husband, and the decision to require removal of the structures was not arbitrary or capricious. The husband's special right in the property as a relative of those buried in the cemetery was therefore subject to the cemetery's maintenance authority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1179 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Matherne v. Broussard


NUMBER 2006 CA 0838


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006 0838 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/14/07); 959 So. 2d 975; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 295



February 14, 2007, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appealed from the Thirty-second Judicial District Court. In and for the Parish of Terrebonne State of Louisiana. Docket Number 143,052. Honorable Randall L. Bethancourt, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED; AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Twenty years after his uncle's death, appellant nephew filed suit claiming an interest in succession property and that appellees, his uncle's widow and their two daughters, intentionally concealed that his uncle was actually his biological father. The Thirty-Second Judicial District Court, Terrebonne Parish, Louisiana, sustained the widow's and the daughters' peremptory exception of prescription and dismissed the claims. The nephew appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the nephew asserted that the trial court erred in his dismissing his claims as untimely under former La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 209. Alternatively, the nephew argued that his claim for intentional concealment was one sounding in tort; therefore, it was exempt from the peremptive period pursuant to the tort exception contained in art. 209. The appellate court disagreed, holding first that the time limitation in art. 209 was peremptive. Accordingly, the nephew's argument that the trial court erred in failing to find that the period was prescriptive and subject to the doctrine of contra non valentem had no merit. The appellate court further found that the nephew's action was one to establish filiation in an effort to recover lost succession rights. Notwithstanding his creative claim for mental pain and suffering, the nephew essentially sought a portion of the former succession property, or, alternatively, to receive the value of that property in "tort" damages. As such, the appellate court found that his claims were not exempt from the peremptive period by virtue of the tort exception in art. 209.


OUTCOME: The judgment was amended to state that the peremptory exception raising the objection of prescription filed by two of the appellees was sustained, and the nephew's claims against them were dismissed. In all other respects, the judgment was affirmed.

 

1180 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lauff


NO. 06-KA-717


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


06-717 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/13/07); 953 So. 2d 813; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 226



February 13, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 3, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 03-7088, DIVISION ''G''. HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "G" (Louisiana), denied defendant's motion to suppress her statements and a motion to quash the indictment. After the State amended the indictment to charge defendant with manslaughter, she entered an Alford plea of guilty to manslaughter, reserving her right to appeal all pretrial motions. She was then sentenced to imprisonment at hard labor for 40 years. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: A dead baby boy was discovered in a trash receptacle at an apartment complex. Although the child's autopsy report indicated that there were levels of cocaine and alcohol in his body at birth, there was no evidence presented at the motion to suppress hearing that defendant was rendered incoherent by intoxication at any time she spoke to the police. Also, a detective denied that she cried for the duration of her two interviews and stated that she had her bouts and periods that she would cry, and sometimes she would not. Further, the detective testified that defendant understood she was under investigation for first degree murder, and that she was coherent and cooperative at the hospital, as well as during the successive recorded statements. Additionally, defendant signed waiver of rights forms prior to making both recorded statements, indicating that she had been advised of her constitutional rights and that she wanted to waive them. Thus, the trial judge could have concluded that defendant's statements were freely and voluntarily given and did not err in denying her motion to suppress her statements to the detective.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence; however, the appellate court remanded the case to the trial court with instructions for the trial court to correctly inform defendant of the prescriptive provisions for seeking post-conviction relief.

 

1181 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Shaw v. Dupuy


2006 CU 0546


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006 0546 (La.App. 1 Cir. 2/9/07); 961 So. 2d 5; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 243



February 9, 2007, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Writ denied by Shaw v. Dupuy, 951 So. 2d 1092, 2007 La. LEXIS 702 (La., Mar. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT (NUMBER 105,176, DIVISION "H"), PARISH OF LIVINGSTON STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE ZORRAINE M. WAGUESPACK, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff maternal grandparents filed a petition against defendant daughter, requesting that they be awarded specific visitation with their daughter's minor children. The Twenty-First Judicial District, Parish of Livingston (Louisiana) granted the grandparents specific visitation privileges with the children. The mother appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued that the trial court erred in finding the requisite extraordinary circumstances required by La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 136B. Accepting only the grandparents' version of the basis for the split with their daughter as true, the appellate court found as a matter of law it was insufficient to constitute the highly unusual set of facts necessary to amount to the extraordinary circumstances justifying interference in the mother's right to make decisions concerning the care, custody, and control of her children. Specifically, the record was devoid of any allegations or proof of the unfitness of the mother. Moreover, the inability of the mother and the grandparents to communicate or agree on many issues or the mother's alleged concern for an encroachment on an inheritance she believed she and her children were entitled to receive from the grandparents did not amount to extraordinary circumstances as required by article 136B to support an award of visitation to the relatives not granted custody of the children.


OUTCOME: The judgment awarding the grandparents visitation was reversed. Appeal costs were assessed to the grandparents.

 

1182 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Kinchen v. Livingston Parish Council


2006 CA 0301


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006 0301 (La.App. 1 Cir. 2/9/07); 959 So. 2d 896; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 245



February 9, 2007, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Writ granted by Kinchen v. Livingston Parish Council, 957 So. 2d 141, 2007 La. LEXIS 1299 (La., 2007)
Reversed by, Remanded by Kinchen v. Livingston Parish Council, 2007 La. LEXIS 2322 (La., Oct. 16, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff-appellant taxpayer appealed a judgment of the Twenty-First Judicial District Court, Parish of Livingston (Louisiana), sustaining a peremptory exception raising the objection of no cause of action filed by defendants against the taxpayer's petition, which sought, inter alia, class certification, damages, a refund, pre-judgment interest, attorney fees, and declaratory relief pronouncing a document transaction tax unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The objection that the petition failed to state a cause of action was properly raised by the peremptory exception. The trial court correctly applied La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2110 to conclude that the taxpayer was afforded a procedure to test the validity of the document transaction tax and that she did not timely avail herself of that remedy. Thus, because her petition failed to allege conformity with the procedure set forth in § 47:2110, it failed to state a cause of action and the trial court correctly sustained defendants' exception.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the dismissal of the taxpayer's petition. Appeal costs were assessed to the taxpayer.

State v. Semien


06-841


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


06-841 (La.App. 3 Cir. 1/31/07); 948 So. 2d 1189; 2007 La. App. LEXIS 126



January 31, 2007, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 16, 2007.
Writ denied by State v. Semien, 965 So. 2d 397, 2007 La. LEXIS 2290 (La., 2007)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Semien v. Warden, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 131238 (W.D. La., Apr. 17, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF ST. LANDRY, NO. 02-K-0612-B. HONORABLE ELLIS J. DAIGLE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Twenty-Seventh Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Landry (Louisiana), found defendant guilty of distribution of cocaine, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967. Defendant was sentenced to 12 years at hard labor, with the first two years to be served without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant's motion to reconsider his sentence was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: There was evidence that the jury was reasonable in finding that defendant was positively identified, including that a detective involved in the drug buy made an in-court identification of defendant as the seller. Defendant contended that the 12-year sentence imposed upon him as a first-time offender convicted of distribution of approximately 1/10th of a gram of crack was excessive under the Eight Amendment and La. Const. art. I, § 20. Although defendant was a first felony offender, the appellate court did not find the sentence imposed upon him by the trial court was excessive because (1) although defendant was a first time felony offender, he had been arrested in the mean time for aggravated assault in which he allegedly possessed a gun and pointed it at other individuals; (2) there was undue risk that during a suspended sentence or probation, he would commit another crime; (3) he was in need of correctional treatment; (4) a lesser sentence would deprecate the seriousness of his crime; (5) there were no mitigating circumstances and no remorse; and (6) the sentence was less than half of the allowable maximum sentence of 30 years under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(B)(4)(b).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1184 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Price


2005 KA 2514


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 2514 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/28/06); 952 So. 2d 112; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2999



December 28, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Price, 2008 La. LEXIS 427 (La., Feb. 22, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 410,629), PARISH OF TERREBONNE STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE JOHN R. WALKER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Thirty-Second Judicial District Court, Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana) of vehicular homicide. Defendant was sentenced to seven years at hard labor, with the first year of the sentence to be served without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant's motion to reconsider sentence was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. The evidence clearly established that defendant had an unlawful blood alcohol concentration while he was operating his vehicle. Five witnesses testified that they saw defendant drinking at a club that night before he wrecked his truck. Moreover, the crime lab report indicated that defendant had a blood alcohol concentration of .25 percent, more than three times the legal limit. The evidence further supported the jury's finding that defendant's highly-inebriated condition caused him to wreck his truck, which resulted in the death of the passenger. Defendant was doing "doughnuts" in his truck shortly before driving down the highway. The passenger told a friend over the telephone that defendant was "driving messed up" and that she was scared and she wanted defendant to pull over. Under those circumstances, given defendant's reckless manner of driving from the time he left the parking lot until the time he wrecked, it was reasonable for the jury to infer that his blood alcohol concentration contributed to his running off the road and losing control of his truck.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1185 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


2006 KA 0820


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2006 0820 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/28/06); 952 So. 2d 1; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 3005



December 28, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Smith, 964 So. 2d 352, 2007 La. LEXIS 2104 (La., Sept. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE SEVENTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 406581), PARISH OF LAFOURCHE. STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE ASHLY BRUCE SIMPSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: ORIGINAL CONVICTION AMENDED TO DISTRIBUTION OF MARIJUANA AND, AS AMENDED, THE CONVICTION IS AFFIRMED. SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED FOR SENTENCING ON AMENDED JUDGMENT OF CONVICTION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Seventeenth Judicial District Court, Parish of LaFourche (Louisiana) of distribution of marijuana as a second or subsequent offender. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeal found, inter alia, that defendant was improperly charged under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:982 because it did not define a crime. Consequently, since § 40:982 was a non-crime, and since La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966 contained no proscriptions against defendant's most recent conduct charged, i.e., distribution of marijuana, the second drug conviction portion of defendant's conviction and sentence was vacated. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in failing to grant his motion for a new trial based upon the fact that several jurors consumed alcoholic beverages during the trial proceedings. The court of appeal disagreed. In denying defendant's request to call the jurors in question, the trial court specifically noted there had been no threshold showing of impairment. The trial court found that absent such evidence of prejudice, there could be no substantial showing of deprivation of constitutional rights to require or allow members of the jury to testify. Under those circumstances, the trial court correctly applied the jury shield law under La. Code Evid. art. 606(B) and limited the testimony at the new trial hearing.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and was amended to a conviction for distribution of marijuana. The sentence was vacated, and the matter was remanded for sentencing on the amended judgment of conviction.

 

1186 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dozier


NO. 2006-KA-0621


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2006-0621 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/20/06); 949 So. 2d 502; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 3033



December 20, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 22, 2007.
Writ denied by State v. Dozier, 2007 La. LEXIS 2129 (La., Sept. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 455-403, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's motion to suppress the evidence was denied, the Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, convicted him of simple possession of cocaine. The State subsequently filed a multiple bill, and defendant was found to be a third offender and was sentenced to serve eight years at hard labor. Defendant's motion to reconsider sentence was denied, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred by finding him to be a third offender and by not strictly complying with the requirements of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. The appellate court disagreed, finding that under Apprendi, defendant's prior convictions were not required to be submitted to a jury. Further, there was no requirement that the State submit its documentation to the defense prior to the multiple bill hearing. And after pleading not guilty to the bill, defendant did not object or ask for a continuance in order to allow him time to investigate the allegations. Defendant and his counsel were allowed time to discuss the matter before he was found to be a third offender, and again defendant did not object to the documents or ask for a continuance. Although La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(D)(3) required the trial court to issue written reasons, the trial court's failure to file written reasons was harmless as its oral reasons showed that it had concluded that the State's documentation was sufficient to establish the prior convictions. The State more than adequately proved that defendant's prior guilty plea was voluntarily and knowingly given.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1187 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Batiste


NO. 2006-KA-0875


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2006-0875 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/20/06); 947 So. 2d 810; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 3045



December 20, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 22, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 451-652, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of manslaughter in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31 and sentenced him to 20 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant killed the victim during a dispute over a bet in a dominos game and defendant currently appealed his conviction for manslaughter and his 20-year sentence. The appellate court affirmed however, stating that the evidence was sufficient. Defendant was free to leave the scene, although $10 poorer. Instead, he armed himself and went back to the victim, eventually shooting him when the victim grabbed him. Defendant also contended that the trial court imposed an excessive sentence, but the appellate court disagreed. First, there was no indication that defendant filed a motion to reconsider the sentence as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1. Additionally, his former counsel's failure to object or file a motion to reconsider the sentence did not constitute the ineffective assistance of counsel because the sentence did not appear to have been excessive as compared to the sentences imposed and upheld in other manslaughter cases. The trial court complied with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 in that its reasons for the sentence were several pages long. Although the trial court did not enumerate that art. 894.1 factors, the record showed the basis for the sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1188 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Henderson


NO. 41,657-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,657 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/13/06); 945 So. 2d 194; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2809



December 13, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Henderson v. State, 2007 La. LEXIS 2419 (La., Nov. 2, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 229,044. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) of one count of forcible rape, two counts of aggravated rape, and three counts of aggravated kidnapping. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in refusing to grant his motion to sever the counts with regard to each victim. The court of appeal disagreed. The trial court, prosecution, and defense referred to the charges as separate offenses at all times during the proceedings. Additionally, both the prosecution and the defense compartmentalized their arguments according to the separate counts. The evidence against defendant on each count was not complex and was presented in an orderly fashion, allowing the jury to segregate the charges and the evidence. Each victim testified exclusively concerning the facts of her individual case. Defendant, his mother, and the DNA analyst were the only witnesses to testify with regard to all three of the rapes. Furthermore, the trial court specifically instructed the jury to consider the counts separately and render a verdict as to each count independently. Therefore, defendant was not prejudiced by the trial court denial of severance of the offenses. In addition, the evidence was sufficient to sustain all of defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1189 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Broussard v. Med. Protective Co.


06-331


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


06-0331 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/13/06); 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2813



December 13, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication January 18, 2007.
Later proceeding at Broussard v. Medical Protective Co., 952 So. 2d 813, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 291 (La.App. 3 Cir., Feb. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 2004-3397. HONORABLE R. RICHARD BRYANT, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a husband and a son, sued defendants, a doctor and his insurer, alleging medical malpractice regarding the treatment of a decedent. In the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, Louisiana, a jury found in favor of the doctor. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent presented to an emergency room complaining of chest pain, nausea, vomiting, and diarrhea. The decedent's father and five siblings died due to heart conditions. After ordering an EKG, lab tests, and chest x-rays, the doctor diagnosed the decedent as having gastroenteritis and prescribed a GI cocktail for her symptoms. This eased the decedent's nausea, but her chest pain did not subside. The doctor eventually gave the decedent a shot of morphine for her pain and discharged her. The decedent was never given any aspirin or nitroglycerine. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2794, the appellate court determined that the decision of the jury that the doctor did not fail to meet his standard of care was manifestly erroneous, unsupported by the record, and a result of jury confusion. The doctor clearly admitted that he breached the standard of care in failing to rule out cardiac ischemia, a potentially life threatening condition, prior to the decedent's discharge. Under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2164 and La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315.1, the appellate court awarded appropriate amounts for the survival action and wrongful death damages.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the judgment of the trial court, rendered judgment in favor of plaintiffs, and awarded, inter alia, wrongful death damages, survival damages, and interest. Costs of the trial, expert witness fees, and costs of the appeal were assessed against defendants.

State v. Cloud


06-877


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


06-877 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/13/06); 946 So. 2d 265; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2821



December 13, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 18, 2007.
Writ denied by State v. Cloud, 2007 La. LEXIS 2009 (La., Sept. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ALLEN, NO. 2003-1773. HONORABLE PATRICIA C. COLE, DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. Cloud, 893 So. 2d 220, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 140 (La.App. 3 Cir., Feb. 2, 2005)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION FOR INDECENT BEHAVIOR REVERSED AND SENTENCE VACATED. CONVICTIONS FOR MOLESTATION OF A JUVENILE, SEXUAL BATTERY, AND ORAL SEXUAL BATTERY AFFIRMED. SENTENCES VACATED AND REMANDED TO TRIAL COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand, defendant was convicted of sexual battery, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.1, oral sexual battery, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.3, molestation of a juvenile, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2, and indecent behavior with a juvenile, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81, by the Thirty-Third Judicial District Court, Parish of Allen (Louisiana). Defendant challenged the convictions and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was not subjected to double jeopardy where his guilty plea convictions and sentence were vacated on appeal. He was not deprived of due process when he received harsher treatment and a longer sentence after successfully appealing his prior guilty pleas as the parties were in the same position as they were prior to acceptance of the plea bargain. Defendant's constitutional protections against multiple punishments was not violated as additional evidence was offered at trial showing that he committed lewd and lascivious behavior, thereby supporting the molestation conviction. However, the indecent behavior conviction subjected defendant to double jeopardy as the same evidence used to prove molestation was used to prove indecent behavior. There was no appearance of retaliation in sentencing as defendant was placed in the same position after the original sentence was vacated. The harsher sentence was justified based on the charge of being a habitual offender. However, the sentence was vacated because it appeared that defendant received four life sentences and the trial court did not specify which of the four counts in the habitual offender bill was being enhanced.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence for indecent behavior with a juvenile was reversed and vacated. Defendant's sentences on the remaining convictions were vacated. The case was remanded to the trial court for resentencing.

 

1191 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Patriot Am. Hospitality P'ship, LP v. Miss. Land Holdings, Inc.


NO. 2006-CA-0601


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2006-0601 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/13/06); 948 So. 2d 249; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 3025



December 13, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Patriot Am. Hospitality P'ship, LP v. Miss. Land Holdings, Inc., 949 So. 2d 450, 2007 La. LEXIS 605 (La., Mar. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM Civil District Court, Orleans Parish. NO. 2004-13362, Division "A-5". Honorable Carolyn Gill-Jefferson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: When it discovered termite damage, appellant hotel buyer sued appellees, the previous owners and businesses involved in a previous renovation. The owners and businesses claimed the suit was perempted due to time limitations under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5607. The Civil District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, agreed and dismissed the owners and business. The buyer's motion for new trial was denied, and it appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the buyer contended the trial court erred by holding that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5607 perempted its claims against the owners and businesses involved in the renovation as the buyer's property right vested prior to the enactment of § 9:5607. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the buyer admitted that it did not acquire or could not have acquired knowledge of the alleged pre-existing termite damage until years after the purchase. Thus was when the buyer acquired the right to sue. Accordingly, the trial court was not manifestly erroneous in its factual conclusions that the buyer did not suffer damage until then, and the peremptive period from § 9:5607 applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1192 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vance


NO. 06-KA-465


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


06-465 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/12/06); 948 So. 2d 1106; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2832



December 12, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 2, 2007.
Writ denied by State v. Vance, 2007 La. LEXIS 2049 (La., Sept. 21, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 05-2676, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED.  


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant's motion to suppress confession, identification, and physical evidence was denied, he entered a plea of guilty. The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court of Jefferson Parish, Louisiana, sentenced defendant to 10 years imprisonment for possession of a firearm by a convicted felon and 5 years fiver years for possession of marijuana. The sentences were ordered to run concurrently with credit given for time served. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress because the attempted stop was without reasonable suspicion or probable cause. The appellate court disagreed, finding that, with or without reasonable suspicion, the officers, from approximately 10 feet away, had the right to ask defendant to come over toward them "for a second." The request, in a public area and without any greater show of authority, did not transform the encounter into a forcible detention, and defendant was free to leave. After defendant took off in headlong flight, the totality of the circumstances known to the officers at the time, including the knowledge that the area was prone to drug trafficking, defendant's suspicious behavior and his unprovoked flight into oncoming traffic, gave rise to reasonable suspicion for an investigatory detention. The detention and pat down for safety reasons following defendant's fall was reasonable to protect the officers and members of the public, especially as defendant behaved as if he was carrying a weapon. Therefore, the appellate court found no error in the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed, but the case was remanded to the trial court with orders that defendant be properly informed of the prescriptive period for filing for post-conviction relief.

State v. Rideau


NO. 2005-KA-0462


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2005-0462 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/06/06); 947 So. 2d 127; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 3041



December 6, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 8, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS. PARISH NO. 427-131, SECTION "E". HONORABLE CALVIN JOHNSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, (Louisiana) convicting and sentencing him for four counts of aggravated battery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34, one count of second-degree kidnapping in violation of La. Rev. Stat. § 14:44.1, and two counts of aggravated assault upon a peace officer with a firearm in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:37.2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of numerous crimes arising out of his holding hostages in his home and shooting at police officers. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred by including aggravated battery as a responsive verdict to the charged crime of attempted first-degree murder of a peace officer because an essential element of aggravated battery, physical contact with the victim, was missing from first-degree murder. Retrying defendant on the charge of first-degree murder would violate defendant's right against double jeopardy because by finding defendant guilty of the lesser offense of aggravated battery, the jury acquitted him of first-degree murder. The court also reversed defendant's conviction of aggravated assault against one of the police officers because that officer did not testify at trial regarding the effect of defendant's actions upon him as required. However, the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction of second-degree kidnapping, even though that victim did not testify, because it was undisputed that defendant aimed a gun at her while using her as a shield from the police.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences on four counts of aggravated battery were reversed, as were his conviction and sentence on one count of aggravated assault on a peace officer with a firearm. His remaining convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

1194 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Int'l Paper Co. v. Hilton


06-895


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


06-895 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/15/06); 950 So. 2d 1; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2606



November 15, 2006, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing denied by Int'l Paper Co. v. Hilton, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 36 (La.App. 3 Cir., Jan. 10, 2007)
Writ granted by Int'l Paper Co. v. Hilton, 957 So. 2d 161, 2007 La. LEXIS 1366 (La., 2007)
Affirmed by Int'l Paper Co. v. Hilton, 966 So. 2d 545, 2007 La. LEXIS 2326 (La., Oct. 16, 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer filed a petition for refund of ad valorem taxes paid under protest claiming that its property was located in an "industrial area" and was, therefore, not subject to taxation. Ultimately, the Ninth Judicial District Court of Rapides Parish, Louisiana, granted appellee taxing entities' motion for summary judgment, finding no genuine issue of fact that the taxpayer was entitled to a refund. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the taxpayer contended, inter alia, that the trial court erred by not finding that industrial areas were not subject to annexation, incorporation, or inclusion by any newly created municipality or district, and therefore, that the taxpayer's property was not "property subject to taxation" by the newly created recreation district, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:130.15-130.16 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:1202-1203. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:130.16 was tacitly repealed and replaced by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:1203. And under § 51:1203, any business located in an industrial area that provided the listed services for itself was, thereafter, immune from being included in any newly created municipality. Further, the distinction between a municipality and a special service district was irrelevant. The tacit repeal of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:130.16, as replaced by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 52:1203, only conferred the exclusion from municipalities.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1195 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davis


No. 41,180-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,180 (La.App. 2 Cir. 11/03/06); 942 So. 2d 1196; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2422



November 3, 2006, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 237068. Honorable Michael R. Walker, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) convicted defendant of possession of a Schedule II controlled dangerous substance, cocaine, and possession of a Schedule I controlled dangerous substance, MDMA (Ecstasy). He was sentenced to serve consecutive sentences of five years for the cocaine conviction and one year for the Ecstasy conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Because it seemed as if two individuals were about to get into a fight, two police officers confronted them. While the first officer performed a pat down search of defendant, he and the second officer observed an object fall to the ground. Defendant appeared to conceal the baggy and mash it into the ground with his foot. Defendant began to resist as the officers attempted to handcuff him. He elbowed the first officer in his chest, ignored the second officer's warning to stop and get on the ground, and fled. The second officer recovered the baggy from the ground and pursued defendant. Defendant was ultimately taken into custody. The baggy was later determined to contain cocaine and Ecstasy. Defense counsel waived defendant's right to a jury trial on defendant's behalf. Pursuant to La. Const. art. I, § 17 and La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 780, the waiver was valid because it was knowingly and intelligently made since defendant waived the right to gain an advantage - a delay before commencement of his trial. Also, because defendant had a prior conviction, resisted arrest, and denied possessing drugs, his sentences were not constitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Rideau


05-1470


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


05-1470 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/02/06); 943 So. 2d 559; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2368



November 2, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 12, 2006.
Writ denied by, Remanded by State v. Rideau, 2007 La. LEXIS 1933 (La., Sept. 14, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE PARISH OF CALCASIEU, DOCKET NO. 15321-01. FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. HONORABLE DAVID A. RITCHIE, DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. Rideau, 852 So. 2d 993, 2003 La. LEXIS 2245 (La., Aug. 21, 2003)



DISPOSITION: ORDER VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Parish of Calcasieu, Fourteenth Judicial District Court (Louisiana), convicted defendant of manslaughter. The trial court sentenced him to the maximum term of 21 years at hard labor. Since he had already served 44 years, he was released from custody. As part of the sentence, the trial court ordered him to pay all court costs associated with the proceedings. He moved to vacate that order, but the trial court denied his motion. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Sixty days after defendant was sentenced, the trial court issued an order casting defendant with court costs and indigent defense fees in the amount of $ 127,905.45 under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 887(A) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:148. The amount defendant had been assessed was extraordinary when compared to the amounts assessed in prior cases. Although he was granted 15 days to object, the trial court appeared to give little consideration to defendant's plea that the total amount was unprecedented, excessive, and too burdensome under the circumstances. The trial court decided to maintain the order directing defendant to pay $ 127, 905.45 as court costs despite the trial court's recognition that defendant was indigent and did not currently have the ability to pay it. In addition, the appellate court found that the trial court was not authorized to issue a judgment directing defendant to reimburse the indigent defender's board for the costs associated with his defense under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:148, including expert witness fees and expenses because, at all relevant times, even up to the date of his sentence, defendant was indigent - a fact which was undisputed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated the trial court's order.

 

1197 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


NO. 06-KA-372


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


06-372 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/31/06); 945 So. 2d 768; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2417



October 31, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 19, 2007.
Writ denied by State v. Anderson, 962 So. 2d 427, 2007 La. LEXIS 1841 (La., 2007)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Writ denied by State ex rel. Anderson v. State, 6 So. 3d 787, 2009 La. LEXIS 312 (La., 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Anderson v. Cooper, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 20688 (E.D. La., Feb. 11, 2010)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Magistrate's recommendation at Ronnell v. Cooper, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 45073 (E.D. La., Mar. 31, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 04-4828, DIVISION "O". HONORABLE ROSS P. LADART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED, SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of distribution of marijuana and sentenced him to 20 years' imprisonment at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of distribution of marijuana, adjudicated as a fourth felony offender, and sentenced to 20 years' imprisonment at hard labor. On appeal, defendant argued that his sentence was excessive. The court found that the record indicated that at the time defendant committed the offense, he was 25 years old and already had three previous felony convictions. Although the prior convictions were not for crimes of violence, that was not enough to warrant a downward deviation of his sentence from that which was mandated under the Louisiana Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. Moreover, it was clear from his record that defendant was likely to commit another offense. Because defendant did not put forth other evidence, he did not prove clearly and convincingly that a downward deviation from the mandatory sentence was warranted. The court concluded that the imposed sentence of 20 years at hard labor was not excessive under La. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Craig


2005 KA 2323


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2005 2323 (La.App. 1 Cir. 10/25/06); 944 So. 2d 660; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2288



October 25, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Craig, 959 So. 2d 518, 2007 La. LEXIS 1627 (La., 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Craig v. Louisiana, 552 U.S. 1062, 128 S. Ct. 714, 169 L. Ed. 2d 554, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 12830 (2007)
Writ denied by State v. Craig, 46 So. 3d 1267, 2010 La. LEXIS 2341 (La., 2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Craig v. Cain, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 142287 (M.D. La., July 21, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and For the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 09-92-0884. Honorable Bonnie Jackson, Judge Presiding.
State v. Craig, 699 So. 2d 865, 1997 La. LEXIS 1312 (La., May 20, 1997)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, convicted defendant of first degree murder, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30. Defendant was sentenced to death by lethal injection. The death sentence was subsequently set aside, and defendant was resentenced to life imprisonment. His motion for reconsideration of sentence was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred in refusing to reconsider his sentence. Defendant argued that the sentence violated the Unites States and Louisiana Constitutions. The appellate court determined that upon invalidation of a provision of statutory capital punishment, the appropriate sentence to be imposed upon a conviction for first degree murder was the most severe penalty established by the legislature for criminal homicide at the time of the offense. The penalty for first degree murder at the time of the offense was death or life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence in accordance with the determination of the jury, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30(C). Imposition of a mandatory sentence of life imprisonment did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VIII. Defendant's sentence did not violate the International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights. Under La. Const. art. I, § 20, there was no reason for the trial court to deviate from the mandatory sentence. The sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive and was not grossly disproportionate to the severity of the offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1199 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dodson


No. 41,415-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


41,415 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/16/06); 942 So. 2d 579; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2266



October 16, 2006, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Dodson, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2984 (La.App. 2 Cir., Dec. 7, 2006)
Reversed by State v. Dodson, 2007 La. LEXIS 2390 (La., Nov. 2, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 106,493. Honorable Jeffrey S. Cox, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE VACATED; MATTER REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his motion to suppress was denied, defendant entered a Crosby plea to illegal carrying of weapons while in the possession of controlled dangerous substances. The Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court of Bossier Parish, Louisiana, sentenced defendant to serve eight years imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence, to be served consecutively with any other sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress and argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95(E) was unconstitutional as applied to him. The appellate court found that the trial judge's advice to defendant of his right to confront his accusers before entering his guilty plea was inadequate and required that his conviction and sentence be vacated. As to defendant's suppression arguments, the appellate court found that the officers had sufficient reason to commence their investigation pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 215.1 when they observed that defendant's vehicle was parked sideways across two parking spaces and its license plate had expired. Furthermore, defendant signed a consent to search form, consent was given almost contemporaneously with the end of the traffic stop, and there was no indication of any coercion or other improper action by the officers. Finally, the appellate court ruled that the exceptions under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95(E) were not irrational and the statute was not invalid because of them.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were vacated and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1200 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Ranger Ins. Co. v. State


06-487


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


06-487 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/11/06); 941 So. 2d 182; 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2241



October 11, 2006, Opinion Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 21, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 2003-6668. HONORABLE MARILYN CARR CASTLE, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Ranger Ins. Co. v. State, 941 So. 2d 191, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2239 (La.App. 3 Cir., Oct. 11, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurance company sought review of an order from the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which denied one of its petitions for nullity against defendant, the State of Louisiana, after judgments of bond forfeiture were entered in two criminal matters for which it acted as a commercial surety.


OVERVIEW: The company filed petitions for nullity after judgments of bond forfeiture were entered in two criminal matters for which it acted as a commercial surety. The trial court granted one of the petitions, annulling one of the judgments after a determination that the forfeiture was not supported by adequate evidence. As for the remaining matter, the trial court found that the commissioner lacked authority to issue the judgment of bond forfeiture. However, due to the trial court's determination that the commissioner was acting as a de facto officer, the petition for nullity was denied. On appeal, the court held that the trial court's application of the de facto official doctrine was consistent with the framework set forth by the Louisiana Supreme Court in O'Reilly. As in O'Reilly, the commissioner entering the judgment of bond forfeiture was not an usurper of office acting without color of right. Rather, like the commissioners in O'Reilly, the commissioner held an office created by statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:716(A). The company's assignment of error further lacked merit insofar as it argued that the commissioner's action was contrary to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:85.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.
